<!-- original page 109 -->

## В§18. Complements on Г©tale morphisms. Henselian local rings

In the present section, we study various properties special to Г©tale morphisms. In addition, the notion of Г©tale
morphism allows one to develop in a very natural fashion Nagata's theory of Henselian rings, as well as that of strictly
local rings. These rings play an important role in many recent developments, by appearing each time that one needs a
"localization" procedure finer than the one provided by the Zariski topology (cf. for example `[43]`, while awaiting the
appearance of the chapter of our Treatise devoted to the study of the "Г©tale topology").

### 18.1. A remarkable equivalence of categories

**Proposition (18.1.1).**

<!-- label: IV.18.1.1 -->

*Let `S` be a prescheme, `S_0` a closed sub-prescheme of `S`, `X_0` an `S_0`-prescheme smooth (resp. Г©tale) over `S_0`,
`x_0` a point of `X_0`. Then there exist an open neighbourhood `U_0` of `x_0` in `X_0`, an `S`-prescheme `U` smooth
(resp. Г©tale) over `S`, and an `S_0`-isomorphism `U Г—_S S_0 вҘІ U_0`.*

Note that if `X_0` is Г©tale over `S_0` at the point `x_0`, then it is a fortiori unramified over `S_0` at that point; if
one has constructed an `S`-prescheme `U` smooth over `S` such that `U Г—_S S_0` is isomorphic to `U_0`, then since the
fibres of the morphisms `U_0 вҶ’ S_0` and `U вҶ’ S` containing `x_0` are then isomorphic, it will follow that `U` is
unramified over `S` at the point `x_0` `(17.4.1, d)`, hence also in a neighbourhood of `x_0`; replacing `U` by this
neighbourhood, one concludes that `U` will be Г©tale over `S`. It is therefore enough to prove the proposition when one
assumes only `X_0` smooth over `S_0`.

The question being local on `S` and on `X_0`, one may suppose that `S = Spec(A)` and `X_0 = Spec(C_0)` are affine, so
that `S_0 = Spec(A_0)`, where `A_0` is a quotient ring of `A`, `C_0 = B_0/рқ”Қ_0`, where `B_0 = A_0[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n]` and `рқ”Қ_0`
is an ideal of finite type of `B_0`; finally, `C_0` is a formally smooth `A_0`-algebra for the discrete topologies. Let
`рқ”ӯ_0` be the ideal `j_{x_0}` in `C_0`; one has `рқ”ӯ_0 = рқ”®_0/рқ”Қ_0`, where `рқ”®_0` is a prime ideal of `B_0`. The Jacobian
criterion `(0, 22.6.4)` combined with `(0, 19.1.12)` shows that there exist in `рқ”Қ_0` a family of `r` polynomials `u_i`
`(1 в©Ҫ i в©Ҫ r)` and `r` indices `j_h` `(1 в©Ҫ h в©Ҫ r)` such that the images of the `u_i` in `(рқ”Қ_0)_{рқ”®_0}/(рқ”Қ_0^2)_{рқ”®_0}`
generate this `(B_0)_{рқ”®_0}`-module and such that

```text
  (18.1.1.1)    det(вҲӮu_i/вҲӮT_{j_h}) вҲү рқ”®_0.
```

Since `(B_0)_{рқ”®_0}` is a local ring, it follows from Nakayama's lemma that one may suppose the images of the `u_i` in
`(рқ”Қ_0)_{рқ”®_0}` generate this `(B_0)_{рқ”®_0}`-module, then, by replacing if necessary `X_0` by an affine open neighbourhood
of `x_0`, that the `u_i` generate `рқ”Қ_0` `(0_I, 5.2.2)`. Put then `B = A[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n]`; `B_0` is thus a quotient ring

<!-- original page 110 -->

of `B`, `рқ”ӯ_0` is the image of a prime ideal `рқ”®` of `B`, and `рқ”®` is the inverse image of `рқ”®_0`. For each `i`, let
`v_i вҲҲ B` be an element whose image is `u_i` in `B_0`, and let `рқ”Қ` be the ideal of `B` generated by the `v_i`, so that
`рқ”Қ_0` is the image of `рқ”Қ` in `B_0`. The proposition will be established by taking for `U` an open neighbourhood of the
point of `Spec(B/рқ”Қ)` corresponding to the prime ideal `рқ”ӯ = рқ”®/рқ”Қ`, provided one proves that `B_рқ”®/рқ”Қ_рқ”®` is a formally smooth
`A`-algebra for the discrete topologies. Now, this follows from the Jacobian criterion, for the images of the `v_i` in
`рқ”Қ_рқ”®/рқ”Қ_рқ”®^2` generate this `B_рқ”®`-module, and it follows from `(18.1.1.1)` that one has `det(вҲӮv_i/вҲӮT_{j_h}) вҲү рқ”®`.

**Theorem (18.1.2).**

<!-- label: IV.18.1.2 -->

*Let `S` be a prescheme, `S_0` a closed sub-prescheme of `S` whose underlying space is identical to that of `S`. Then
the functor*

```text
  X вҶҰ X Г—_S S_0
```

*from the category of `S`-preschemes Г©tale over `S` to the category of `S_0`-preschemes Г©tale over `S_0` is an
equivalence of categories.*

Let us show first that this functor is *fully faithful*. Let `X`, `Y` be two `S`-preschemes Г©tale over `S`, and put
`X_0 = X Г—_S S_0`, `Y_0 = Y Г—_S S_0`. If `Z = X Г—_S Y`, the set `Hom_S(X, Y)` is in canonical bijective correspondence
with the set of `X`-sections `О“(Z/X)`, and similarly `Hom_{S_0}(X_0, Y_0)` is in canonical bijective correspondence with
`О“(Z_0/X_0)`, where `Z_0 = Z Г—_S S_0 = X_0 Г—_{S_0} Y_0`. Now `Z` is Г©tale over `X`, `Z_0` Г©tale over `X_0`, and `X_0`
(resp. `Z_0`) is a closed sub-prescheme of `X` (resp. `Z`) having the same underlying space. The open subsets of `Z`
such that the restriction of the morphism `Z вҶ’ X` is surjective and radicial are therefore the same as the subsets of
`Z_0` having the corresponding properties, and our assertion follows accordingly from `(17.9.3)`.

To complete the proof, it suffices to see that for every `S_0`-prescheme `X_0` Г©tale over `S_0`, there exist an
`S`-prescheme `X` Г©tale over `S` and an `S_0`-isomorphism `X_0 вҘІ X Г—_S S_0`. By virtue of Prop. `(18.1.1)`, there is an
open cover `(U_Оұ)` of `X_0` and, for each `Оұ`, an `S`-prescheme `V_Оұ` which is Г©tale over `S`, and finally an
`S_0`-isomorphism `Оё_Оұ : U_Оұ вҘІ V_Оұ Г—_S S_0`. Moreover, by the first part of the proof, there exists a unique
`S_0`-isomorphism `ПҶ_{ОұОІ}` from `Оё_Оұ(U_Оұ вҲ© U_ОІ)` onto `Оё_ОІ(U_Оұ вҲ© U_ОІ)`, corresponding to the identity automorphism of
`U_Оұ вҲ© U_ОІ`, and it is immediate, for the same reason, that these isomorphisms satisfy the gluing condition
`(0_I, 4.1.7)`. There is consequently an `S`-prescheme `X` such that the `V_Оұ` are canonically identified with
sub-preschemes induced on open sets of `X`, the `Оё_Оұ` being identified with `S_0`-isomorphisms which coincide on the
intersections `U_Оұ вҲ© U_ОІ` and therefore define an `S_0`-isomorphism `X_0 вҘІ X Г—_S S_0`. It is clear that `X` is Г©tale
over `S` `(17.3.2)`, which completes the proof.

**Corollary (18.1.3).**

<!-- label: IV.18.1.3 -->

*Let `S` be a prescheme, `X` an `S`-prescheme Г©tale over `S`, `S'` an `S`-prescheme, `S'_0` a closed sub-prescheme of
`S'` having the same underlying space. Then the canonical map `X(S')_S вҶ’ X(S'_0)_S` `(I, 3.4.3)` is bijective.*

Indeed, put `X' = X Г—_S S'`, `X'_0 = X Г—_S S'_0`, so that `X(S')_S = О“(X'/S')` and `X(S'_0)_S = О“(X'_0/S'_0)`; the
corollary follows from the fact that the functor defined in `(18.1.2)` (with `S` and `S_0` replaced by `S'` and `S'_0`
respectively) is fully faithful (or directly from `(17.9.3)`).

<!-- original page 111 -->

### 18.2. Гүtale covers

**(18.2.1)** Given a ring `A` and a commutative `A`-algebra `B` which is *finite* and is a *free* `A`-module, recall
(Bourbaki, _Alg._, chap. VIII, В§12, nВ° 2) that one defines on `B` an `A`-linear form `Tr_{B/A}`, the "*trace form*";
from this one deduces the definition of a *symmetric `A`-bilinear form* (also called the "*trace form*")

```text
  (18.2.1.1)    (x, y) вҶҰ Tr_{B/A}(xy)
```

whose datum is equivalent to that of the associated `A`-linear map `astr_{B/A} : B вҶ’ BМҢ` of the `A`-module `B` into its
*dual* `BМҢ`, equal to its transpose. When `A` is a *field*, it is equivalent to say that this bilinear form is
*nondegenerate* or that `B` is a *separable* `A`-algebra (Bourbaki, _Alg._, chap. IX, В§2, prop. 5).

Let `f : A вҶ’ A'` be a homomorphism of rings; put `B' = B вҠ—_A A'`, and let `g : B вҶ’ B'` be the canonical homomorphism;
the image under `g` of a basis of the `A`-module `B` is then a basis of the `A'`-module `B'`, and it follows from the
definitions that one has, for every `x вҲҲ B`,

```text
  (18.2.1.2)    Tr_{B'/A'}(g(x)) = f(Tr_{B/A}(x)).
```

**(18.2.2)** Consider now a ringed space `(X, рқ’Ә_X)` and let `в„¬` be an `рқ’Ә_X`-Algebra which, as an `рқ’Ә_X`-Module, is
*locally free of finite rank*; then, for every open `U вҠӮ X` such that `в„¬ | U` is (as an `рқ’Ә_U`-Module) isomorphic to
`рқ’Ә_U^n` (for an `n` depending on `U`), `О“(U, в„¬)` is a `О“(U, рқ’Ә_X)`-algebra which, as a `О“(U, рқ’Ә_X)`-module, is free of
finite rank and therefore defines a `О“(U, рқ’Ә_X)`-linear form `Tr_{О“(U, в„¬)/О“(U, рқ’Ә_X)}`, which we shall also denote
`Tr_{в„¬/рқ’Ә_X, U}`; from this one deduces an associated linear map

```text
  astr_{в„¬/рқ’Ә_X, U} : О“(U, в„¬) вҶ’ О“(U, в„¬)МҢ = О“(U, в„¬МҢ).
```

Moreover, it follows from `(18.2.1.2)` that these linear maps are compatible with the operations of restriction from `U`
to a smaller open set, and therefore define on the one hand a homomorphism of `рқ’Ә_X`-Modules, also called the *trace
homomorphism*:

```text
  (18.2.2.1)    Tr_{в„¬/рқ’Ә_X} : в„¬ вҶ’ рқ’Ә_X
```

and on the other hand a homomorphism of `рқ’Ә_X`-Modules

```text
  (18.2.2.2)    astr_{в„¬/рқ’Ә_X} : в„¬ вҶ’ в„¬МҢ
```

said to be *associated with the trace*, and equal to its own transpose. It also follows from `(18.2.1.2)` that for every
`x вҲҲ X` one has

```text
  (18.2.2.3)    (Tr_{в„¬/рқ’Ә_X})_x = Tr_{в„¬_x/рқ’Ә_{X,x}}
  (18.2.2.4)    (astr_{в„¬/рқ’Ә_X})_x = astr_{в„¬_x/рқ’Ә_{X,x}}.
```

Finally, under the conditions of `(18.2.1)`, if one puts `X = Spec(A)` and if `в„¬ = BМғ` is the `рқ’Ә_X`-Algebra
corresponding to `B`, the form `Tr_{в„¬/рқ’Ә_X}` (resp. the homomorphism `astr_{в„¬/рқ’Ә_X}`) corresponds to the form `Tr_{B/A}`
(resp. to the homomorphism of `A`-modules `astr_{B/A}`), as also follows from `(18.2.1.2)`.

<!-- original page 112 -->

**Proposition (18.2.3).**

<!-- label: IV.18.2.3 -->

*Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a finite morphism of preschemes and let `в„¬ = f_*(рқ’Ә_X)`. The following conditions are equivalent:*

*a) `f` is Г©tale.*

*a') `f` is a flat morphism of finite presentation and, for every `x вҲҲ X`, if one puts `y = f(x)`, then
`рқ’Ә_{X, x}/рқ”Ә_y В· рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is a field, a finite separable extension of `k(y)`.*

*b) `в„¬` is a locally free `рқ’Ә_Y`-Module and, for every `y вҲҲ Y`, `в„¬_y вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_{Y,y}} k(y)` is a finite separable
`k(y)`-algebra (hence the direct composite of a finite number of fields, finite separable extensions of `k(y)`).*

*c) `в„¬` is a locally free `рқ’Ә_Y`-Module and the homomorphism `astr_{в„¬/рқ’Ә_Y} : в„¬ вҶ’ в„¬МҢ` `(18.2.2)` is bijective.*

Taking into account that `f` is quasi-compact, the equivalence of a) and a') has already been proved `(17.6.2)`. To
prove the rest of the proposition, one may restrict to the case where `Y = Spec(A)` and `X = Spec(B)` are affine, `B`
being a finite `A`-algebra and `в„¬ = BМғ`. To say that `f` is a morphism of finite presentation amounts then to saying
that `B` is an `A`-module of finite presentation `(1.4.7)`. If in addition `f` is flat, hence `B` a flat `A`-module, one
knows (Bourbaki, _Alg. comm._, chap. II, В§5, nВ° 2, cor. 2 of th. 1) that `B` is a projective `A`-module, hence `в„¬` a
locally free `рқ’Ә_Y`-Module (loc. cit., nВ° 2, th. 1), and the converse is immediate. On the other hand, `fвҒ»В№(y)` is none
other than the spectrum of the `k(y)`-algebra `в„¬(y) = в„¬_y вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_{Y,y}} k(y)`, which completes the proof of the
equivalence of a') and b). To see that b) is equivalent to c), note that the second assertion of b) is equivalent to the
fact that the homomorphism `astr_{в„¬(y)/k(y)} : в„¬(y) вҶ’ в„¬(y)МҢ` is bijective; since `в„¬(y) = в„¬_y вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_{Y,y}} k(y)` and
`в„¬(y)МҢ = в„¬МҢ_y вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_{Y,y}} k(y)`, and since `в„¬_y` and `в„¬МҢ_y` are free `рқ’Ә_{Y,y}`-modules, it follows from `(18.2.2.4)` and
from Bourbaki, _Alg. comm._, chap. II, В§3, nВ° 3, cor. of prop. 6, that the homomorphism
`astr_{в„¬_y/рқ’Ә_{Y,y}} : в„¬_y вҶ’ в„¬МҢ_y` is also bijective; the converse being obvious, this completes the proof.

When an `рқ’Ә_X`-Algebra `в„¬` verifies the equivalent conditions b) and c) of `(18.2.3)`, one says that `в„¬` is a *finite
Г©tale `рқ’Ә_X`-Algebra*. When `X = Spec(A)` is affine and one therefore has `в„¬ = BМғ`, where `B` is an `A`-algebra, it
amounts to the same, by virtue of `(18.2.3)`, to say that `в„¬` is a finite Г©tale `рқ’Ә_X`-Algebra or that `B` is a finite
Г©tale `A`-algebra (in the sense of `(17.3.2)`).

**Corollary (18.2.4).**

<!-- label: IV.18.2.4 -->

*Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a finite morphism of finite presentation, and put `в„¬ = f_*(рқ’Ә_X)`. Let `y` be a point of `Y`. The
following conditions are equivalent:*

*a) There exists an open neighbourhood `U` of `y` in `Y` such that the restriction `fвҒ»В№(U) вҶ’ U` of `f` is an Г©tale
morphism.*

*b) `в„¬_y` is a free `рқ’Ә_{Y,y}`-module of finite type and `в„¬_y вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_{Y,y}} k(y)` is a separable `k(y)`-algebra.*

It is clear that a) implies b) by virtue of `(18.2.3)`. On the other hand, `в„¬` is an `рқ’Ә_Y`-Module of finite presentation
`(1.6.3 and 1.4.7)`; hence, if `в„¬_y` is a free `рқ’Ә_{Y,y}`-module, there exists an open neighbourhood `U` of `y` in `Y`
such that `в„¬ | U` is a locally free `рқ’Ә_U`-Module `(0_I, 5.2.7)`; in addition, by hypothesis, the homomorphism
`astr_{в„¬_y/рқ’Ә_{Y,y}} : в„¬_y вҶ’ в„¬МҢ_y` being

<!-- original page 113 -->

bijective, it also follows from `(0_I, 5.2.7)` that one may suppose `U` chosen so that the homomorphism
`astr_{в„¬ | U/рқ’Ә_U}` is bijective. The fact that b) implies a) then follows from `(18.2.3)`.

**Corollary (18.2.5).**

<!-- label: IV.18.2.5 -->

*Let `Y` be a quasi-compact or locally Noetherian prescheme, `f : X вҶ’ Y` a finite morphism of finite presentation; put
`в„¬ = f_*(рқ’Ә_X)`. Suppose that for every closed point `y` of `Y`, `в„¬_y` is a free `рқ’Ә_{Y,y}`-module and
`в„¬_y вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_{Y,y}} k(y)` is a separable `k(y)`-algebra. Then `f` is Г©tale.*

Indeed, it follows from `(18.2.4)` that every closed point `y` of `Y` has an open neighbourhood `U` such that the
restriction `fвҒ»В№(U) вҶ’ U` of `f` is Г©tale; the conclusion follows from the fact that in the two cases considered, every
non-empty closed subset of `Y` contains a closed point `(5.1.11 and 0_I, 2.1.3)`.

**Corollary (18.2.6).**

<!-- label: IV.18.2.6 -->

*If `f : X вҶ’ Y` is a finite Г©tale morphism, and if one puts `в„¬ = f_*(рқ’Ә_X)`, then the `рқ’Ә_Y`-homomorphism
`Tr_{в„¬/рқ’Ә_Y} : в„¬ вҶ’ рқ’Ә_Y` `(18.2.2)` (also denoted `Tr_f`) is surjective.*

The question being local, one may, by virtue of `(18.2.3)`, suppose that `Y = Spec(A)`, `X = Spec(B)` with `в„¬ = BМғ`, `B`
being a free `A`-module; since by virtue of `(18.2.3)` the bilinear form `(18.2.1.1)` is nondegenerate, this entails in
particular that the linear form `Tr_{B/A}` is surjective.

**Remarks (18.2.7).** вҖ” (i) When `f : X вҶ’ Y` is a finite morphism such that `f_*(рқ’Ә_X)` is a locally free `рқ’Ә_Y`-Module
(resp. locally free of rank `n`), one says further that `f` is a *finite locally free morphism* (resp. *locally free of
rank `n`*). This condition, by virtue of `(18.2.3)`, is verified if `f` is a finite Г©tale morphism, but does not by
itself imply that `f` be Г©tale, as is shown by the example where `X = Spec(K)` and `Y = Spec(k)` are spectra of fields,
`K` being a finite non-separable extension of `k`. When `f : X вҶ’ Y` is a finite Г©tale morphism, one also says that `X`
is an *Г©tale cover* of `Y`. One will note that in that case, `f` is universally open and universally closed, and in
particular `f(X)` is a subset of `Y` both open and closed.

One says that an Г©tale cover `X` of `Y` is *trivial* if `X` is a sum of a finite number of preschemes isomorphic to `Y`.
One says that an Г©tale cover `X` of `Y` is *locally trivial* if the morphism `f : X вҶ’ Y` is such that every point
`y вҲҲ Y` has an open neighbourhood `U` for which the cover `fвҒ»В№(U)` of `U` is trivial.

(ii) Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a finite morphism, locally free of rank `n`; put `в„¬ = f_*(рқ’Ә_X)` and let
`u = astr_{в„¬/рқ’Ә_Y} : в„¬ вҶ’ в„¬МҢ`; from this one deduces a homomorphism of `n`-th exterior power
`Оӣ^n u : Оӣ^n в„¬ вҶ’ Оӣ^n в„¬МҢ = (Оӣ^n в„¬)МҢ` between invertible `рқ’Ә_Y`-Modules, and consequently `(0_I, 5.4.2)` an element

```text
  (18.2.7.1)    d_{X/Y} вҲҲ О“(Y, (Оӣ^n в„¬МҢ) вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_Y} (Оӣ^n в„¬МҢ))
```

called the *discriminant* of `X` over `Y`. Moreover, since `(Оӣ^n в„¬МҢ) вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_Y} (Оӣ^n в„¬МҢ)` is the dual of
`(Оӣ^n в„¬) вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_Y} (Оӣ^n в„¬)`, `d_{X/Y}` may also be identified with a homomorphism

```text
  (18.2.7.2)    (Оӣ^n в„¬) вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_Y} (Оӣ^n в„¬) вҶ’ рқ’Ә_Y
```

and one denotes by `рқ’ҹ_{X/Y}` the quasi-coherent Ideal of finite type of `рқ’Ә_Y`, image of the homomorphism `(18.2.7.2)`,
also called the *discriminant Ideal* of `X` over `Y`.

<!-- original page 114 -->

That being so, for the homomorphism `u` to be bijective, it is necessary and sufficient that `Оӣ^n u` be bijective, or
again that the section `d_{X/Y}` have an invertible germ at every point `y вҲҲ Y`, which one also writes `d_{X/Y}(y) вү  0`
for every `y` `(0_I, 5.5.2)`. It also amounts to the same to say that the discriminant Ideal `рқ’ҹ_{X/Y}` is equal to
`рқ’Ә_Y`.

The terminology of "cover" introduced in `(18.2.7, (i))` is justified by the following proposition:

**Proposition (18.2.8).**

<!-- label: IV.18.2.8 -->

*Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a morphism Г©tale, separated and of finite type, and for every `y вҲҲ Y` let `n(y)` be the geometric
number of points of `fвҒ»В№(y)`. Then the function `y вҶҰ n(y)` is lower semi-continuous in `Y`. For it to be continuous at a
point `y` (hence constant in a neighbourhood of `y`), it is necessary and sufficient that there exist an open
neighbourhood `U` of `y` such that the restriction `fвҒ»В№(U) вҶ’ U` of `f` be a finite (Г©tale) morphism.*

Since `f` is quasi-finite `(17.6.1)` and locally of finite presentation, it amounts to the same to say that `f` is
finite or that `f` is proper `(8.11.1)`: in addition, each fibre `fвҒ»В№(y)` is geometrically reduced over `k(y)`. The
conclusions then follow from `(15.5.9, (i) and (ii))` and from the fact that `f` is flat.

**Corollary (18.2.9).**

<!-- label: IV.18.2.9 -->

*Let `Y` be a connected prescheme, `f : X вҶ’ Y` a morphism Г©tale, separated and of finite type. For `f` to be finite (in
other words, for `X` to be an Г©tale cover of `Y`), it is necessary and sufficient that all the fibres of `f` have the
same geometric number of points.*

**Remarks (18.2.10).** вҖ” (i) The example of the "affine line with one point doubled" `(I, 5.5.11)` shows that an Г©tale
morphism of finite type of Noetherian preschemes can be *non-separated*; for this example, the first assertion of
`(18.2.8)` no longer holds.

(ii) For a separated, Г©tale morphism of finite type `f : X вҶ’ Y` to make `X` into a *locally trivial* cover, it is
necessary and sufficient that for every `x вҲҲ X` there exist an open neighbourhood `U` of `y = f(x)` and a `U`-section
`g` of `fвҒ»В№(U)` such that `g(y) = x`. Indeed, the condition is obviously necessary; the fact that it is sufficient
follows from the fact that every fibre `fвҒ»В№(y)` is finite (`(17.6.1)` and `(I, 6.2.2)`), from the characterization of
sections of an Г©tale `Y`-scheme `(17.9.3)`, and from prop. `(18.2.8)`.

### 18.3. Finite Г©tale algebras

**Proposition (18.3.1).**

<!-- label: IV.18.3.1 -->

*Let `A` be a ring, `B` an `A`-algebra of finite presentation.*

*(i) For `B` to be an unramified `A`-algebra, it is necessary and sufficient that `B` be an `A`-module of finite
presentation and that `B` be a projective `(B вҠ—_A B)`-module.*

*(ii) Suppose moreover that `B` is a finite `A`-algebra. For `B` to be an Г©tale `A`-algebra, it is necessary and
sufficient that `B` be a projective `A`-module and a projective `(B вҠ—_A B)`-module.*

It is understood that the `(B вҠ—_A B)`-module structure on `B` is the one coming from the `(B вҠ—_A B)`-algebra structure
on `B` corresponding to the canonical `A`-homomorphism of rings `B вҠ—_A B вҶ’ B`, which is surjective and of kernel
`рқ”Қ_{B/A}` `(0, 20.4.1)`.

(i) To say that the morphism `Spec(B) вҶ’ Spec(A)` is locally of finite presentation is equivalent to saying that `B` is
an `A`-algebra of finite presentation `(1.4.6)`. To say

<!-- original page 115 -->

that `B` is an unramified `A`-algebra means then `(17.4.2)` that `Spec((B вҠ—_A B)/рқ”Қ_{B/A})` is a sub-scheme induced on an
open and closed subset of `Spec(B вҠ—_A B)`, and one knows that for this to be so, it is necessary and sufficient that
`рқ”Қ_{B/A}` be a direct factor ideal of `B вҠ—_A B` (Bourbaki, _Alg. comm._, chap. II, В§4, nВ° 3, prop. 15); but it amounts
to the same to say that the `(B вҠ—_A B)`-module quotient `(B вҠ—_A B)/рқ”Қ_{B/A}` is projective (Bourbaki, _Alg._, chap. II,
3rd ed., В§2, nВ° 2, prop. 4).

(ii) If one recalls that a flat `A`-module of finite presentation is projective and conversely (Bourbaki, _Alg. comm._,
chap. II, В§5, nВ° 2, cor. 2 of th. 1), the assertion of (ii) follows from that of (i) and from `(17.6.2)`.

**Proposition (18.3.2).**

<!-- label: IV.18.3.2 -->

*Let `A` be a ring, `рқ”Қ` an ideal of `A` such that, for the `рқ”Қ`-preadic topology, `A` is separated and complete; put
`A_0 = A/рқ”Қ`. Then the functor*

```text
  B вҶҰ B вҠ—_A A_0
```

*is an equivalence from the category of finite Г©tale `A`-algebras to the category of finite Г©tale `A_0`-algebras.*

We shall first prove the following lemma:

**Lemma (18.3.2.1).**

<!-- label: IV.18.3.2.1 -->

*Let `A` be a ring, `рқ”Қ` an ideal of `A` such that, for the `рқ”Қ`-preadic topology, `A` is separated and complete.*

*(i) Every projective `A`-module of finite type `M` is separated and complete for the `рқ”Қ`-preadic topology, hence the
projective limit of the projective `(A/рқ”Қ^{n+1})`-modules `M/рқ”Қ^{n+1} M`.*

*(ii) Conversely, put `A_n = A/рқ”Қ^{n+1}`, and let `(M_n)` be a projective system of `A_n`-modules such that, for each
`n`, the homomorphism `M_{n+1} вҠ—_{A_{n+1}} A_n вҶ’ M_n` deduced from the di-homomorphism of transition `M_{n+1} вҶ’ M_n` is
bijective. Suppose moreover that the `M_n` are projective and `M_0` of finite type. Then `M = lim_вҶҗ M_n` is a projective
`A`-module of finite type such that the canonical homomorphism `M вҠ—_A A_0 вҶ’ M_0` is bijective.*

(i) There exists a free `A`-module of finite type `L` such that `M` is isomorphic to a direct factor of `L`; since `L`
is separated for the `рқ”Қ`-preadic topology, so is every submodule `N` of `L`, since `рқ”Қ^{n+1} N вҠӮ рқ”Қ^{n+1} L`; in
particular `M` is separated for this topology, and since the surjective homomorphism `f : L вҶ’ M` is continuous for the
`рқ”Қ`-preadic topology, its kernel `N` is closed for the topology induced by that of `L`; since `L` is complete and `f` a
strict morphism, one concludes that `M` is complete (Bourbaki, _Top. gГ©n._, chap. IX, 2nd ed., В§3, nВ° 1, prop. 4).

(ii) It follows from Nakayama's lemma that if `M_0` is generated by a finite family `(x_{i,0})` of `r` elements and if
for each `n`, `x_{i,n}` is an element of `M_n` whose image in `M_{n-1}` is `x_{i, n-1}`, then `(x_{i,n})_{1 в©Ҫ i в©Ҫ r}` is
a system of generators of `M_n` (Bourbaki, _Alg. comm._, chap. II, В§3, cor. 2 of prop. 4). That being so, for each `n`,
put `L_n = A_n^r`; if `(e_{i,n})_{1 в©Ҫ i в©Ҫ r}` is the canonical basis of `L_n`, let `u_n : L_n вҶ’ M_n` be the `A`-linear
map such that `u_n(e_{i,n}) = x_{i,n}` for each `i`. By hypothesis one has a split exact sequence

```text
  0 вҶ’ N_n вҶ’^{v_n} L_n вҶ’^{u_n} M_n вҶ’ 0
```

<!-- original page 116 -->

and since `L_n = L_{n+1}/рқ”Қ^{n+1} L_{n+1}` and `M_n = M_{n+1}/рқ”Қ^{n+1} M_{n+1}`, the vertical arrows in the commutative
diagram

```text
  0 вҶ’ N_{n+1} вҶ’^{v_{n+1}} L_{n+1} вҶ’^{u_{n+1}} M_{n+1} вҶ’ 0
              вҶ“                  вҶ“                    вҶ“
  0 вҶ’ N_n     вҶ’^{v_n}     L_n    вҶ’^{u_n}     M_n      вҶ’ 0
```

are all three *surjective*. Now one has `M = lim_вҶҗ M_n` and `L = A^r = lim_вҶҗ L_n`; if one puts `N = lim_вҶҗ N_n`,
`u = lim_вҶҗ u_n`, `v = lim_вҶҗ v_n`, one has, by virtue of `(0_III, 13.2.2)`, the exact sequence

```text
  (18.3.2.2)    0 вҶ’ N вҶ’^v L вҶ’^u M вҶ’ 0.
```

Moreover, since for each `n`, `v_n` is left-invertible and `M_n` is a projective `A_n`-module, it follows from
`(0, 19.1.8)` that the exact sequence `(18.3.2.2)` is split, which proves the lemma.

That being so, let us show first that the functor in the statement of `(18.3.2)` is *fully faithful*. Put, as in the
lemma, `A_n = A/рқ”Қ^{n+1}`; let `B`, `C` be two finite Г©tale `A`-algebras, and put, for each `n`, `B_n = B вҠ—_A A_n`,
`C_n = C вҠ—_A A_n`; by virtue of `(18.3.1)` and `(18.3.2.1)`, `B` and `C` are separated and complete for the `рқ”Қ`-preadic
topology, and one has `B = lim_вҶҗ B_n`, `C = lim_вҶҗ C_n`; moreover every homomorphism of `A`-algebras `u : B вҶ’ C` is
continuous for the `рқ”Қ`-preadic topologies, and therefore gives a projective system of homomorphisms of `A_n`-algebras
`u_n = u вҠ— 1 : B_n вҶ’ C_n` of which it is the projective limit; the converse being obvious, one has therefore a canonical
bijection

```text
  Hom_{A-alg.}(B, C) вҘІ lim_вҶҗ Hom_{A_n-alg.}(B_n, C_n).
```

But since `B` and `C` are *Г©tale* `A`-algebras, it follows at once from `(18.1.2)` that the canonical map

```text
  Hom_{A_{n+1}-alg.}(B_{n+1}, C_{n+1}) вҶ’ Hom_{A_n-alg.}(B_n, C_n)
```

is bijective for `n в©ҫ 0`, which finishes proving that the canonical map `Hom_{A-alg.}(B, C) вҶ’ Hom_{A_0-alg.}(B_0, C_0)`
is bijective.

To complete the proof of `(18.3.2)`, it suffices to see that for every finite Г©tale `A_0`-algebra `B_0`, there exist a
finite Г©tale `A`-algebra `B` and an `A_0`-isomorphism `B_0 вҘІ B вҠ—_A A_0`. Now, it follows from `(18.1.2)` that there is a
projective system `(B_n)` such that `B_n` is a finite Г©tale `A_n`-algebra and the homomorphisms
`B_{n+1} вҠ—_{A_{n+1}} A_n вҶ’ B_n` are bijective. It follows from `(18.3.1)` and `(18.3.2.1)` that the `A`-algebra
`B = lim_вҶҗ B_n` is a projective `A`-module of finite type and that `B_0` is isomorphic to `B вҠ—_A A_0`. To prove that `B`
is an Г©tale `A`-algebra, it suffices, by virtue of `(18.2.5)`, to show that for every maximal ideal `рқ”Ә` of `A`,
`B_рқ”Ә/рқ”Ә B_рқ”Ә` is a separable `(A/рқ”Ә)`-algebra. Now, since `рқ”Қ` is contained in the radical of `A` `(0_I, 7.1.10)`,

<!-- original page 117 -->

one has `рқ”Қ вҠӮ рқ”Ә`, and if `рқ”Ә_0 = рқ”Ә/рқ”Қ`, one has `A_0/рқ”Ә_0 = A/рқ”Ә` and `B_рқ”Ә/рқ”Ә B_рқ”Ә = (B_0)_{рқ”Ә_0}/рқ”Ә_0 (B_0)_{рқ”Ә_0}`; the
conclusion therefore follows from the fact that `B_0` is a finite Г©tale `A_0`-algebra `(18.2.5)`.

**Example (18.3.3).** вҖ” Prop. `(18.3.2)` applies in particular when `A` is a *separated and complete local ring*, `рқ”Қ`
being the maximal ideal of `A`, so that `A_0` is a *field* and the category of finite Г©tale `A_0`-algebras is identical
to that of finite separable `A_0`-algebras, hence isomorphic to direct composites of fields, separable and finite
extensions of `A_0`. In particular, if the field `A_0` is *separably closed*, these extensions are all identical to
`A_0`, and consequently every Г©tale cover of `Spec(A)` is *trivial* `(18.2.7)` by virtue of `(18.3.2)`.

**Theorem (18.3.4).**

<!-- label: IV.18.3.4 -->

*Let `A` be a Noetherian ring, `рқ”Қ` an ideal of `A` such that `A` is separated and complete for the `рқ”Қ`-preadic topology,
`A_0 = A/рқ”Қ`. Put `S = Spec(A)`, `S_0 = Spec(A_0)`. Let `X` be an `S`-scheme proper over `S`, and put `X_0 = X Г—_S S_0`.
Then the functor*

```text
  Z вҶҰ Z Г—_X X_0
```

*from the category of `X`-schemes finite and Г©tale over `X` to the category of `X_0`-schemes finite and Г©tale over `X_0`
is an equivalence of categories.*

Let us show first that this functor is *fully faithful*. Let `Z'` and `Z''` be two `X`-schemes finite and Г©tale over
`X`. Put `S_n = Spec(A/рқ”Қ^{n+1})`, `X_n = X Г—_S S_n`, `Z'_n = Z' Г—_S S_n`, `Z''_n = Z'' Г—_S S_n` for each `n в©ҫ 0`. It
follows from `(III, 5.4.1)` that one has a canonical bijection `Hom_X(Z', Z'') вҘІ lim_вҶҗ Hom_{X_n}(Z'_n, Z''_n)`. Now, by
virtue of `(18.1.2)`, the canonical map `Hom_{X_{n+1}}(Z'_{n+1}, Z''_{n+1}) вҶ’ Hom_{X_n}(Z'_n, Z''_n)` is bijective,
which completes the proof of our assertion.

It remains to prove that if `в„¬_0` is a finite Г©tale `рқ’Ә_{X_0}`-Algebra, there exists an `рқ’Ә_X`-Algebra `в„¬` finite and
Г©tale and an isomorphism `в„¬_0 вҘІ в„¬ вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_X} рқ’Ә_{X_0}`. It follows from `(18.1.2)` that there is a projective system
`(в„¬_n)`, where `в„¬_n` is a finite Г©tale `рқ’Ә_{X_n}`-Algebra, and the second comparison theorem `(III, 5.1.4)` proves the
existence of a coherent `рқ’Ә_X`-Module `в„¬` and of a projective system of isomorphisms `в„¬_n вҘІ в„¬ вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_X} рқ’Ә_{X_n}`. The datum
of an Algebra structure on a Module `в„ұ` being equivalent to that of a homomorphism `в„ұ вҠ— в„ұ вҶ’ в„ұ` making commutative
diagrams in which only tensor powers of `в„ұ` intervene, it follows from `(III, 5.1.3)`, `(I, 10.11.4)` and `(I, 10.11.7)`
that `в„¬` is naturally endowed with an `рқ’Ә_X`-Algebra structure for which the isomorphism `в„¬_n вҘІ в„¬ вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_X} рқ’Ә_{X_n}` is an
isomorphism of Algebras. Moreover, `в„¬` is a *locally free* `рқ’Ә_X`-Module; this also follows from `(III, 5.1.3)`,
`(I, 10.11.4)`, `(I, 10.11.7)` and from the fact that, in the category of coherent `рқ’Ә_X`-Modules, locally free
`рқ’Ә_X`-Modules `в„ұ` may be defined as those for which the functor `рқ’ў вҶҰ в„Ӣom_{рқ’Ә_X}(в„ұ, рқ’ў)` is exact. Finally, to see that `в„¬`
is an Г©tale `рқ’Ә_X`-Algebra, it suffices `(18.2.5)` to show that for every closed point `x вҲҲ X`, `в„¬_x вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_{X,x}} k(x)` is
a separable `k(x)`-algebra. But since the structure morphism `f : X вҶ’ S` is proper, `f(x)` is a closed point of `S`,
hence belongs to `S_0`, since `рқ”Қ` is contained in the radical of `A` `(0_I, 7.1.10)`; the conclusion therefore follows
from the fact that `X_0 = fвҒ»В№(S_0)` and that `в„¬_0` is a finite Г©tale `рқ’Ә_{X_0}`-Algebra.

<!-- original page 118 -->

### 18.4. Local structure of unramified and Г©tale morphisms

**Lemma (18.4.1).**

<!-- label: IV.18.4.1 -->

*Let `A` be a ring, `B` a finite monogenic `A`-algebra, `u` a generator of the `A`-algebra `B`, `F вҲҲ A[T]` a polynomial
such that `F(u) = 0`, `F'` the derived polynomial; put `u' = F'(u)`. Then the ideal of `B`, annihilator of `О©^1_{B/A}`,
contains `u' B`; it is equal to `u' B` if the ideal `рқ”Қ` of `A[T]` formed by the polynomials `G` such that `G(u) = 0` is
generated by `F`, in other words if the canonical surjective homomorphism `ПҶ : A[T]/F В· A[T] вҶ’ B` transforming the image
of `T` into `u` is bijective.*

Put `C = A[T]`, so that `B = C/рқ”Қ`. One has the exact sequence `(0, 20.5.12.1)`

```text
  рқ”Қ/рқ”ҚВІ вҶ’ О©^1_{C/A} вҠ—_C B вҶ’ О©^1_{B/A} вҶ’ 0
```

and `О©^1_{B/A}` is therefore identified with the quotient `B/рқ”Қ'`, `рқ”Қ'` being the ideal generated by the elements
`G'(u)`, where `G` ranges over a system of generators of the ideal `рқ”Қ` `(0, 20.5.13)`; the lemma follows immediately.

**Proposition (18.4.2).**

<!-- label: IV.18.4.2 -->

*With the notations of `(18.4.1)`, let `рқ”®` be a prime ideal of `B`. Then:*

*(i) If `рқ”®` does not contain `u'`, `B_рқ”®` is a formally unramified `A_рқ”ӯ`-algebra (`рқ”ӯ` being the inverse image of `рқ”®` in
`A`); in other words, `Spec(B_рқ”®)` is formally unramified over `Spec(A)`.*

*(ii) Suppose moreover that `F` is unitary and generates `рқ”Қ`. Then, for `Spec(B)` to be Г©tale over `Spec(A)` at the
point `рқ”®`, it is necessary and sufficient that `u' вҲү рқ”®`.*

The hypothesis that `u' вҲү рқ”®` entails that `О©^1_{B_рқ”®/A_рқ”ӯ} = 0` `(0, 20.5.9)`, hence (i) follows from `(17.2.1)`.
Moreover, under the hypotheses of (ii), `B` is a free `A`-module by virtue of Euclidean division; since the annihilator
`рқ”Қ'` of `О©^1_{B/A}` is then equal to `u' B` by virtue of `(18.4.1)`, and `О©^1_{B/A}` is a `B`-module of finite
presentation `(16.4.22)`, the annihilator of `О©^1_{B_рқ”®/A_рқ”ӯ}` is equal to `u' B_рқ”®` (Bourbaki, _Alg. comm._, chap. II, В§2,
nВ° 4, formula (9)), and (ii) follows therefore from (i) and from the implication c) вҮ’ a) in `(17.6.1)`.

**Corollary (18.4.3).**

<!-- label: IV.18.4.3 -->

*With the notations of `(18.4.2)`, suppose that `F` is unitary and generates `рқ”Қ`. Then, for `B` to be an Г©tale
`A`-algebra, it is necessary and sufficient that `u'` be invertible in `B` (or, what amounts to the same, that the ideal
of `A[T]` generated by `F` and `F'` be equal to `A[T]`).*

Taking `(18.4.2, (ii))` into account, to say that `Spec(B)` is Г©tale over `Spec(A)` means indeed that `u'` does not
belong to any prime ideal of `B`, i.e. that it is invertible in `B`.

One says that a unitary polynomial `F вҲҲ A[T]` such that the ideal of `A[T]` generated by `F` and `F'` is equal to `A[T]`
itself is *separable*; it is immediate that this definition coincides with the usual definition (Bourbaki, _Alg._, chap.
V, В§7, nВ° 6) when `A` is a field.

**Lemma (18.4.4).**

<!-- label: IV.18.4.4 -->

*Let `A` be a local ring, `B` a finite monogenic `A`-algebra, `u` a generator of the `A`-algebra `B`. Let `рқ”«_i`
`(1 в©Ҫ i в©Ҫ r)` be maximal ideals of `B` such that `Spec(B)` is formally unramified over `Spec(A)` at the points `рқ”«_i`.
Then there exists a unitary polynomial `F вҲҲ A[T]` such that `F(u) = 0` and `F'(u) вҲү рқ”«_i` for every index `i`
`(1 в©Ҫ i в©Ҫ r)`. Moreover, if `k` is the residue field*

<!-- original page 119 -->

*of `A`, `f вҲҲ k[T]` the minimal polynomial of the image of `u` in `B вҠ—_A k`, there exists an `F вҲҲ A[T]` of which `f` is
the canonical image and such that `F(u) = 0`; such a polynomial `F` verifies the conditions `F'(u) вҲү рқ”«_i` for
`1 в©Ҫ i в©Ҫ r`.*

The maximal ideal `рқ”Ә` of `A` is the inverse image of each of the `рқ”«_i` `(II, 6.1.10)`; let `L = B вҠ—_A k`, which is a
finite `k`-algebra. Let `О¶` be the image of `u` in `L`, and let `n` be the rank of `L` over `k`; the minimal polynomial
`f вҲҲ k[T]` of `О¶` over `k` is therefore of degree `n`, and `L` is isomorphic to `k[T]/f В· k[T]`. If `рқ”«'_i = рқ”«_i/рқ”Ә B`,
the hypothesis entails that `Spec(L)` is Г©tale over `k` at the points `рқ”«'_i` `(1 в©Ҫ i в©Ҫ r)` by virtue of `(17.6.1, c)`,
hence `f'(О¶) вҲү рқ”«'_i` by virtue of `(18.4.2, (ii))`. Note now that `рқ”Ә B` is contained in the radical of `B`; since
`1, О¶, вҖҰ, О¶^{n-1}` form a basis of `L` over `k`, it follows from Nakayama's lemma that `1, u, вҖҰ, u^{n-1}` generate the
`A`-module `B`, and consequently there exists a unitary polynomial `F вҲҲ A[T]` of degree `n` such that `F(u) = 0`; in
addition, since `О¶` is a root of the canonical image of `F` in `k[T]`, this image is necessarily equal to `f`. But then
the image of `F'(u)` in `L` is `f'(О¶)`, and since `f'(О¶) вҲү рқ”«'_i`, one has `F'(u) вҲү рқ”«_i` for each `i`.

**Proposition (18.4.5).**

<!-- label: IV.18.4.5 -->

*Let `A` be a local ring, `k` its residue field, `B` a finite (resp. finite and of finite presentation) `A`-algebra.
Suppose moreover either that the field `k` is infinite, or that `B` is a local ring. Let `n` be the rank of
`L = B вҠ—_A k` over `k`. For `B` to be a formally unramified (resp. Г©tale) `A`-algebra, it is necessary and sufficient
that there exist a unitary separable polynomial `F вҲҲ A[T]` `(18.4.3)` such that `B` is isomorphic to a quotient of
`A[T]/F В· A[T]` (resp. isomorphic to `A[T]/F В· A[T]`). Moreover, one may suppose `F` of degree `n` (resp. `F` is
necessarily of degree `n`).*

The conditions are sufficient by virtue of `(18.4.2)`, without assuming `k` infinite or `B` local. To see that the
conditions are necessary, note that if `B` is a formally unramified `A`-algebra, `L` is a finite and separable algebra
over `k`, hence the direct composite of a finite number of finite and separable extensions `k_j` of `k` `(1 в©Ҫ j в©Ҫ r)`,
`k_j` being therefore generated by an element `Оҫ_j` of minimal polynomial `f_j` `(1 в©Ҫ j в©Ҫ r)` (Bourbaki, _Alg._, chap.
V, В§11, nВ° 4, prop. 4). Let us show that by virtue of the hypotheses made on `k` or `B`, there exists an element `О¶` of
`L` generating the `k`-algebra `L`. This is immediate if `B` is local, since then `r = 1`. Otherwise, `k` being supposed
infinite, one may suppose that the irreducible polynomials `f_j вҲҲ k[T]` are all distinct (by replacing if necessary each
`Оҫ_j` by `Оҫ_j + a_j`, for a suitable element `a_j вҲҲ k`); if one puts `f = f_1 f_2 вӢҜ f_r`, it is clear that `L` is
isomorphic to `k[T]/f В· k[T]` in both cases considered, hence is generated by an element `О¶` of minimal polynomial
`f вҲҲ k[T]` of degree `n`. If `u вҲҲ B` is an element whose image is `О¶` in `L`, Nakayama's lemma shows that the elements
`1, u, вҖҰ, u^{n-1}` generate the `A`-module `B`; this already shows that there exists a unitary polynomial `F вҲҲ A[T]` of
degree `n` such that `F(u) = 0`, `u` generating the `A`-algebra `B`, which is consequently isomorphic to a quotient
algebra of `A[T]/F В· A[T]`; moreover `B` is a semi-local ring, and at each of its maximal ideals `рқ”«_i` one has
`F'(u) вҲү рқ”«_i` by `(18.4.4)`, which proves that `F'(u)` is invertible in `B`, hence that `F` is a separable polynomial.
Finally, if `B` is an Г©tale `A`-algebra, `B` being a flat `A`-module of finite presentation `(1.4.7)` is a free
`A`-module, and `1, u, вҖҰ, u^{n-1}` form a basis of the `A`-module `B` (Bourbaki, _Alg. comm._, chap. II, В§3, nВ° 2, prop.
5), in other words the `A`-algebra `B` is

<!-- original page 120 -->

isomorphic to `A[T]/F В· A[T]`, and for every other unitary polynomial `G вҲҲ A[T]` such that `B` is isomorphic to
`A[T]/G В· A[T]`, `G` is necessarily of degree `n`.

**Theorem (18.4.6) (Chevalley).**

<!-- label: IV.18.4.6 -->

*(i) Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a morphism locally of finite type, `x` a point of `X`, `y = f(x)`, and put `A = рқ’Ә_{Y, y}`. For
`рқ’Ә_{X, x}` to be a formally Г©tale (resp. formally unramified) `A`-algebra, it is necessary and sufficient that there
exist a unitary polynomial `F вҲҲ A[T]` and a maximal ideal `рқ”«` of `B = A[T]/F В· A[T]` (resp. of a quotient algebra `B` of
`A[T]/F В· A[T]`) such that `рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is `A`-isomorphic to `B_рқ”«` and such that, if `u` is the image of `T` in `B`, one
has `F'(u) вҲү рқ”«`.*

*(ii) Suppose moreover that `f` is locally of finite presentation. Then, for `f` to be Г©tale at the point `x`, it is
necessary and sufficient that one can in addition take `B = A[T]/F В· A[T]`.*

The conditions are sufficient by virtue of `(18.4.2)`. To see that they are necessary, one may obviously restrict to the
case where `X` and `Y` are affine, and, taking remark `(17.4.1.2)` into account, to the case where `f` is formally
unramified and quasi-finite. Since `f` is affine, it follows from `(8.12.8)` that there exist a finite `A`-algebra `C`
and a maximal ideal `рқ”Ҝ` of `C` (necessarily above the maximal ideal `рқ”Ә` of `A`) such that `рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is `A`-isomorphic
to `C_рқ”Ҝ`. Moreover `(17.4.1.2)`, the residue field `C/рқ”Ҝ = C_рқ”Ҝ/рқ”Ҝ C_рқ”Ҝ` is a finite separable extension of `k = A/рқ”Ә`, hence
of the form `k[v]`, where `v` is separable over `k`. Let `рқ”Ҝ_i` `(1 в©Ҫ i в©Ҫ h)` be the maximal ideals of the semi-local
ring `C` other than `рқ”Ҝ`; there exists an element `u вҲҲ C` belonging to all the `рқ”Ҝ_i` and such that its image in `C/рқ”Ҝ` is
equal to `v` (Bourbaki, _Alg. comm._, chap. II, В§1, nВ° 2, prop. 5). We shall show that the sub-`A`-algebra `B = A[u]` of
`C` and the ideal (necessarily maximal since `C` is finite over `B`) `рқ”« = рқ”Ҝ вҲ© B` of `B` answer the question.

To handle the case where `рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is a formally unramified `A`-algebra, it will suffice to prove that `B_рқ”«` is
isomorphic to `C_рқ”Ҝ`; indeed, `B_рқ”«` will then be formally unramified over `A`, and the existence of the polynomial
`F вҲҲ A[T]` having the properties of the statement will follow from `(18.4.4)`. Note now that, since `f` is formally
unramified, `C/рқ”Ҝ` is isomorphic to the `A`-algebra `C_рқ”Ҝ/рқ”Ә C_рқ”Ҝ` `(17.4.1.2)`. One is thus reduced to proving the
following lemma:

**Lemma (18.4.6.1).**

<!-- label: IV.18.4.6.1 -->

*Let `A` be a local ring, `рқ”Ә` its maximal ideal, `C` a finite `A`-algebra, `рқ”Ҝ` a maximal ideal of `C`. Let `u` be an
element of `C` belonging to all the maximal ideals of `C` distinct from `рқ”Ҝ`, not belonging to `рқ”Ҝ`, and such that
`C_рқ”Ҝ/рқ”Ә C_рқ”Ҝ` is a monogenic algebra over `k = A/рқ”Ә`, generated by the image of `u` in `C_рқ”Ҝ/рқ”Ә C_рқ”Ҝ`. Put `B = A[u]`,
`рқ”« = рқ”Ҝ вҲ© B`. Then the canonical homomorphism `B_рқ”« вҶ’ C_рқ”Ҝ` is an isomorphism.*

Put `R = B вҲ’ рқ”«`, `S = C вҲ’ рқ”Ҝ`, so that `B_рқ”« = RвҒ»В№ B` and `C_рқ”Ҝ = SвҒ»В№ C`; the canonical homomorphism `B_рқ”« вҶ’ C_рқ”Ҝ` may be
written as the composite

```text
  RвҒ»В№ B вҶ’ RвҒ»В№ C вҶ’ SвҒ»В№ C
```

and it suffices to show that each of these two homomorphisms is bijective.

Let us first show that `h : RвҒ»В№ C вҶ’ SвҒ»В№ C = C_рқ”Ҝ` is bijective; it suffices to see that the images in `RвҒ»В№ C` of the
elements of `S` are invertible, or again that every maximal ideal `рқ”ӯ` of `RвҒ»В№ C` has an inverse image in `C` not meeting
`S`, hence necessarily equal to `рқ”Ҝ`. Now, since `RвҒ»В№ C` is a `(RвҒ»В№ B)`-algebra finite, the inverse image of `рқ”ӯ` in

<!-- original page 121 -->

`RвҒ»В№ B = B_рқ”«` is the unique maximal ideal `рқ”« B_рқ”«` of this ring, hence the inverse image of `рқ”ӯ` in `B` is equal to `рқ”«`.
But on the other hand, if `рқ”®` is the inverse image of `рқ”ӯ` in `C`, one has `рқ”® вҲ© B = рқ”«`, and since `рқ”«` is maximal in `B`
and `C` is a `B`-algebra finite, `рқ”®` is necessarily one of the maximal ideals of `C`; in addition, one has `u вҲү рқ”®` since
`u вҲү рқ”«` and `u вҲҲ B`, hence by hypothesis one has necessarily `рқ”® = рқ”Ҝ`.

On the other hand, since `B вҠӮ C`, the homomorphism `g : RвҒ»В№ B вҶ’ RвҒ»В№ C` is injective `(0_I, 1.3.2)`; to see that it is
surjective, note that `RвҒ»В№ C` is a `(RвҒ»В№ B)`-module of finite type, and on the other hand that `рқ”Ә RвҒ»В№ B` is contained in
the maximal ideal of the local ring `RвҒ»В№ B`; by virtue of Nakayama's lemma, it suffices to prove that the homomorphism
`RвҒ»В№ B/рқ”Ә RвҒ»В№ B вҶ’ RвҒ»В№ C/рқ”Ә RвҒ»В№ C` is surjective. But by virtue of the first part of the proof, `RвҒ»В№ C/рқ”Ә RвҒ»В№ C` is
identified with `C_рқ”Ҝ/рқ”Ә C_рқ”Ҝ`; by hypothesis this `k`-algebra is generated by the image of `u`, and a fortiori it is equal
to the image of `RвҒ»В№ B/рқ”Ә RвҒ»В№ B`.

Consider in the second place the case where `f` is Г©tale at the point `x`. Replacing `X` by a neighbourhood of `x`, one
may suppose that `X` is a neighbourhood of `рқ”«` in `Spec(B)` `(1.7.2)`. Put `B' = Spec(A[T]/F В· A[T])` and let `рқ”«'` be
the inverse image of `рқ”«` in `B'`; since the image of `F'(T)` in `B'` does not belong to `рқ”«'` by hypothesis, the morphism
`Spec(B') вҶ’ Spec(A)` is Г©tale at the point `рқ”«'` by `(18.4.2, (ii))`. Since by hypothesis `Spec(B) вҶ’ Spec(A)` is Г©tale at
the point `рқ”«`, one concludes `(17.3.4)` that `Spec(B) вҶ’ Spec(B')` is Г©tale at the point `рқ”«`; but since this morphism is
an immersion, it can be Г©tale at a point only if it is a local isomorphism at that point `(17.9.1)`, hence `B_рқ”«` and
`B'_{рқ”«'}` are isomorphic.

Finally, suppose that `рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is a formally Г©tale `A`-algebra; with the previous notations, it follows from
`(17.1.5)` that `B_рқ”«` is a formally Г©tale `B_рқ”«`-algebra; but since the homomorphism `B_рқ”« вҶ’ рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is surjective, this
can hold only if this homomorphism is bijective `(0, 19.10.3, (i))`. This completes the proof of `(18.4.6)`.

**Corollary (18.4.7).**

<!-- label: IV.18.4.7 -->

*Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a morphism locally of finite type, `x` a point of `X`. For `f` to be formally unramified at the
point `x`, it is necessary and sufficient that there exist an open neighbourhood `U` of `x` such that `f | U` factors as
`U вҶ’^j X' вҶ’^h Y`, where `h` is an Г©tale morphism and `j` a closed immersion.*

One may obviously restrict to the case where `Y = Spec(R)` is affine and `f` of finite type. If `A = рқ’Ә_{Y, y}` with
`y = f(x)`, the condition for `f` to be formally unramified at the point `x` is equivalent, by virtue of `(17.4.1.2)`,
to saying that `рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is a formally unramified `A`-algebra. If this is so, one may apply `(18.4.6, (i))`; replacing
if necessary `Y` by an affine neighbourhood of `y`, one may suppose (with the notations of `(18.4.6)`) that the
polynomial `F` is the image in `A[T]` of a unitary polynomial `G вҲҲ R[T]`. One then puts `X' = Spec(R[T]/G В· R[T])`; let
`x'` be the image of the point `рқ”«` of `Spec(B)` under the morphism corresponding to the composite homomorphism
`R[T]/G В· R[T] вҶ’ A[T]/F В· A[T] вҶ’ B`. It follows from `(18.4.2)` that the morphism `h : X' вҶ’ Y` corresponding to the
canonical homomorphism `R вҶ’ R[T]/G В· R[T]` is Г©tale at the point `x'`, hence, by restricting if necessary `X'` and `Y`
to open neighbourhoods of `x'` and `y` respectively, one may suppose `h` Г©tale. On the other hand, by virtue of
`(I, 6.5.1, (ii))` and of `(1.7.2)`, it follows from the fact that one has a local homomorphism
`ПҶ : рқ’Ә_{X', x'} вҶ’ рқ’Ә_{X, x}` that this homomorphism corresponds to a

<!-- original page 122 -->

morphism `j : U вҶ’ X'` of an open neighbourhood `U` of `x` in `X'`; by restricting `U` if necessary, one may, by applying
`(I, 6.5.1, (i))`, suppose that `h вҲҳ j = f | U`, hence `j` is of finite type `(I, 6.3.4, (v))`; finally, the
homomorphism `ПҶ` is surjective by `(18.4.6, (i))`, hence it follows from `(I, 6.5.4, (i))` that one may, by restricting
`U` and `X'` again, suppose that `j` is a closed immersion. This proves therefore the necessity of the stated condition;
its sufficiency is immediate `(17.1.3, (i) and (ii))`.

**Corollary (18.4.8).**

<!-- label: IV.18.4.8 -->

*Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a morphism locally of finite presentation. For `f` to be unramified (resp. Г©tale), it is necessary
and sufficient that there exist a family of flat morphisms `g_Оұ : Y_Оұ вҶ’ Y` and, for each `Оұ`, an open set `U_Оұ` in
`X_Оұ = X Г—_Y Y_Оұ`, such that, if `g'_Оұ : X_Оұ вҶ’ X` and `f_Оұ : X_Оұ вҶ’ Y_Оұ` are the canonical projections, the `g'_Оұ(U_Оұ)`
form a cover of `X`, and each of the composite morphisms `U_Оұ вҶ’ X_Оұ вҶ’ Y_Оұ` is a closed immersion (resp. an open
immersion). One may moreover then take the `g_Оұ` Г©tale.*

The necessity of the condition for Г©tale morphisms is trivial, by taking a single `Y_Оұ` equal to `X`, the morphism `g_Оұ`
being equal to `f`, and the open set `U вҠӮ X Г—_Y X` being the diagonal. When `f` is unramified, the necessity of the
condition follows from `(18.4.7)`; one takes an open cover `(V_Оұ)` of `X` such that for each `Оұ`, `f | V_Оұ` factors as
`V_Оұ вҶ’^{j_Оұ} Y_Оұ вҶ’ Y`, where `j_Оұ` is a closed immersion and `g_Оұ` an Г©tale morphism. Then `j_Оұ : V_Оұ вҶ’ Y_Оұ` factors as
`V_Оұ вҶ’^{s_Оұ} X_Оұ вҶ’^{f_Оұ} Y_Оұ`, where `s_Оұ` is a `V_Оұ`-section of `X_Оұ`, and since the morphism `g'_Оұ : X_Оұ вҶ’ X` is
Г©tale, `s_Оұ` is an open immersion `(17.4.1)`, and it suffices to take `U_Оұ = s_Оұ(V_Оұ)` to answer the question.

The sufficiency of the conditions follows from `(17.7.1)`; one concludes from it that `f` is unramified (resp. Г©tale) at
each point of `g'_Оұ(U_Оұ)`, hence in `X` entirely since the `g'_Оұ(U_Оұ)` cover `X`.

**Proposition (18.4.9).**

<!-- label: IV.18.4.9 -->

*Let `S` be a prescheme, `f : X вҶ’ S` a morphism, `h : Y вҶ’ S` a morphism locally of finite presentation, `g : X вҶ’ Y` an
`S`-morphism, `x` a point of `X`, `y = g(x)`. The following conditions are equivalent:*

*a) `h` is Г©tale at the point `y` and `g` is flat at the point `x`.*

*b) `h` is unramified at the point `y` and `f` is flat at the point `x`.*

Since `f = h вҲҳ g`, a) entails that `f` is flat at the point `x` `(2.1.6)`, and obviously that `h` is unramified at the
point `y`, hence a) implies b).

To prove that b) entails a), one may first suppose that `h` is unramified (by replacing `Y` by a neighbourhood of `y`);
then, by replacing `S` by an open neighbourhood of `s = h(y) = f(x)`, one may suppose that there exist an Г©tale morphism
`u : S' вҶ’ S`, a point `y'` of `Y' = Y Г—_S S'` above `y`, and an open neighbourhood `V` of `y'` in `Y'` such that, if
`h' = h_{(S')} : Y' вҶ’ S'`, the restriction of `h'` to `V` is a closed immersion `(18.4.8)`. If one then proves that `h'`
is Г©tale at the point `y'`, it will follow that `h` is Г©tale at the point `y` `(17.7.1, (ii))`; in addition,
`f' = f_{(S')} : X Г—_S S' вҶ’ S'` is flat at every point `x'` above `x`. Since the projections `v : Y' вҶ’ Y`, `w : X' вҶ’ X`
are Г©tale morphisms (hence flat), if one proves that `g' = g_{(S')} : X_{(S')} вҶ’ Y_{(S')}` is flat at the point `x'`, it
will follow from `(2.2.11, (iv))` that `g` will be flat at the point `x`. One may therefore restrict to the case where
`h` is a closed immersion

<!-- original page 123 -->

of finite presentation, `f` being supposed flat at the point `x`. Let `рқ’Ҙ` be the quasi-coherent Ideal of finite type of
`рқ’Ә_S` which defines the closed sub-prescheme `Y` of `S`. The hypothesis that `f` is flat at the point `x` entails that
the homomorphism `рқ’Ә_{S, s} вҶ’ рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is injective `(0_I, 6.5.1)`; a fortiori the homomorphism `рқ’Ҙ_s вҶ’ рқ’Ә_{Y, y}` is
injective, which means that `рқ’Ҙ_s = 0`, since this is the kernel of the preceding homomorphism. Since `рқ’Ҙ` is of finite
type, there is an open neighbourhood `U` of `s` in `S` such that `рқ’Ҙ | U = 0` `(0_I, 5.2.2)`. One may therefore suppose
that `h` is an open immersion, and then it is clear that `g` is flat at the point `x`.

**Proposition (18.4.10).**

<!-- label: IV.18.4.10 -->

*Let `P(f, x)` denote a property verifying the following conditions:*

*1В° For every morphism `f : X вҶ’ Y` and every local isomorphism `h : Y вҶ’ Z`, `P(f, x)` is equivalent to `P(h вҲҳ f, x)` for
`x вҲҲ X`.*

*2В° For every morphism `f : X вҶ’ Y`, every Г©tale morphism `g : Y' вҶ’ Y`, every point `x вҲҲ X`, if one puts `X' = X Г—_Y Y'`,
`f' = f_{(Y')} : X' вҶ’ Y'`, and if `x' вҲҲ X'` is above `x`, the properties `P(f, x)` and `P(f', x')` are equivalent
("invariance under Г©tale base change").*

*Let then `S` be a prescheme, `f : X вҶ’ S` and `h : Y вҶ’ S` two morphisms, `g : X вҶ’ Y` an `S`-morphism, `x` a point of
`X`, `y = g(x)`, and suppose `h` Г©tale at the point `y`. Then the properties `P(f, x)` and `P(g, x)` are equivalent.*

With the same notations as in the proof of `(18.4.9)` and by replacing `S` (resp. `Y`) by a neighbourhood of `s = h(y)`
(resp. of `y`), one may here, by virtue of `(18.4.8)`, find an Г©tale morphism `u : S' вҶ’ S` such that `h'` is an open
immersion; if `x' вҲҲ X'` is above `x`, `P(f', x')` (resp. `P(g', x')`) is then by hypothesis equivalent to `P(f, x)`
(resp. `P(g, x)`). One may therefore restrict to the case where `h` is an open immersion. Since the hypothesis entails
that `P(g, x)` is then equivalent to `P(h вҲҳ g, x)`, one deduces the conclusion.

**Examples (18.4.11).** вҖ” One may take for property `P(f, x)` any one of the following, taking `(17.7.4, (ii))` into
account:

(i) `f` is flat at the point `x` `(2.2.11, (iv))`;

(ii) `f` is locally of finite presentation and of codepth `в©Ҫ n` at the point `x` `(6.8.1 and 6.7.8)`;

(iii) `f` is locally of finite presentation and Cohen-Macaulay at the point `x` `(6.8.1 and 6.7.8)`;

(iv) `f` is locally of finite presentation and possesses property `(S_n)` at the point `x` `(6.8.1 and 6.7.8)`;

(v) `f` is locally of finite presentation and possesses property `(R_n)` at the point `x` `(6.8.1 and 6.7.8)`;

(vi) `f` is locally of finite presentation and normal at the point `x` `(6.8.1 and 6.7.8)`;

(vii) `f` is locally of finite presentation and reduced at the point `x` `(6.8.1 and 6.7.8)`;

(viii) `f` is unramified at the point `x` `(17.7.4)`;

(ix) `f` is smooth at the point `x` `(17.7.4)`;

(x) `f` is Г©tale at the point `x` `(17.7.4)`.

<!-- original page 124 -->

**Corollary (18.4.12).**

<!-- label: IV.18.4.12 -->

*(i) Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a morphism locally of finite type, `x` a point of `X`. If `f` is flat and formally unramified at
the point `x`, then, in every factorization `f | U : U вҶ’^j X' вҶ’^h Y`, where `U` is an open neighbourhood of `x`, `j` a
closed immersion and `h` an Г©tale morphism `(18.4.7)`, the homomorphism `рқ’Ә_{X', j(x)} вҶ’ рқ’Ә_{X, x}` corresponding to `j`
is bijective (in particular `рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is an essentially Г©tale `рқ’Ә_{Y, y}`-algebra `(18.6.1)`).*

*(ii) For a morphism `f : X вҶ’ Y` to be Г©tale, it is necessary and sufficient that it be locally of finite type, formally
unramified and flat.*

(i) Since the homomorphism `рқ’Ә_{X', j(x)} вҶ’ рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is surjective, it suffices to prove that it is injective, and for
that it suffices to make `рқ’Ә_{X, x}` into a faithfully flat `рқ’Ә_{X', j(x)}`-module, or merely a flat one
`(0_I, 6.5.1 and 6.6.2)`; in other words, it is a matter of showing that `j` is a flat morphism at the point `x`; but
since `h вҲҳ j = f` is by hypothesis flat at the point `x` and `h` is Г©tale, this follows from `(18.4.10)` and
`(18.4.11, (i))`.

(ii) There is only the sufficiency of the stated conditions to prove. For every `x вҲҲ X`, one has in an open
neighbourhood `U` of `x` a factorization of `f | U` having the properties considered in (i). Since by hypothesis `f` is
flat and formally unramified at all points of `U`, the result of (i) applies not only to `x` but to all points of `U`;
this means that if `рқ’Ҙ` is the quasi-coherent Ideal of `рқ’Ә_{X'}` corresponding to the closed sub-prescheme of `X'`
associated with `j`, one has `рқ’Ҙ_z = 0` for every `z вҲҲ U`, hence `j` is an open immersion, and `f` is consequently Г©tale
at every point of `U`, hence at every point of `X`.

**Corollary (18.4.13).**

<!-- label: IV.18.4.13 -->

*Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a morphism locally of finite type, `x` a point of `X`, `y = f(x)`. Suppose that `y` admits an open
neighbourhood which is a reduced prescheme having only a finite number of irreducible components. Then, for `f` to be
Г©tale at the point `x`, it is necessary and sufficient that `f` be flat and formally unramified at the point `x`.*

There is only the sufficiency of the condition to prove. The question being local on `X` and `Y`, one may suppose
`(18.4.7)` that `f` factors as `X вҶ’^j X' вҶ’^h Y` where `h` is Г©tale and `j` a closed immersion, and moreover that `Y` is
reduced and has only a finite number of irreducible components. Then `X'` is reduced `(17.5.7)` and, by replacing if
necessary `X'` by an open neighbourhood of `j(x)`, one may suppose that `X'` has only a finite number of irreducible
components: indeed, one may suppose `h` quasi-finite `(17.6.1)`, and since the maximal points of `X'` lie above the
maximal points of `Y` `(2.3.4)`, their number is finite. Everything comes down to showing, with the notations of the
proof of `(18.4.12)`, that one has `рқ’Ҙ_{x'} = 0` for all the points `x'` of a neighbourhood of `j(x)` in `X'`, knowing
that `рқ’Ҙ_{j(x)} = 0`. Now, by replacing `X'` by an affine neighbourhood of `j(x)`, one may suppose that all the
irreducible components of `X'` contain `j(x)`; if `X' = Spec(A')`, and if `рқ”ӯ'` is the prime ideal of `A'` corresponding
to the point `j(x)`, the morphism `Spec(A'_{рқ”ӯ'}) вҶ’ Spec(A')` is dominant, hence the corresponding homomorphism
`A' вҶ’ A'_{рқ”ӯ'}` is injective since `A'` is reduced `(I, 1.2.7)`. If `рқ’Ҙ = рқ”ҚМғ`, where `рқ”Қ` is an ideal of `A'`, `рқ”Қ` is
therefore identified with a subset of `рқ”Қ_{рқ”ӯ'}`, and the hypothesis `рқ”Қ_{рқ”ӯ'} = 0` therefore entails `рқ”Қ = 0`.

**Corollary (18.4.14).**

<!-- label: IV.18.4.14 -->

*Let `A` be a local ring of maximal ideal `рқ”Ә`, of residue field `k`, `B` a finite `A`-algebra.*

<!-- original page 125 -->

*(i) For `B` to be a formally unramified `A`-algebra, it is necessary and sufficient that `B вҠ—_A k` be an Г©tale
`k`-algebra.*

*(ii) For `B` to be an Г©tale `A`-algebra, it is necessary and sufficient that `B вҠ—_A k` be an Г©tale `k`-algebra and that
`B` be a flat `A`-module (which is equivalent to saying `(0_I, 6.3.3)` that for every maximal ideal `рқ”«` of `B`
(necessarily above `рқ”Ә`), `B_рқ”«` is a flat `A`-module).*

One obviously has only to prove the sufficiency of the stated conditions. It is clear that (ii) follows from (i) and
from `(18.4.12, (ii))`, taking `(17.1.2, (i))` into account. To prove (i), note that if `B вҠ—_A k` is an Г©tale
`k`-algebra, one has `О©^1_{B вҠ—_A k/k} = 0` `(17.2.1)`. Now one has `О©^1_{B вҠ—_A k/k} = О©^1_{B/A} вҠ—_B (B вҠ—_A k)`
`(0, 20.5.5)`, and since `B` is an `A`-algebra of finite type, `О©^1_{B/A}` is a `B`-module of finite type `(0, 20.4.7)`.
But since `B` is a finite `A`-algebra, `рқ”Ә B` is contained in the radical of `B` (Bourbaki, _Alg. comm._, chap. V, В§2, nВ°
1, prop. 1), hence Nakayama's lemma proves that `О©^1_{B/A} = 0`, and consequently `B` is a formally unramified
`A`-algebra `(17.2.1)`.

### 18.5. Henselian local rings[^18.5-azumaya-nagata]

**(18.5.1)** Let `X` be a prescheme, `в„°` a locally free `рқ’Ә_X`-Module of finite rank; the dual `в„°МҢ = в„Ӣom_{рқ’Ә_X}(в„°, рқ’Ә_X)`
is thus a locally free `рқ’Ә_X`-Module whose rank at every point of `X` is equal to that of `в„°` at that point, and the
canonical homomorphism `в„° вҶ’ в„Ӣom_{рқ’Ә_X}(в„°МҢ, рқ’Ә_X) = (в„°МҢ)МҢ` is bijective. For every morphism `X' вҶ’ X`, put
`в„°_{(X')} = в„° вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_X} рқ’Ә_{X'}`, which is a locally free `рқ’Ә_{X'}`-Module, and consider the set `О“(X', в„°МҢ_{(X')})` of
sections of this `рқ’Ә_{X'}`-Module over `X'`. We are going to see that one thereby defines a representable contravariant
functor

```text
  (18.5.1.1)    рқ’ұ : X' вҶҰ О“(X', в„°МҢ_{(X')})
```

from the category of `X`-preschemes to that of sets `(0_III, 8.1.8)`.

First of all, one has indeed defined a functor, for if `f : X'' вҶ’ X'` is an `X`-morphism of `X`-preschemes, one has
`в„°_{(X'')} = f*(в„°_{(X')})`, whence `(0_I, 4.4.3.2)` a map
`О“(X', в„°МҢ_{(X')}) вҶ’ О“(X'', f*(в„°МҢ_{(X')})) = О“(X'', в„°МҢ_{(X'')})` which completes the definition of the functor `рқ’ұ`. Let
us show next that the `X`-prescheme `рқҗ•(в„°)` `(II, 1.7.8)` represents the functor `рқ’ұ`. Indeed, it is immediate that one
has `(в„°_{(X')})МҢ = в„°МҢ_{(X')}`, hence `рқ’ұ(X') = О“(X', (в„°_{(X')})МҢ)`; taking `(I, 3.3.14)` into account, one is reduced to
defining a bijection `О“(рқҗ•(в„°)/X) вҘІ О“(X, в„°МҢ)`, and to verifying that the bijection `О“(рқҗ•(в„°_{(X')})/X') вҘІ О“(X', в„°МҢ_{(X')})`
is functorial in `X'`. Now, one has a canonical bijection of `О“(рқҗ•(в„°)/X)` onto `Hom_{рқ’Ә_X}(в„°, рқ’Ә_X)` `(II, 1.7.8)`, and the
transposition `u вҶҰ ЕҘu` is a canonical bijection of `Hom_{рқ’Ә_X}(в„°, рқ’Ә_X)` onto `Hom_{рқ’Ә_X}(рқ’Ә_X, в„°МҢ) = О“(X, в„°МҢ)` by reason of
the identification of `(в„°МҢ)МҢ` with `в„°`. The verification of the functorial property is immediate.

<!-- original page 126 -->

Let us further note that, in conformity with the general theory `(0_III, 8.1.6)`, the identity automorphism of `рқҗ•(в„°)`
corresponds canonically to a section `c` of `в„°МҢ_{(рқҗ•(в„°))}` over `рқҗ•(в„°)`, that is to say `(II, 1.4.1)` to a homomorphism of
`рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_X}^вҖў(в„°)`-Modules `u : рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_X}^вҖў(в„°) вҶ’ рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_X}^вҖў(в„°) вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_X} в„°МҢ`; for every affine open `W` of `X`, if one puts
`О“(W, рқ’Ә_X) = A`, if one identifies `О“(W, рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_X}^вҖў(в„°))` with a polynomial algebra `C = A[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n]`, so that the
`T_i` form a basis of `О“(W, в„°)`, and if finally one denotes by `(e_i)` the dual basis of `(T_i)` in
`О“(W, в„°МҢ) = О“(W, в„°)МҢ`, one sees at once that `u` corresponds to the homomorphism of `C`-modules such that
`u(1) = вҲ‘_{i=1}^n T_i вҠ— e_i`.

If `X' = Spec(A)` is affine and such that `в„°_{(X')}` is isomorphic to `рқ’Ә_{X'}^n`, `О“(X', в„°МҢ_{(X')})` is a free
`A`-module of rank `n`; in a figurative way, one may say that the object `рқҗ•(в„°)` represents "the set of points of the
affine space twisted over `X` defined by `в„°`".

**(18.5.2)** Recall `(II, 1.7.8)` that one has by definition `рқҗ•(в„°) = Spec(рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_X}^вҖў(в„°))`. Let `в„җ` be a quasi-coherent
Ideal of `рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_X}^вҖў(в„°)`, so that `Spec(рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_X}^вҖў(в„°)/в„җ)` is a closed sub-prescheme of `рқҗ•(в„°)`; we are going to interpret
it as representing a functor from the category of `X`-preschemes to that of sets. Note for this that a section
`u вҲҲ О“(X, в„°МҢ)` is canonically identified with an `рқ’Ә_X`-homomorphism `u : рқ’Ә_X вҶ’ в„°МҢ`, to which corresponds by
transposition an `рқ’Ә_X`-homomorphism `ЕҘu : в„° вҶ’ рқ’Ә_X`, and consequently a homomorphism of `рқ’Ә_X`-Algebras
`v : рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_X}^вҖў(в„°) вҶ’ рқ’Ә_X`. Let `Al(X, в„°МҢ, в„җ)` denote the set of `u вҲҲ О“(X, в„°МҢ)` such that `в„җ` is contained in the kernel
of `v`; it follows at once from these definitions that

```text
  X' вҶҰ Al(X', в„°МҢ_{(X')}, в„җ вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_X} рқ’Ә_{X'})
```

is a functor represented by `Spec(рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_X}^вҖў(в„°)/в„җ)`. If `X' = Spec(A)` is affine and such that `в„°_{(X')}` is isomorphic
to `рқ’Ә_{X'}^n`, `О“(X', в„°МҢ_{(X')})` can be identified with the set `A^n`, and `в„җ вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_X} рқ’Ә_{X'}` with an `рқ’Ә_{X'}`-Module
of the form `рқ”ҚМғ`, where `рқ”Қ` is an ideal of the polynomial ring `A[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n]`; the set
`Al(X', в„°МҢ_{(X')}, в„җ вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_X} рқ’Ә_{X'})` is then identified with the subset of `A^n` formed by the points `(t_1, вҖҰ, t_n)`
such that `P(t_1, вҖҰ, t_n) = 0` for every polynomial `P вҲҲ рқ”Қ`; in a figurative way, one may therefore say that the object
`Spec(рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_X}^вҖў(в„°)/в„җ)` represents "the algebraic subset of the affine space twisted `О“(X, в„°МҢ)` formed by the points
annulling the ideal `О“(X, в„җ)`". One also denotes this `X`-prescheme by `рқҗҖрқҗҘ(в„°, в„җ)`. One will note that if `в„җ` is an Ideal
of finite type of `рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_X}^вҖў(в„°)`, `рқҗҖрқҗҘ(в„°, в„җ)` is an `X`-prescheme of finite presentation, since `рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_X}^вҖў(в„°)` is an
`рқ’Ә_X`-Algebra of finite presentation.

**Lemma (18.5.3).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.3 -->

*Let `S` be a prescheme, `f : X вҶ’ S` a morphism finite and locally free `(18.2.7)`. Consider the contravariant functor
from the category of `S`-preschemes to the category of sets*

```text
  (18.5.3.1)    S' вҶҰ Of(X Г—_S S')
```

*where `Of(X Г—_S S')` is the set of subsets simultaneously open and closed of the space underlying `X Г—_S S'`. Then this
functor is representable by an `S`-prescheme `рқҗҺрқҗҹ(X)`, which is affine, Г©tale and of finite presentation over `S`.*

<!-- original page 127 -->

One has by hypothesis `X = Spec(в„¬)`, where `в„¬ = f_*(рқ’Ә_X)` is a finite and locally free `рқ’Ә_S`-Algebra. Put
`X' = X Г—_S S'`, `f' = f_{(S')}`, `в„¬' = в„¬ вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_S} рқ’Ә_{S'} = f'_*(рқ’Ә_{X'})`, so that `X' = Spec(в„¬')`; there is then a
canonical bijection, functorial in `S'`, of the set `Of(X')` onto the set `Id(в„¬')` of *idempotents* of the ring
`О“(S', в„¬') = О“(X', рқ’Ә_{X'})`. Indeed, by virtue of the equivalence of the category of `S'`-schemes affine over `S'` and
the opposite category of the category of quasi-coherent `рқ’Ә_{S'}`-Algebras `(II, 1.2.7 and 1.3.1)`, there is canonical
biunivocal correspondence between the decompositions of `X'` into a sum `X'_1 вЁҝ X'_2` of two sub-preschemes induced on
open sets of `X'` and the decompositions of `в„¬'` into direct composite of two Ideals `в„¬'_1`, `в„¬'_2`; these latter in
turn form a set in canonical biunivocal correspondence (and functorial in `S'`) with `Id(в„¬')`. It therefore suffices to
prove the lemma for the functor `S' вҶҰ Id(в„¬')`.

For this, we are going to show that there exists an Ideal of finite type `в„җ` of `рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_S}^вҖў(в„¬МҢ)` such that `Id(в„¬')` is of
the form `Al(S', в„¬МҢ', в„җ вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_S} рқ’Ә_{S'})` `(18.5.2)`. Note for this effect that since `в„¬` is an `рқ’Ә_S`-Algebra, its
inverse image `в„¬_{(рқҗ•(в„¬МҢ))}` is an `рқ’Ә_{рқҗ•(в„¬МҢ)}`-Algebra, and one may therefore form the *square* `cВІ`, in this Algebra, of
the canonical section `c` `(18.5.1)`; it corresponds canonically to a homomorphism
`u^{(2)} : рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_S}^вҖў(в„¬) вҶ’ рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_S}^вҖў(в„¬) вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_S} в„¬` of `рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_S}^вҖў(в„¬)`-Modules, and one verifies at once that for an affine
open `W` of `S`, with the notations of `(18.5.1)`, `u^{(2)}` corresponds to the homomorphism of `C`-modules such that
`u^{(2)}(1) = вҲ‘_{k} (вҲ‘_{i,j} c_{ijk} T_i T_j) вҠ— e_k`, where `(c_{ijk})` is the multiplication table of the algebra
`О“(W, в„¬)`. Let us show that the Ideal `в„җ` of `рқҗ’_{рқ’Ә_S}^вҖў(в„¬)` generated by the kernel of the homomorphism `u вҲ’ u^{(2)}`
answers the question. It suffices indeed to note that the ideal `О“(W, в„җ)` of `C` is generated by the polynomials
`P_k(T_1, вҖҰ, T_n) = T_k вҲ’ вҲ‘_{i,j} c_{ijk} T_i T_j` and that the *idempotents* of `О“(W, в„¬)` are precisely the elements
`вҲ‘_i t_i e_i` of this algebra such that `(t_1, вҖҰ, t_n)` annuls all the polynomials `P_k` `(1 в©Ҫ k в©Ҫ n)`. One therefore
deduces from `(18.5.2)` that the `S`-prescheme affine of finite presentation `рқҗҺрқҗҹ(X) = рқҗҖрқҗҘ(в„¬, в„җ)` indeed represents the
functor `(18.5.3.1)`. It remains to prove that `рқҗҺрқҗҹ(X)` is Г©tale over `S`, or, what amounts to the same, that it is
*formally Г©tale* over `S`. But if `S'` is an `S`-prescheme, `S'_0` a closed sub-prescheme of `S'` defined by a locally
nilpotent Ideal of `рқ’Ә_{S'}` (and having therefore the same underlying space as `S'`), it is clear that `X' = X Г—_S S'`
and `X'_0 = X Г—_S S'_0` have the same underlying space, hence the canonical map `Of(X') вҶ’ Of(X'_0)` is bijective, which
completes the proof `(17.1.1)`.

**Proposition (18.5.4).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.4 -->

*Let `S` be a prescheme, `S_0` a closed sub-prescheme of `S`; consider the following properties:*

*a) For every finite morphism `g : S' вҶ’ S`, the canonical map*

```text
  (18.5.4.1)    Of(S') вҶ’ Of(S' Г—_S S_0)    (cf. (18.5.3))
```

*is bijective.*

*a') For every finite and locally free morphism `g : S' вҶ’ S`, the map `(18.5.4.1)` is bijective.*

<!-- original page 128 -->

*b) For every Г©tale and separated morphism `g : S' вҶ’ S`, the canonical map*

```text
  (18.5.4.2)    О“(S'/S) вҶ’ О“(S' Г—_S S_0/S_0)
```

*is bijective.*

*The condition b) entails a'); if moreover `S` is quasi-compact and quasi-separated, the condition a) entails b).*

Let us first prove that b) entails a'). Suppose then b) verified, and let `g : S' вҶ’ S` be a finite and locally free
morphism; put `S'_0 = S' Г—_S S_0`, so that `g_0 = g_{(S_0)} : S'_0 вҶ’ S_0` is finite and locally free. Then it follows
from `(18.5.3)` that `P = рқҗҺрқҗҹ(S')` is an Г©tale and separated `S`-prescheme; moreover, the definition of the functor `рқҗҺрқҗҹ`
shows at once that if one puts `P_0 = рқҗҺрқҗҹ(S'_0)` (for the category of `S_0`-preschemes), one has `P_0 = P Г—_S S_0`. That
being so, one has by definition the commutative diagram

```text
        О“(P/S)   вҶ’  О“(P_0/S_0)
         вҶ“ вүҖ          вҶ“ вүҖ
        Of(S')   вҶ’  Of(S'_0)
```

where the vertical arrows are the canonical bijections. Since hypothesis b), applied to the morphism `P вҶ’ S`, entails
that the top row is a bijection, so is the bottom row, which establishes our assertion.

Before proving that a) entails b) when `S` is quasi-compact and quasi-separated, we shall establish the

**Lemma (18.5.4.3).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.4.3 -->

*If `S` and `S_0` verify condition a) of `(18.5.4)`, then, for every finite morphism `g : S' вҶ’ S`, `S'` is the unique
neighbourhood of `S'_0 = gвҒ»В№(S_0) = S' Г—_S S_0` in `S'`.*

Indeed, it amounts to the same to say that if `T'` is a closed subset of `S'` such that `T' вҲ© S'_0 = вҲ…`, then `T' = вҲ…`.
Now, if one denotes again by `T'` a closed sub-prescheme of `S'` having `T'` for underlying space, the composite
morphism `h : T' вҶ’ S' вҶ’ S` is finite and `hвҒ»В№(S_0)` is empty; condition a) applied to the morphism `h` entails that `T'`
is necessarily empty.

This lemma being established, let us prove first that under hypothesis a), the map `(18.5.4.2)` is injective. Indeed, if
`u'`, `u''` are two `S`-sections of `S'`, the fact that the morphism `S' вҶ’ S` is unramified entails that the prescheme
of coincidences of `u'` and `u''` is induced on an open set `U` of `S` `(17.4.6)`. If the restrictions to `S_0` of `u'`
and `u''` are the same, the fact that `u'` and `u''` are open immersions `(17.4.1)` entails that `U` contains `S_0`,
hence is equal to `S` by virtue of the lemma `(18.5.4.3)` applied to the case `S' = S`.

It remains to show that under hypothesis a), the map `(18.5.4.2)` is surjective (`S` being quasi-compact and
quasi-separated). Let then `u_0 : S_0 вҶ’ S'_0` be an `S_0`-section of `S'_0`; `u_0(S_0)` being quasi-compact in `S'`, may
be covered by a finite number of affine open sets

<!-- original page 129 -->

`V_i` such that the restriction `g | V_i` is a morphism of finite type; if `V` is the union of the `V_i`, one concludes
that `g | V : V вҶ’ S` is a morphism of finite presentation, being separated and locally of finite presentation by
hypothesis `(1.6.1)`. Replacing `S'` by `V`, one may therefore suppose that `g` is of finite presentation. Since `S` is
quasi-compact and quasi-separated and `g` is quasi-finite and separated `(17.6.1)`, it follows from the "Main theorem"
`(8.12.6)` that `g` factors as `S' вҶ’^j S'' вҶ’^f S`, where `j` is an open immersion and `f` a finite morphism. Put
`S''_0 = S'' Г—_S S_0`, `j_0 = j_{(S_0)} : S'_0 вҶ’ S''_0`, which is an open immersion, and
`f_0 = f_{(S_0)} : S''_0 вҶ’ S_0`, which is a finite morphism. Then `u_0` is also an `S_0`-section of `S''_0`. Since
`g_0 : S'_0 вҶ’ S_0` is Г©tale, `u_0` is an open immersion of `S_0` in `S'_0` `(17.4.1)`, hence `u_0(S_0)` is open in
`S'_0`, and a fortiori in `S''_0`; but on the other hand, since `f_0` is a finite morphism, hence separated, `u_0` is a
closed immersion of `S_0` in `S''_0` `(I, 5.4.6)`, hence `X_0 = u_0(S_0)` is both open and closed in `S''_0`. By virtue
of hypothesis a), there exists a subset both open and closed `X` of `S''` such that `X вҲ© S''_0 = X_0`. Let us show first
that the morphism `f : S'' вҶ’ S` is *Г©tale at the points of `X`*: indeed, the set `U` of points of `X` where `f | X` is
Г©tale is open and contains by hypothesis `X_0 вҠӮ S'_0`. But the lemma `(18.5.4.3)` applied to the finite morphism `f | X`
proves that `U = X`. On the other hand, `S' вҲ© X` is open in `X` and contains `X_0` by hypothesis, hence the same
reasoning proves that `S' вҲ© X = X`, that is to say `X вҠӮ S'`. It remains to show that, for every `s вҲҲ S`, the geometric
number `n(s)` of points of `X вҲ© fвҒ»В№(s)` is equal to `1`, for it will follow that `f | X` is radicial and surjective, and
since `f | X` is Г©tale, one will have shown `(17.9.1)` that `f | X` is an isomorphism of the open `X вҠӮ S'` onto `S`, of
which the inverse isomorphism `u` will be the `S`-section sought extending `u_0`. But since `f | X` is Г©tale and finite,
`s вҶҰ n(s)` is continuous on `S` `(18.2.8)`, and since `X вҲ© S_0 = X_0`, one has `n(s) = 1` on `S_0`; the set of points
`s вҲҲ S` such that `n(s) = 1` being open in `S` and containing `S_0`, it is equal to `S` by `(18.5.4.3)`. Q.E.D.

**Remark (18.5.4.4).** вҖ” One can show that the statement `(18.5.4)` remains valid when, in condition b), one assumes
only the morphism `g` Г©tale (but not necessarily separated) `[43, exp. XII]`.

**Definition (18.5.5).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.5 -->

*One says that a prescheme `S` and a closed sub-prescheme `S_0` of `S` form a **Henselian couple** if they verify
condition a) of `(18.5.4)`.*

Taking `(I, 5.1.8)` into account, it amounts to the same to say that `(S, S_0)` is a Henselian couple or that
`(S_red, (S_0)_red)` is one.

**Proposition (18.5.6).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.6 -->

*(i) If `(S, S_0)` is a Henselian couple, then, for every finite morphism `f : S' вҶ’ S`, if `S'_0` is the sub-prescheme
`fвҒ»В№(S_0)` of `S'`, the couple `(S', S'_0)` is Henselian.*

*(ii) Let `S = вЁҝ_Оұ S^{(Оұ)}` be a sum of preschemes, `S_0` a closed sub-prescheme of `S`, sum of the closed
sub-preschemes `S_0^{(Оұ)}` of the `S^{(Оұ)}`. For the couple `(S, S_0)` to be Henselian, it is necessary and sufficient
that each of the couples `(S^{(Оұ)}, S_0^{(Оұ)})` be so.*

Assertion (i) is an immediate consequence of the definition, since for every finite morphism `g : S'' вҶ’ S'`,
`f вҲҳ g : S'' вҶ’ S` is a finite morphism. Similarly, under the conditions of (ii), for a morphism `g : S' вҶ’ S` to be
finite, it is necessary and sufficient that each

<!-- original page 130 -->

of its restrictions `g^{(Оұ)} : S'^{(Оұ)} = gвҒ»В№(S^{(Оұ)}) вҶ’ S^{(Оұ)}` be so, and if one puts `S'_0 = gвҒ»В№(S_0)`,
`S'^{(Оұ)}_0 = (g^{(Оұ)})вҒ»В№(S_0^{(Оұ)})`, there is biunivocal correspondence between the open and closed subsets `U` (resp.
`U_0`) of `S'` (resp. `S'_0`) and the families `(U^{(Оұ)})` (resp. `U_0^{(Оұ)}`), where `U^{(Оұ)}` (resp. `U_0^{(Оұ)}`) is
an open and closed subset of `S'^{(Оұ)}` (resp. `S'^{(Оұ)}_0`), whence assertion (ii).

**Remark (18.5.7).** вҖ” Let `S = Spec(A)` be an affine scheme, `S_0` a closed sub-scheme of `S` defined by an ideal `рқ”Қ`
of `A`. Then, if the couple `(S, S_0)` is Henselian, the ideal `рқ”Қ` is necessarily contained in the radical of `A`.
Indeed, if `рқ”Ә` is a maximal ideal of `A`, `рқ”Ә` must belong to `V(рқ”Қ) = S_0`, by virtue of `(18.5.4.3)`, in other words one
must have `рқ”Қ вҠӮ рқ”Ә`, whence the conclusion. In particular, suppose that `S_0` is reduced to a point, that is to say that
the ideal `рқ”Қ` is *maximal*; then `рқ”Қ` must be the radical of `A`, in other words `A` must be a *local* ring, `S_0` being
the unique closed point of `Spec(A)`.

**Definition (18.5.8).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.8 -->

*One says that a ring `A` is **Henselian** if it is semi-local and if, denoting by `рқ”Ҝ` the radical of `A`, the couple
`(Spec(A), Spec(A/рқ”Ҝ))` is Henselian. One calls **Henselian local scheme** a scheme isomorphic to the spectrum of a
Henselian local ring.*

**Proposition (18.5.9).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.9 -->

*(i) For a semi-local ring `A` to be Henselian, it is necessary and sufficient that it be a direct composite of
Henselian local rings.*

*(ii) For a local ring `A` to be Henselian, it is necessary and sufficient that every finite `A`-algebra `B` be
isomorphic to a product of local rings.*

(i) Indeed, the definition, applied to `S = Spec(A)` and `S_0 = Spec(A/рқ”Ҝ)`, shows, since `S_0` is a finite discrete
closed subset in `S`, that `S` is the union of a finite number of open and closed subsets `S_i` `(1 в©Ҫ i в©Ҫ n)` pairwise
disjoint, each of which contains exactly one of the maximal ideals `рқ”Ә_i` of `A`; the conclusion follows from
`(18.5.6, (ii))` and from remark `(18.5.7)`.

(ii) Every finite morphism `S' вҶ’ Spec(A)` is of the form `Spec(B) вҶ’ Spec(A)`, where `B` is a finite `A`-algebra. If `k`
is the residue field of `A`, `Spec(B вҠ—_A k)` is a spectrum of an Artinian ring, hence finite and discrete. To say that
the couple `(Spec(A), Spec(k))` is Henselian therefore signifies that `B` is direct composite of rings `A_i` such that
`Spec(A_i вҠ—_A k)` is reduced to a point, that is to say that `A_i` (which is a finite `A`-algebra) must have only one
maximal ideal (Bourbaki, _Alg. comm._, chap. V, В§2, nВ° 1, prop. 1).

The study of Henselian rings is therefore essentially reduced to that of Henselian local rings.

**Proposition (18.5.10).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.10 -->

*If `A` is a Henselian ring, every finite `A`-algebra `B` is a Henselian ring (hence direct composite of Henselian local
rings `(18.5.9)`).*

Indeed, if `рқ”Ҝ'` is the radical of `B`, the inverse image of `рқ”Ҝ'` in `A` is the radical `рқ”Ҝ` of `A`, and every ideal of
`B` above a maximal ideal of `A` is a maximal ideal of `B`, hence the set `V(рқ”Ҝ')` in `Spec(B)` is the inverse image of
the set `V(рқ”Ҝ)` in `Spec(A)`. The proposition is then a consequence of `(18.5.6, (i))`.

**Theorem (18.5.11).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.11 -->

*Let `A` be a local ring, `рқ”Ә` its maximal ideal. The following conditions are equivalent:*

*a) `A` is Henselian, in other words, every finite `A`-algebra `B` is isomorphic to a product of local rings.*

<!-- original page 131 -->

*a') Condition a) is satisfied for all `A`-algebras `B` of the form `A[T]/F В· A[T]`, where `F вҲҲ A[T]` is a unitary
polynomial.*

*b) Let `S = Spec(A)`, `S_0 = Spec(k)`. For every Г©tale morphism `g : S' вҶ’ S`, if one puts `S'_0 = S' вҠ—_A k`, every
`S_0`-section `u_0` of `S'_0` is the restriction of an `S`-section `u` of `S'`.*

*c) For every morphism `f : X вҶ’ S`, separated and locally of finite type, and every point `x вҲҲ X` such that `f(x)` is
equal to the closed point `s` of `S` and that `f` is quasi-finite at the point `x` `(Err_{III}, 20)`, `X` is a sum of
two preschemes `X'`, `X''` such that `X' = Spec(рқ’Ә_{X, x})` and `f | X' : X' вҶ’ S` is a finite morphism.*

*c') For every morphism `f : X вҶ’ S` locally of finite type, and every point `x вҲҲ X` such that `f` is quasi-finite at the
point `x` and `f(x)` is equal to the closed point `s` of `S`, `рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is a finite algebra over `рқ’Ә_{S, s} = A`.*

*c'') For every morphism `f : X вҶ’ S` locally of finite presentation, and every point `x вҲҲ X` such that `f` is
quasi-finite at the point `x` and that `f(x)` is equal to the closed point `s` of `S`, `рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is a finite algebra of
finite presentation over `рқ’Ә_{S, s} = A`.*

Note first that condition c') (resp. c'')) is equivalent to the same condition where one supposes in addition `f`
separated, the question being local on `X`. Similarly, condition b) is equivalent to the same condition where one
supposes in addition `g` separated: indeed, it suffices to apply this latter to the restriction of `g` to an affine open
neighbourhood of the point `u_0(S_0)` in `S'`. Let us restrict ourselves therefore from now on to the case where, in b),
c') and c''), the given morphisms are separated.

The fact that a) implies b) and that b) implies a') is a particular case of `(18.5.4)`. Let us moreover show that a')
implies a). It is a matter of proving that if `e_0` is an idempotent of `C = B вҠ—_A k`, there exists an idempotent
`e вҲҲ B` whose canonical image is `e_0`. If `b` is an element of `B` whose image in `C` is `e_0`, the sub-`A`-algebra
`A[b] = B'` of `B` is finite, and the canonical image `C'` of `B' вҠ—_A k` in `C` contains `e_0`. Now, `B' вҠ—_A k` is a
finite `k`-algebra, hence the direct composite of finite local `k`-algebras, and consequently `e_0` is the image in `C'`
of an idempotent `e'_0` of `B' вҠ—_A k`. One is thus reduced to the case where `B` is monogenic, and consequently
isomorphic to an `A`-algebra quotient of an algebra of the form `A[T]/F В· A[T]`, where `F` is a unitary polynomial. Now,
by virtue of a'), `A[T]/F В· A[T]` is direct composite of local rings, hence so are all its quotient algebras, which
completes the proof of the existence of the idempotent `e`.

It is immediate that c) entails a), as one sees by reasoning by induction on the number of maximal ideals of the
semi-local ring `B`. To see that a) implies c), one may, by virtue of `(13.1.4)`, restrict to the case where `f` is an
affine and quasi-finite morphism. Then, by application of the "Main theorem" `(8.12.8)`, `f` may be written as a
composite morphism `X вҶ’^j Y вҶ’^g S`, where `g` is a finite morphism and `j` an open immersion. Since `Y = Spec(B)`, where
`B` is a finite `A`-algebra, it follows from a) that `B` is direct composite of local rings, which are obviously finite
`A`-algebras, and `рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is identified with one of these local rings since `f(x) = s`; in addition, every open of
`Y` containing `x` necessarily contains `Spec(рқ’Ә_{X, x})`.

It is trivial that c) implies c'), by virtue of the remark at the start. Let us prove that c') implies c''). Suppose
indeed c') verified, and prove that under the conditions

<!-- original page 132 -->

of c''), the set `Z = Spec(рқ’Ә_{X, x})` is then identified with an open and closed subset of `X`, which will establish c''
