`(I, 2.4.2)`. In the first place, the composite morphism `Z вҶ’^j X вҶ’^f S`, where `j` is the canonical morphism
`(I, 2.4.1)`, is finite and of finite presentation by hypothesis, and since `f` is separated and locally of finite
presentation, `j` is also a morphism finite and of finite presentation (`(II, 6.1.5)` and `(1.4.3)`); `j` is
consequently a closed morphism `(II, 6.1.10)`, which proves that `Z` is closed in `X`. It then follows from `(I, 2.4.2)`
and `(I, 4.2.2)` that `j` is a closed immersion. But if `рқ’Ҙ` is the Ideal of `рқ’Ә_X` defining `Z`, one has then by
hypothesis `рқ’Ҙ_x = 0`, hence also `рқ’Ҙ_z = 0` at every point `z` of an open neighbourhood `V` of `x` in `X`, since by
hypothesis `рқ’Ҙ` is a quasi-coherent `рқ’Ә_X`-Module of finite type (`(1.4.7)` and `(0_I, 5.2.2)`). Now, such a neighbourhood
contains `Z`, hence `Z` is open in `X` since `рқ’Ҙ | V = 0`.

Finally, c'') implies a'): indeed, if `B = A[T]/F В· A[T]`, the morphism `X = Spec(B) вҶ’ Spec(A) = Y` is finite and of
finite presentation, and the preceding proof shows that `B` is direct composite of the finite `A`-algebras `рқ’Ә_{X, x_i}`,
where the `x_i` are the points of the fibre of the closed point of `Y`.

**Corollary (18.5.12).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.12 -->

*Let `A` be a semi-local ring, `рқ”Ҝ` its radical; put `S = Spec(A)`, `S_0 = Spec(A/рқ”Ҝ)`. For `A` to be Henselian, it is
necessary and sufficient that, for every finite morphism `f : X вҶ’ S` and every Г©tale and separated morphism `g : Y вҶ’ S`,
if one puts `X_0 = X Г—_S S_0` and `Y_0 = Y Г—_S S_0`, the canonical map*

```text
  Hom_S(X, Y) вҶ’ Hom_{S_0}(X_0, Y_0)
```

*is bijective.*

The sufficiency of the condition follows from the equivalence of a) and b) in `(18.5.11)`, by applying this condition to
the case where `f = 1_S`. To see that the condition is necessary, note that if `A` is Henselian, the couple `(X, X_0)`
is Henselian by `(18.5.6, (i))`; in addition `Hom_S(X, Y) = О“(X Г—_S Y/X)` and
`Hom_{S_0}(X_0, Y_0) = О“(X_0 Г—_{S_0} Y_0/X_0)`; since `X Г—_S Y` is Г©tale and separated over `X`, the conclusion follows
from the fact that a) implies b) in `(18.5.4)`.

**Remark (18.5.13).** вҖ” The equivalent conditions a), a'), b) of theorem `(18.5.11)` are also equivalent to the
following ("*Hensel's lemma*"):

*a'') For every unitary polynomial `F вҲҲ A[T]`, of canonical image `F_0 вҲҲ k[T]`, and every decomposition `F_0 = G_0 H_0`
of `F_0` into a product of two coprime unitary polynomials `G_0`, `H_0` of `k[T]`, there exists a unique couple `(G, H)`
of unitary polynomials of `A[T]` having the following properties: `G_0` and `H_0` are the canonical images respectively
of `G` and `H`, one has `F = GH`, and the ideal of `A[T]` generated by `G` and `H` is equal to `A[T]`.*

We shall first establish the following lemma:

**Lemma (18.5.13.1).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.13.1 -->

*Let `A` be a local ring of residue field `k`, `F вҲҲ A[T]` a unitary polynomial, `B` the `A`-algebra `A[T]/F В· A[T]`.
There exists a canonical correspondence between the decompositions of `B` into direct composite of two `A`-algebras
quotients `B'`, `B''` and the decompositions `F = GH` of `F` into product of two unitary polynomials `G`, `H` of `A[T]`,
such that the ideal generated by `G` and `H` is equal to `A[T]`; the quotient algebras `B'`, `B''` corresponding to such
a pair of polynomials `G`, `H` are respectively `A[T]/H В· A[T]` and `A[T]/G В· A[T]`.*

<!-- original page 133 -->

If `F = GH` and if `G` and `H` generate the ideal `A[T]`, there are two polynomials `P`, `Q` of `A[T]` such that
`1 = PG + QH`. One deduces that the intersection of the principal ideals `рқ”һ = G В· A[T]` and `рқ”ҹ = H В· A[T]` is equal to
`рқ”  = F В· A[T]`: indeed, if `R вҲҲ G В· A[T] вҲ© H В· A[T]`, one may write `R = PRG + QRH`; now `RH` (resp. `RG`) is a multiple
of `F` since `R` is a multiple of `G` (resp. `H`), hence `R вҲҲ F В· A[T]`. Since `A[T] = рқ”һ + рқ”ҹ`, `A[T]/рқ” ` is direct sum of
the ideals `рқ”һ/(рқ”һ вҲ© рқ”ҹ)` and `рқ”ҹ/(рқ”һ вҲ© рқ”ҹ)`, canonically isomorphic respectively to `A[T]/рқ”ҹ` and `A[T]/рқ”һ`.

Conversely, suppose given a decomposition of `B` into direct composite of two `A`-algebras `B'`, `B''`, which are
canonically identified with two ideals `e'B`, `e''B` of `B`, corresponding to a decomposition `1 = e' + e''` of `1` into
orthogonal idempotents `e'`, `e''` of `B`. Put further `B_0 = B вҠ—_A k = k[T]/F_0 В· k[T]`, where `F_0` is the canonical
image of `F` in `k[T]`, of the same degree `n` as `F`; if `e'_0`, `e''_0` are the canonical images of `e'`, `e''` in
`B_0`, these are two orthogonal idempotents such that `1 = e'_0 + e''_0`, and `B_0` is therefore direct composite of
`B'_0 = e'_0 B_0` and `B''_0 = e''_0 B_0`. Let `t` and `t_0` be the canonical images of `T` in `B` and `B_0`; since
`B'_0` (resp. `B''_0`) is a finite `k`-algebra generated by `t'_0 = e'_0 t_0` (resp. `t''_0 = e''_0 t_0`), it admits a
basis of the form `{e'_0, t'_0, t'_0^2, вҖҰ, t'_0^{s-1}}` (resp. `{e''_0, t''_0, t''_0^2, вҖҰ, t''_0^{r-1}}`) with
`r + s = n`. On the other hand, `B` being a free `A`-module (with basis `{1, t, вҖҰ, t^{n-1}}`), `B'` and `B''` are
projective `A`-modules, hence free since `A` is a local ring (Bourbaki, _Alg. comm._, chap. II, В§5, nВ° 3, cor. of prop.
5); it therefore follows from what precedes and from Bourbaki, _Alg. comm._, chap. II, В§3, nВ° 3, prop. 5, that if one
puts `t' = e't`, `t'' = e''t`, `{e', t', вҖҰ, t'^{s-1}}` (resp. `{e'', t'', вҖҰ, t''^{r-1}}`) is a basis of the `A`-module
`B'` (resp. `B''`). There is therefore a unitary polynomial `H` (resp. `G`) of degree `s` (resp. `r`) of `A[T]` such
that `e' H(t') = 0` and `e'' G(t'') = 0`; since `t^h = t'^h + t''^h` for every integer `h в©ҫ 1`, and `t'^h = e' t^h`,
`t''^h = e'' t^h`, one has also `G(t) = e' G(t')` and `H(t) = e'' H(t'')`, whence `G(t) H(t) = 0`; one concludes that
the polynomial `G(T) H(T)` is divisible by `F(T)`; but since the degrees of these two unitary polynomials are the same,
one has `GH = F`. In addition, `B'` (resp. `B''`) is isomorphic to `A[T]/H В· A[T]` (resp. `A[T]/G В· A[T]`). Finally,
there are two polynomials `R`, `S` of `A[T]` such that `e' = R(t)` and `e'' = S(t)`; since
`R(t) = e' R(t') + e'' R(t'')`, one has necessarily `e'' R(t'') = 0` and similarly `e' S(t') = 0`, so that, by
definition of `G` and `H`, `R = QH` and `S = PG`, where `P`, `Q` belong to `A[T]`; the relation `1 = R(t) + S(t)` in `B`
thus gives by definition `PG + QH = 1 + LF` for some polynomial `L вҲҲ A[T]`, and since `F = GH`, this proves that the
ideal generated by `G` and `H` is `A[T]`, and completes the proof of the lemma.

This lemma being established, it suffices to apply it to the local ring `A` on the one hand, to the field `k` on the
other, to see at once that conditions a') and a'') are equivalent.

**Proposition (18.5.14).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.14 -->

*Every semi-local ring `A`, separated and complete for the `рқ”Ҝ`-preadic topology (where `рқ”Ҝ` is the radical of `A`) is
Henselian.*

Indeed, `A` is direct composite of separated and complete local rings (Bourbaki, _Alg. comm._, chap. III, В§2, nВ° 13,
cor. of prop. 19), hence one is reduced to the case where `A` is a local ring. Let us verify criterion a') of
`(18.5.11)`. Since `B` is a free `A`-module of finite type, it is obviously separated and complete for the `рқ”Ҝ`-preadic
topology,

<!-- original page 134 -->

which is also the `рқ”°`-preadic topology, where `рқ”°` is the radical of the semi-local ring `B`, for `B/рқ”Ҝ B` is an Artinian
ring of radical `рқ”°/рқ”Ҝ B`. One then knows (Bourbaki, _Alg. comm._, chap. III, В§2, nВ° 13, cor. of prop. 19) that `B` is
direct composite of local rings.

**Proposition (18.5.15).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.15 -->

*Let `A` be a Henselian ring, `рқ”Ҝ` its radical. Then the functor `B вҶҰ B/рқ”Ҝ B` is an equivalence from the category of
finite Г©tale `A`-algebras with the category of finite Г©tale `(A/рқ”Ҝ)`-algebras.*

The fact that the functor in the statement is fully faithful is a particular case of `(18.5.12)`. To show that this
functor is an equivalence of categories, one may restrict to the case where `A` is local; it then suffices to apply
`(18.1.1)` (for Г©tale morphisms), to `S = Spec(A)` and `S_0 = Spec(A/рқ”Ҝ)`, reduced to a single point.

**Remarks (18.5.16).** вҖ” (i) We do not know whether proposition `(18.5.15)` generalizes to a Henselian couple
`(S, S_0)`, even when `S` is affine and Noetherian.

(ii) Let `A` be a Noetherian ring, `рқ”Қ` an ideal of `A` such that `A` is separated and complete for the `рқ”Қ`-preadic
topology. Then the couple `(Spec(A), Spec(A/рқ”Қ))` is Henselian: indeed, for every finite `A`-algebra `B`, `B` is
separated and complete for the `рқ”Қ`-preadic topology `(0_I, 7.3.6)`. Replacing `B` by `A` and `рқ”Қ B` by `рқ”Қ`, everything
comes down to seeing that the map which, to every idempotent of `A`, associates its class `mod рқ”Қ`, is bijective. Now,
one has `A = lim_вҶҗ (A/рқ”Қ^n)`. Let `Idem(A)` denote the set of idempotents of `A`, and for every ring homomorphism
`ПҶ : A вҶ’ B`, let `Idem(ПҶ)` denote the map from `Idem(A)` to `Idem(B)` restriction of `ПҶ`; it follows from the definition
of the projective limit that one has `Idem(A) = lim_вҶҗ Idem(A/рқ”Қ^n)` for the maps `ПҲ_{nm} : Idem(A/рқ”Қ^m) вҶ’ Idem(A/рқ”Қ^n)`
restriction of the canonical maps `A/рқ”Қ^m вҶ’ A/рқ”Қ^n`. But since `Spec(A/рқ”Қ^n) вҶ’ Spec(A/рқ”Қ^m)` is a homeomorphism, the
`ПҲ_{nm}` are bijections (as one saw in the proof of `(18.5.3)`); this therefore proves our assertion.

**Theorem (18.5.17).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.17 -->

*Let `A` be a Henselian local ring, `S = Spec(A)`, `s` the closed point of `S`. For every smooth morphism `f : X вҶ’ S`,
the canonical map*

```text
  О“(X/S) вҶ’ О“(X_s/k(s))
```

*(where `X_s = fвҒ»В№(s)`) is surjective.*

The datum of a `k(s)`-section of `X_s` is equivalent to that of a point `x вҲҲ X` above `s` rational over `k(s)`, and it
is a matter of proving that there exists an `S`-section `u : S вҶ’ X` such that `u(s) = x`. Taking `(17.16.3, (i))` into
account, one may suppose that `f` is Г©tale. Then the conclusion follows from criterion `(18.5.11, b))`. (The reader will
note that by virtue of this criterion, the validity of `(18.5.17)` for a given local ring `A` is necessary and
sufficient for `A` to be Henselian.)

**Remark (18.5.18).** вҖ” The conditions of `(18.5.11)` are also equivalent to the following:

*d) For every morphism `f : X вҶ’ S` locally of finite type and every point `x вҲҲ X` such that `f(x)` is the closed point
`s` of `S` and that `рқ’Ә_{X, x}/рқ”Ә_s рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is a field canonically isomorphic to `k(s) = A/рқ”Ә_s`, there exists an open
neighbourhood `U` of `x` in `X` such that `f | U` is a closed immersion.*

<!-- original page 135 -->

It is immediate that d) implies condition b) of `(18.5.11)` since a closed Г©tale immersion is an open immersion
`(18.9.1)`. Conversely, suppose the conditions of `(18.5.11)` verified and let us prove d). The hypothesis of d) implies
that `f` is quasi-finite at the point `x` `(Err_{III}, 20)`, by virtue of `(13.1.4)`. Hence by virtue of condition c) of
`(18.5.11)`, `рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is a finite `A`-algebra and `Spec(рқ’Ә_{X, x})` an open neighbourhood `U` of `x` in `X`. In
addition, since `рқ’Ә_{X, x}/рқ”Ә_s рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is isomorphic to `k = A/рқ”Ә_s`, Nakayama's lemma proves that the homomorphism
`A вҶ’ рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is surjective, hence `f | U` is a closed immersion.

**Proposition (18.5.19).**

<!-- label: IV.18.5.19 -->

*Let `A` be a Noetherian and Henselian local ring, `S = Spec(A)`, `s` the closed point of `S`, `f : X вҶ’ S` a proper
morphism; put `X_s = fвҒ»В№(s)`. Then the map `Y вҶҰ Y вҲ© X_s` is a bijection of the set of connected components of `X` onto
the set of connected components of `X_s`.*

By considering a closed sub-prescheme of `X` having for underlying space a connected component of `X`, one is reduced to
proving that if `X` is connected and non-empty, then `X_s` is connected and non-empty. The fact that `X_s` is non-empty
follows from `(II, 7.2.1)`; to prove that `X_s` is connected, let us reason by contradiction, considering the Stein
factorization `f : X вҶ’^{f'} S' вҶ’^g S` of the proper morphism `f` `(III, 4.3.3)`; by hypothesis, the discrete finite set
`gвҒ»В№(s)` would contain at least two points. Since `A` is Henselian and `g` separated and of finite type, it would then
follow from `(18.5.11, c)` that `S'` would be a sum of two non-empty preschemes `S'_1`, `S'_2` (since the intersection
of one of them with `gвҒ»В№(s)` is reduced to a single point). Since `f'` is surjective `(III, 4.3.1)`, one would conclude
that `X` is a sum of two non-empty preschemes, contrary to the hypothesis.

<!-- original page 135 -->

### 18.6. Henselization

**(18.6.1)** Given a local ring `A`, we say that a local `A`-algebra `B` is **essentially Г©tale** if there exist an
Г©tale `A`-algebra `C` and a prime ideal `рқ”«` of `C` such that `B` is `A`-isomorphic to `C_рқ”«` and the composite
homomorphism `A вҶ’ C вҶ’ C_рқ”«` is local (in other words, that `рқ”«` lies over the maximal ideal `рқ”Ә` of `A`); this entails
`(17.6.1)` that `рқ”«` is the only prime ideal of `B` lying over `рқ”Ә`, since `B` is a local ring. If `B`, `B'` are two
essentially Г©tale local `A`-algebras, then every `A`-homomorphism `B вҶ’ B'` is local.

If `A'` is an essentially Г©tale local `A`-algebra and `A''` an essentially Г©tale local `A'`-algebra, then `A''` is an
essentially Г©tale local `A`-algebra. Indeed, by hypothesis we have `A' = B_рқ”«`, where `B` is an Г©tale `A`-algebra and `рқ”«`
a prime ideal of `B` lying over the maximal ideal of `A`, and `A'' = B'_{рқ”«'}`, where `B'` is an Г©tale `A'`-algebra and
`рқ”«'` a prime ideal of `B'` lying over the ideal `рқ”« B_рқ”«`. Setting `S = B вҲ’ рқ”«`, so that `A' = S^{вҲ’1} B`, `B'` is of the
form `S^{вҲ’1} C`, where `C` is a `B`-algebra of finite presentation. Consequently `C` is an `A`-algebra of finite
presentation and `A''` is of the form `C_рқ”Ҝ`, where `рқ”Ҝ` is a prime ideal of `C` lying over the maximal ideal of `A`.
Since `A'` is a formally Г©tale `A`-algebra and `A''` a formally Г©tale `A'`-algebra, `A''` is a formally Г©tale

<!-- original page 136 -->

`A`-algebra (for the discrete topologies `(0_IV, 19.3.5)` `(17.1.3)`); the morphism `Spec(C) вҶ’ Spec(A)` is therefore
Г©tale at the point `рқ”Ҝ` `(17.6.1)`, and consequently there exists an element `g вҲҲ C` such that `C_g` is an Г©tale
`A`-algebra, which proves that `A''` is an essentially Г©tale `A`-algebra.

Given a local ring `A`, there exists a set `рқ”Ҳ` of essentially Г©tale local `A`-algebras such that every essentially Г©tale
local `A`-algebra is `A`-isomorphic to an algebra belonging to `рқ”Ҳ`. To see this, it evidently suffices to observe that
there exists a set `рқ”ү` of `A`-algebras of finite type such that every `A`-algebra of finite type is isomorphic to an
algebra belonging to `рқ”ү`; one may take `рқ”ү` to be the set of quotients of the polynomial algebras `A[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n]`
`(n вҲҲ в„•)`.

In what follows, if `A` and `B` are two local rings, we shall denote by `Hom.loc(A, B)` the set of local homomorphisms
from `A` to `B`.

**Lemma (18.6.2).**

<!-- label: IV.18.6.2 -->

*Let `A`, `A'` be two local rings, `k`, `k'` their respective residue fields, `ПҶ : A вҶ’ A'` a (local) homomorphism making
`A'` into an essentially Г©tale `A`-algebra `(18.6.1)` and such that the corresponding homomorphism `k вҶ’ k'` is
bijective. Then, for every Henselian local ring `B`, the canonical map*

```text
  (18.6.2.1)    Hom(ПҶ, 1_B) : Hom.loc(A', B) вҶ’ Hom.loc(A, B)
```

*is bijective.*

Set `S = Spec(A)`, `Y = Spec(B)`, and let `s` and `y` be the closed points of `S` and `Y` respectively. By hypothesis,
`A'` is isomorphic to a local ring `рқ’Ә_{X, x}` of an `S`-scheme `X` Г©tale over `S`, at a point `x вҲҲ X` lying over `s`.
Suppose given a local homomorphism `ПҲ : A вҶ’ B`, making `Y` into an `S`-scheme; the problem is to see that there exists
one and only one `S`-morphism `f : Y вҶ’ X` such that `f(y) = x`. Set `X' = X Г—_S Y`, and note that since `k(x) = k(s)`,
there exists a single point `x' вҲҲ X'` lying over `x` and over `y`, and that `k(x') = k(y)`. It must be shown that there
exists a unique `Y`-section `f'` of `X'` such that `f'(y) = x'`. Now, the morphism `g : X' вҶ’ Y` is Г©tale and separated,
and the fibre `X'_y = g^{вҲ’1}(y)` has at the point `x'` the local ring `k(x') = k(y)` for its local ring. If one sets
`Y_0 = Spec(k(y))`, there exists therefore a unique `Y_0`-section `f_0` of `X'_y` such that `f_0(y) = x'`, and the
conclusion follows from the assumption that `B` is Henselian and from `(18.5.11, e)`.

We shall say that a local `A`-algebra `A'` satisfying the conditions of `(18.6.2)` is **strictly essentially Г©tale**.
Note that the criterion `(18.5.11, b)` signifies that, in order for `A` to be Henselian, it is necessary and sufficient
that every strictly essentially Г©tale `A`-algebra be `A`-isomorphic to `A`.

**Lemma (18.6.3).**

<!-- label: IV.18.6.3 -->

*Let `A` be a local ring, `A_1`, `A_2` two strictly essentially Г©tale local `A`-algebras.*

*(i) There exists at most one `A`-homomorphism (necessarily local) from `A_1` to `A_2`.*

*(ii) There exist a strictly essentially Г©tale local `A`-algebra `A_3` and two `A`-homomorphisms `A_1 вҶ’ A_3`,
`A_2 вҶ’ A_3`.*

Set `S = Spec(A)`; by hypothesis there are two `S`-schemes `X_1`, `X_2` Г©tale over `S`, and two points `x_1 вҲҲ X_1`,
`x_2 вҲҲ X_2` lying over the closed point `s` of `S` and such that `A_1 = рқ’Ә_{X_1, x_1}`, `A_2 = рқ’Ә_{X_2, x_2}`. Set
`X_3 = X_1 Г—_S X_2`; the hypotheses `k(x_1) = k(x_2) = k(s)` entail that there exists a single point `x_3 вҲҲ X_3` lying
over `x_1` and `x_2` and that `k(x_3) = k(s)` `(I, 3.4.9)`. Moreover, `X_3` is Г©tale over `S` `(17.3.3)`, so
`A_3 = рқ’Ә_{X_3, x_3}` satisfies the conditions of (ii). On the other hand,

<!-- original page 137 -->

we have seen that an `A`-homomorphism from `A_1` to `A_2` is necessarily local; it corresponds to an `S`-morphism `f`
from `X_2 = Spec(A_2)` to `X_1` such that `f(x_2) = x_1`, or again, setting `X_3 = X_1 Г—_S X_2`, to an `X_2`-section
`f'` of `X_3` such that `f'(x_2) = x_3`. Since `k(x_3) = k(x_2)` and `X_3` is connected, the uniqueness of `f` follows
from `(17.4.9)`, whence (i).

**(18.6.4)** Denote by `рқ”–` the subset of the set `рқ”Ҳ` defined in `(18.6.1)` consisting of the strictly essentially Г©tale
`A`-algebras belonging to `рқ”Ҳ`. It follows from `(18.6.3)` that the relation "there exists an `A`-homomorphism from `A_О»`
to `A_Ој`" is a preorder relation on `рқ”–` and makes `рқ”–` into an increasing filtered set. Indexing `рқ”–` by itself by means
of the identity map, it follows from `(18.6.3, (i))` that if `О» в©Ҫ Ој` in `рқ”–`, there exists a unique `A`-homomorphism
`ПҶ_{ОјО»} : A_О» вҶ’ A_Ој` and `(A_О», ПҶ_{ОјО»})` is evidently an inductive system of local `A`-algebras, the `ПҶ_{ОјО»}` being
local homomorphisms. Moreover, it follows from `(17.3.5)` that for `О» в©Ҫ Ој`, `A_Ој` is a strictly essentially Г©tale
`A_О»`-algebra.

**Definition (18.6.5).**

<!-- label: IV.18.6.5 -->

*One calls the **Henselization** of a local ring `A`, and denotes by `^h A`, the inductive-limit `A`-algebra of the
inductive system `(A_О», ПҶ_{ОјО»})` defined in `(18.6.4)`.*

This definition depends on the choice of `рқ”Ҳ` only in appearance; if `рқ”Ҳ'` is another set of essentially Г©tale local
`A`-algebras with the same property as `рқ”Ҳ`, and `рқ”–'` is the subset of `рқ”Ҳ'` consisting of the strictly essentially Г©tale
`A`-algebras, it follows from `(18.6.3, (ii))` that, for the preorder relations considered, `рқ”–` and `рқ”–'` are cofinal in
`рқ”–'' = рқ”Ҳ вҲӘ рқ”Ҳ'`, hence give the same inductive limit up to isomorphism. We shall also see below `(18.6.6, (i) and (ii))`
that `^h A` and the canonical homomorphism `A вҶ’ ^h A` form a solution of a universal problem, and consequently are
determined up to unique isomorphism.

One will note that if `A` is a field, one obviously has `^h A = A`. In the general case, `^h A` is also the
Henselization of all the strictly essentially Г©tale `A`-algebras `A_О» (О» вҲҲ рқ”–)`, for if `B` is a strictly essentially
Г©tale `A_О»`-algebra, `B` is also a strictly essentially Г©tale `A`-algebra `(18.6.1)`, hence (up to `A`-isomorphism) one
of the `A_Ој` for `Ој в©ҫ О»`, and the `A_Ој` such that `Ој в©ҫ О»` and such that `A_Ој` is a strictly essentially Г©tale
`A_О»`-algebra form a cofinal set in the preordered set of the `A_Ој`, by virtue of `(18.6.1)` and `(18.6.3)`.

**Theorem (18.6.6).**

<!-- label: IV.18.6.6 -->

*Let `A` be a local ring, `^h A` its Henselization.*

*(i) `^h A` is a Henselian local ring and the structure homomorphism `A вҶ’ ^h A` is local.*

*(ii) For every Henselian local ring `B`, the canonical map*

```text
  Hom.loc(^h A, B) вҶ’ Hom.loc(A, B)
```

*is bijective.*

*(iii) `^h A` is a faithfully flat `A`-module, and if `рқ”Ә` is the maximal ideal of `A`, `рқ”Ә В· ^h A` is the maximal ideal
of `^h A`, and the homomorphism `A/рқ”Ә вҶ’ ^h A / рқ”Ә В· ^h A` of residue fields is bijective.*

*(iv) If `ГӮ` and `(^h A)^вҲ§` are the separated completions of the local rings `A` and `^h A`, the homomorphism
`ГӮ вҶ’ (^h A)^вҲ§` deduced from the structure homomorphism `A вҶ’ ^h A` by completion is bijective.*

*(v) In order for `^h A` to be Noetherian, it is necessary and sufficient that `A` be so.*

*(vi) If `A` is Henselian, the canonical homomorphism `A вҶ’ ^h A` is bijective.*

<!-- original page 138 -->

Let `рқ”Ә_О»` be the maximal ideal of `A_О»`; it follows from the fact that, in `(17.6.1)`, a) implies c'), that for `О» в©Ҫ Ој`,
one has `рқ”Ә_Ој = рқ”Ә_О» В· A_Ој`, the homomorphism `A_О» / рқ”Ә_О» вҶ’ A_Ој / рқ”Ә_Ој` is bijective, and `A_Ој` is a flat `A_О»`-module. The
fact that `^h A` is local, that the homomorphism `A вҶ’ ^h A` is local, assertion (iii), and the sufficiency of (v) follow
therefore from `(0_III, 10.3.1.3)`; the necessity of (v) follows from the fact that `^h A` is a faithfully flat
`A`-module `(0_I, 6.5.2)`.

To prove that `^h A` is Henselian, let us apply the criterion `(18.5.11, b)`. Set `S = Spec(^h A)`,
`S_0 = Spec(^h A / рқ”Ә В· ^h A)`, and let `g : S' вҶ’ S` be an Г©tale morphism; set `S'_0 = g^{вҲ’1}(S_0)`, and let
`f_0 : S_0 вҶ’ S'_0` be an `S_0`-section of `S'_0`. Reasoning as in `(18.5.4)`, one may suppose that `g` is of finite
presentation. It then follows from `(8.8.2)` and `(17.7.5)` that there exist an index `О» вҲҲ рқ”–`, an Г©tale morphism
`g^{(О»)} : S'^{(О»)} вҶ’ S^{(О»)} = Spec(A_О»)` and, on setting `S_0^{(О»)} = Spec(A_О» / рқ”Ә A_О»)` and
`S'_0^{(О»)} = g^{(О»)вҲ’1}(S_0^{(О»)})`, an `S_0^{(О»)}`-section `f_0^{(О»)} : S_0^{(О»)} вҶ’ S'_0^{(О»)}` such that
`S' = S'^{(О»)} Г—_{S^{(О»)}} S`, `g = g^{(О»)} Г— 1` and `f_0 = f_0^{(О»)} Г— 1`. Let `s` be the closed point of `S`,
`x = f_0(s)`, `x^{(О»)}` the projection of `x` in `S'^{(О»)}`; since `x^{(О»)}` lies over the closed point `s^{(О»)}` of
`S^{(О»)}`, the local ring `C^{(О»)}` of `S'^{(О»)}` at the point `x^{(О»)}` is an essentially Г©tale `A_О»`-algebra;
moreover, since `f_0^{(О»)}(s^{(О»)}) = x^{(О»)}`, one has `k(x^{(О»)}) = k(s^{(О»)})`, in other words, `C^{(О»)}` is a
strictly essentially Г©tale local `A_О»`-algebra, and consequently `(18.6.1)` is `A_О»`-isomorphic to an `A`-algebra `A_Ој`
with `Ој в©ҫ О»`. There is therefore an `A_О»`-homomorphism `C^{(О»)} вҶ’ ^h A`, that is to say an `S^{(О»)}`-morphism
`h : S вҶ’ S'^{(О»)}` such that `h(s) = x^{(О»)}`, and consequently there does exist an `S`-section `f` of `S'` such that
`f(s) = x`, which completes the proof of (i).

To prove (ii), it suffices to note that one has `Hom.loc(^h A, B) = lim_вҶ’ Hom.loc(A_О», B)` and that by `(18.6.2)` the
canonical homomorphisms `Hom.loc(A_О», B) вҶҗ Hom.loc(A, B)` are bijective.

To establish (iv), note that for every `О»` and every integer `n > 0`, one has `рқ”Ә_О»^n = рқ”Ә^n В· A_О»`, and
`(рқ”Ә В· ^h A)^n = рқ”Ә^n В· ^h A = lim_вҶ’ рқ”Ә_О»^n`. One concludes, by the exactness of the functor `lim_вҶ’` in the category of
`A`-modules, that `^h A / (рқ”Ә В· ^h A)^n = lim_вҶ’ (A_О» / рқ”Ә_О»^n)`, and consequently it suffices to show that, for every
integer `n` and every index `О»`, the homomorphism `A / рқ”Ә^n вҶ’ A_О» / рқ”Ә_О»^n` is bijective. Now, this is true by hypothesis
for `n = 1`; on the other hand, since `A_О»` is a flat `A`-module, one has

```text
  рқ”Ә_О»^n / рқ”Ә_О»^{n+1} = (рқ”Ә^n / рқ”Ә^{n+1}) вҠ—_A A_О» = (рқ”Ә^n / рқ”Ә^{n+1}) вҠ—_{A/рқ”Ә} (A_О» / рқ”Ә A_О»),
```

and since `A/рқ”Ә вҶ’ A_О» / рқ”Ә A_О» = A_О» / рқ”Ә_О»` is bijective, the homomorphism `рқ”Ә^n / рқ”Ә^{n+1} вҶ’ рқ”Ә_О»^n / рқ”Ә_О»^{n+1}` is also
bijective; the conclusion follows therefore from `(Bourbaki, Alg. comm., chap. III, В§ 2, nВ° 8, cor. 3 of th. 1)`.

Finally, if `A` is Henselian, it follows from the remark preceding `(18.6.3)` that the homomorphisms `A вҶ’ A_О»` are
bijective, which proves (vi) by the definition of `^h A`.

**(18.6.7)** Now let `A` be a semi-local ring, `рқ”Ә_i (1 в©Ҫ i в©Ҫ r)` its maximal ideals. One calls the **Henselization** of
`A` and one still denotes by `^h A` the product ring `вҲҸ ^h(A_{рқ”Ә_i})` of the Henselizations of the local rings `A_{рқ”Ә_i}`.
It is a faithfully flat `A`-module and a semi-local `A`-algebra whose maximal ideals are the `рқ”Ә_i В· ^h A` by virtue of
`(18.6.6, (iii))`; moreover, if `рқ”Ҝ = вӢӮ рқ”Ә_i` is the radical of `A`, it follows from what precedes that `рқ”Ҝ В· ^h A`

<!-- original page 139 -->

is the radical of `^h A` and that the canonical map `A / рқ”Ҝ вҶ’ ^h A / рқ”Ҝ В· ^h A` is bijective. As the separated completion
`ГӮ` of `A` for the `рқ”Ҝ`-preadic topology is the product of the separated completions `ГӮ_{рқ”Ә_i}`
`(Bourbaki, Alg. comm., chap. III, В§ 2, nВ° 13, prop. 18)`, the canonical homomorphism `ГӮ вҶ’ (^h A)^вҲ§` is bijective by
`(18.6.6, (iv))`, and it is clear by `(18.6.6, (v))` that in order for `^h A` to be Noetherian it is necessary and
sufficient that `A` be so.

To obtain the analogue of the universal property `(18.6.6, (ii))`, let us agree, when `A` and `B` are two semi-local
rings of radicals `рқ”Ҝ`, `рқ”°` respectively, to call a **semi-local homomorphism** from `A` to `B` any homomorphism `ПҶ` such
that `ПҶ(рқ”Ҝ) вҠӮ рқ”°`. In the particular case where `B` is a product of local rings `B_j (1 в©Ҫ j в©Ҫ n)`, the datum of such a
homomorphism amounts to that of its projections `ПҶ_j : A вҶ’ B_j`, which are homomorphisms subject only to the condition
that `ПҶ_j(рқ”Ҝ) вҠӮ рқ”«_j`, where `рқ”«_j` is the maximal ideal of `B_j`. Furthermore, if `рқ”Ә_i (1 в©Ҫ i в©Ҫ m)` are the maximal ideals
of `A`, the prime ideal `ПҶ_j^{вҲ’1}(рқ”«_j)` must contain one of the `рқ”Ә_i` since it contains their intersection `рқ”Ҝ`, hence it
equals one of the `рқ”Ә_i` and `ПҶ_j` factors as `A вҶ’ A_{рқ”Ә_i} вҶ’^{ПҶ'_j} B_j`, where `ПҶ'_j` is a local homomorphism. If
`Hom.sloc(A, B)` denotes the set of semi-local homomorphisms from `A` to `B`, one can thus identify this set with
`вҲҸ_j (вӢғ_i Hom.loc(A_{рқ”Ә_i}, B_j))` in the case considered; as a Henselian semi-local ring is a direct product of
Henselian local rings, one sees that the universal property `(18.6.6, (ii))` is still valid for a semi-local ring `A`,
on replacing local homomorphisms by semi-local homomorphisms.

**Proposition (18.6.8).**

<!-- label: IV.18.6.8 -->

*Let `A` be a semi-local ring, `B` a semi-local `A`-algebra that is integral over `A`. Then `B вҠ—_A (^h A)` is a
semi-local `B`-algebra isomorphic to `^h B`.*

Since `B вҠ—_A (^h A)` is integral over `^h A`, each of its maximal ideals lies over one of the maximal ideals of `^h A`,
hence over a maximal ideal of `A`, and since `B` is integral over `A`, the prime ideals of `B` lying over a maximal
ideal of `A` are maximal ideals of `B`, so that finally a maximal ideal of `B вҠ—_A (^h A)` has as projections in
`Spec(^h A)` and `Spec(B)` maximal ideals; taking into account `(18.6.6, (iii))` and `(I, 3.4.9)`, one concludes that
the ring `B вҠ—_A (^h A)` is semi-local. Moreover, for every Henselian local ring `C`, `Hom.sloc(B вҠ—_A (^h A), C)` is in
bijective correspondence with the set of pairs `(ПҶ, ПҲ)` of semi-local homomorphisms `ПҶ : B вҶ’ C`, `ПҲ : ^h A вҶ’ C` such
that the composites `A вҶ’ B вҶ’^ПҶ C`, `A вҶ’ ^h A вҶ’^ПҲ C` are equal. But by virtue of the bijective correspondence between
`Hom.sloc(A, C)` and `Hom.sloc(^h A, C)`, one sees that for every `ПҶ вҲҲ Hom.sloc(B, C)` there exists one and only one `ПҲ`
having the previous property, hence the map `Hom.sloc(B вҠ—_A (^h A), C) вҶ’ Hom.sloc(B, C)` is bijective, which proves the
proposition by virtue of the uniqueness of the solution of a universal problem.

**Theorem (18.6.9).**

<!-- label: IV.18.6.9 -->

*Let `A` be a semi-local ring.*

*(i) In order for `^h A` to be reduced (resp. normal), it is necessary and sufficient that `A` be so.*

*(ii) Suppose `A` Noetherian. Then, for every prime ideal `рқ”ӯ` of `A`, the ring `(^h A)_рқ”ӯ / рқ”ӯ В· (^h A)_рқ”ӯ` is a direct
composite of a finite number of separable algebraic extensions of `k(рқ”ӯ)` (which implies that the fibres of the canonical
morphism `Spec(^h A) вҶ’ Spec(A)` are geometrically regular).*

<!-- original page 140 -->

(i) Since `^h A` is a faithfully flat `A`-module, it follows from `(2.1.13)` that if `^h A` is reduced (resp. normal),
the same holds for `A`. To prove the converse, one may restrict to the case where the ring `A` is local, so that with
the notations of `(18.6.4)`, one has `^h A = lim_вҶ’ A_О»`. Now, it follows from the definition of the `A_О»` and from
`(17.5.7)` that if `A` is reduced (resp. integral and integrally closed), the same holds for the `A_О»`; moreover, the
homomorphisms `A_Оұ вҶ’ A_ОІ` for `Оұ в©Ҫ ОІ` are injective by virtue of `(0_I, 6.5.1)` since `A_ОІ` is a faithfully flat
`A_Оұ`-module; hence the morphisms `Spec(A_ОІ) вҶ’ Spec(A_Оұ)` are dominant, and one concludes from `(5.13.2)` (resp.
`(5.13.4)`) that `^h A` is reduced (resp. integral and integrally closed).

(ii) One may restrict to the case where `A` is local. By virtue of the fact that the functor `lim_вҶ’` commutes with
tensor products, the fibre of the morphism `Spec(^h A) вҶ’ Spec(A)` at a point `x` is the inductive limit of the fibres of
the morphisms `Spec(A_О») вҶ’ Spec(A)` at this point. Since `^h A` is Noetherian, one sees, taking into account `(17.6.2)`,
that one is reduced to proving the following lemma:

**Lemma (18.6.9.1).**

<!-- label: IV.18.6.9.1 -->

*Let `(B_Оұ)` be an inductive system of Artinian rings, `B = lim_вҶ’ B_Оұ` its inductive limit. If `B` is Noetherian, then
`B` is Artinian; if moreover, for `Оұ в©Ҫ ОІ`, the homomorphisms `ПҶ_{ОІОұ} : B_Оұ вҶ’ B_ОІ` are injective, then there exists `О»`
such that, for `Оұ в©ҫ О»`, the number of local components `B_{Оұi}` of `B_Оұ` is constant, `ПҶ_{ОІОұ}(B_{Оұi}) вҠӮ B_{ОІi}` for
every `i`, and the `B_i = lim_вҶ’ B_{Оұi}` are the local components of `B`.*

In effect, let `Y_Оұ = Spec(B_Оұ)`, `Y = Spec(B)`, which as a topological space is equal to `lim_вҶҗ Y_Оұ` `(8.2.10)`. The
spaces `Y_Оұ` are finite and discrete; moreover, if the `ПҶ_{ОІОұ}` are injective, the canonical morphisms `Y_ОІ вҶ’ Y_Оұ` are
dominant, hence surjective. The lemma will therefore result from the following purely topological lemma:

**Lemma (18.6.9.2).**

<!-- label: IV.18.6.9.2 -->

*Let `(Y_Оұ, ПҲ_{ОұОІ})` be a projective system of finite discrete topological spaces. If `Y = lim_вҶҗ Y_Оұ` is Noetherian, `Y`
is finite and discrete. If moreover the `ПҲ_{ОұОІ}` are surjective, there exists `О»` such that for `Оұ в©ҫ О»`, the number of
elements of `Y_Оұ` is constant and equal to the number of elements of `Y`.*

In effect, `Y` being compact and Noetherian, every part of `Y` is compact, hence closed, which implies that `Y` is
discrete, hence finite since it is compact. If moreover the `ПҲ_{ОұОІ}` are surjective, the same holds for `ПҲ_Оұ : Y вҶ’ Y_Оұ`,
hence `Card(Y) в©Ҫ Card(Y_Оұ)`, and as `Card(Y_Оұ)` is an increasing function of `Оұ`, there exists `О»` such that for
`Оұ в©ҫ О»`, `Card(Y_Оұ) = Card(Y_О»)`; the `ПҲ_{ОұОІ}` are then bijective for `Оұ в©ҫ О»` and one has therefore
`Card(Y) = Card(Y_О»)`.

**Corollary (18.6.10).**

<!-- label: IV.18.6.10 -->

*Let `A` be a Noetherian local ring. In order for `^h A` to possess one of the following properties:*

*a) being a Cohen-Macaulay ring `(0, 16.5.3)`;*

*b) satisfying property `(S_n)` `(5.7.3)`;*

*c) being regular;*

*d) satisfying property `(R_n)` `(5.8.2)`;*

*it is necessary and sufficient that `A` possess this same property.*

<!-- original page 141 -->

This follows immediately from the fact that the fibres of the morphism `Spec(^h A) вҶ’ Spec(A)` are geometrically regular
`(18.6.9)` and from `(6.4.1)`, `(6.5.1)` and `(6.5.3)`.

**Corollary (18.6.11).**

<!-- label: IV.18.6.11 -->

*Let `A` be a Noetherian semi-local ring. In order for a prime ideal `рқ”ӯ` of `^h A` to belong to `Ass(^h A)`, it is
necessary and sufficient that `рқ”ӯ вҲ© A` belong to `Ass(A)`.*

Taking into account the description of the fibres of the morphism `Spec(^h A) вҶ’ Spec(A)`, this follows immediately from
`(3.3.1)`.

**Proposition (18.6.12).**

<!-- label: IV.18.6.12 -->

*Let `A` be a local ring; the following properties are equivalent:*

*a) `A` is unibranch `(0, 23.2.1)` (resp. reduced and unibranch).*

*b) For every strictly essentially Г©tale local `A`-algebra `A'`, `Spec(A')` is irreducible (resp. integral).*

*c) `Spec(^h A)` is irreducible (resp. integral).*

Let us first note that `^h(A_{red}) = (^h A)_{red}`, for `^h(A_{red}) = A_{red} вҠ—_A (^h A)` `(18.6.8)`, and since
`^h(A_{red})` is reduced `(18.6.9)`, it equals `(^h A)_{red}`. This permits us, in the proof, to consider only the case
where `A` is reduced, so that `A'` is also reduced `(17.5.7)` and `^h A` is also reduced `(18.6.9)`.

With the notations of `(18.6.4)`, condition b) signifies that all the `A_О»` are integral; one concludes that
`^h A = lim_вҶ’ A_О»` is integral `(5.13.3)`, so b) entails c).

It is clear that if `^h A` is integral, the same holds for the `A_О» вҠӮ ^h A`, so c) entails b). Let us show that c)
entails a). Note first that `A вҠӮ ^h A` is integral; let `K` and `L` be the fields of fractions of `A` and `^h A`
respectively. It suffices to see that for every finite `A`-algebra `B вҠӮ K`, `B` is a local ring. Now `B` is a semi-local
ring, whose Henselization is therefore `B вҠ—_A (^h A)` `(18.6.8)`. By flatness, `B вҠ—_A (^h A)` identifies with a subring
of `K вҠ—_A (^h A)` and the latter with a subring of `L`, so `^h B` is integral. But since `^h B` is a Henselian
semi-local ring, it is a direct composite of local rings `(18.5.9)`, hence can be integral only if it is local, which
entails that `B` is local.

Let us finally prove that a) implies c). Let `C` be the integral closure of the integral ring `A`. Since `C` is a local
ring by hypothesis, `C вҠ—_A (^h A)` is the Henselization of `C` `(18.6.8)`, hence is integral and integrally closed
`(18.6.9)`. Since `A` is a subring of `C`, `^h A` identifies with a subring of `^h C` by flatness, so it too is
integral, which completes the proof.

**Corollary (18.6.13).**

<!-- label: IV.18.6.13 -->

*Let `A` be a Henselian local ring. Then, in order for `A` to be unibranch, it is necessary and sufficient that `A` be
integral.*

**Proposition (18.6.14).**

<!-- label: IV.18.6.14 -->

*(i) Every filtered inductive limit of Henselian local rings (where the transition homomorphisms are local) is a
Henselian local ring.*

*(ii) The functor `A вҶҰ ^h A` on the category of local rings (where the morphisms are the local homomorphisms) commutes
with filtered inductive limits.*

*(iii) Every Henselian local ring `A` is the inductive limit of a filtered inductive system of Henselian and Noetherian
local rings `A_О»` (the transition homomorphisms `A_О» вҶ’ A_Ој` being local).*

(i) Let `(A_О»)` be a filtered inductive system of Henselian local rings, where the transition homomorphisms are local.
Let us show that `A' = lim_вҶ’ A_О»`, which is local `(0_III, 10.3.1.3)`, is Henselian. Let `C` be an Г©tale `A'`-algebra,
`рқ”«` a prime ideal

<!-- original page 142 -->

of `C` lying over the maximal ideal `рқ”Ә'` of `A'`, such that `C_рқ”«` is strictly essentially Г©tale over `A'` `(18.6.1)`, in
other words such that `k(рқ”Ә') вҶ’ k(рқ”«)` is an isomorphism. By virtue of `(8.8.2, (ii))` and `(17.7.8)`, there exist an
index `О»` and an Г©tale `A_О»`-algebra `C_О»` such that `C = C_О» вҠ—_{A_О»} A'` up to isomorphism; moreover, if `рқ”«_О»` is the
inverse image of `рқ”«` in `C_О»`, and `рқ”Ә_О»` the maximal ideal of `A_О»`, one may, by virtue of `(8.8.2.4)` and the
transitivity of fibres `(I, 3.6.4)`, suppose that `(C_О»)_{рқ”«_О»}` is strictly essentially Г©tale over `A_О»`; since `A_О»` is
Henselian, `(C_О»)_{рқ”«_О»}` is necessarily isomorphic to `A_О»` `(18.5.11, b)`; there is consequently a neighbourhood of
`рқ”«_О»` in `Spec(C_О»)` isomorphic to `Spec(A_О»)` `(I, 6.5.4)`; one concludes that there is a neighbourhood of `рқ”«` in
`Spec(C)` isomorphic to `Spec(A')`, hence `C_рқ”«` is isomorphic to `A'`, which proves that `A'` is Henselian `(18.6.2)`
and completes the proof.

(ii) Suppose that `B = lim_вҶ’ B_О»`, where the `B_О»` are local rings, the transition homomorphisms `B_О» вҶ’ B_Ој (О» в©Ҫ Ој)`
being local. Set `A_О» = ^h B_О»`; the `A_О»` are Henselian local rings `(18.6.6, (vi))`, and by virtue of `(18.6.6, (ii))`
the transition homomorphisms `B_О» вҶ’ B_Ој` determine in a unique way local homomorphisms `A_О» вҶ’ A_Ој`, so that `(A_О»)` is
an inductive system. Everything reduces to seeing that `A' = lim_вҶ’ A_О»` is canonically isomorphic to `A = ^h B`. By
virtue of `(18.6.6, (ii))` and the definition of inductive limits, one has, for every Henselian local ring `E`,

```text
  Hom.loc(A', E) = lim_вҶҗ Hom.loc(A_О», E) = lim_вҶҗ Hom.loc(B_О», E) = Hom.loc(B, E).
```

But since `A'` is Henselian by (i), this proves our assertion.

(iii) The ring `A` is a filtered inductive limit of its Noetherian local subrings `B_О»`, the transition homomorphisms
being local `(5.13.3, (iii))`. Since the `^h B_О»` are Henselian and Noetherian local rings `(18.6.6, (v))` and
`A = ^h A` `(18.6.6, (vi))`, it suffices to apply (ii) to the inductive system `(B_О»)`.

**Corollary (18.6.15).**

<!-- label: IV.18.6.15 -->

*Let `A` be a Henselian local ring, `X` an `A`-prescheme of finite presentation over `A`. There then exist a Henselian
Noetherian local ring `A_0`, a local homomorphism `A_0 вҶ’ A`, a prescheme `X_0` of finite type over `A_0`, and an
`A`-isomorphism `X_0 вҠ—_{A_0} A вҘІ X`.*

This results from `(18.6.14)` and `(8.8.2, (ii))`.

### 18.7. Henselization and excellent rings

**(18.7.1)** We shall denote in this nВ° by `P(Z, k)` a property of the form considered in `(7.3.1)`, where we suppose in
addition that the property `Q(A, k)` satisfies the following condition:

For every separable algebraic extension `k'` of `k`, and every Noetherian local `k'`-algebra `A`, the property `Q(A, k)`
is equivalent to `Q(A, k')`.

It is immediate that all the properties `P` considered in `(7.3.8)` satisfy the preceding condition, taking into account
that if `K` is a finite extension of `k`, `k' вҠ—_k K` is a direct composite of separable algebraic extensions of `K`.

<!-- original page 143 -->

**Proposition (18.7.2).**

<!-- label: IV.18.7.2 -->

*Let `A` be a Noetherian local ring. In order for `^h A` to be a `P`-ring `(7.3.13)`, it is necessary and sufficient
that `A` be so.*

In effect, by virtue of `(18.6.6, (iv))`, the completion `ГӮ` of `A` is also the completion of `^h A`, and one has
therefore `A вҠӮ ^h A вҠӮ ГӮ`. According to `(18.6.9)`, for every `x вҲҲ Spec(A)`, the fibre at `x` of the morphism
`Spec(^h A) вҶ’ Spec(A)` is discrete and finite, and at each of the points `y_i` of this fibre, `k(y_i)` is a separable
algebraic extension of `k(x)`. The formal fibre of `A` at the point `x` is therefore a prescheme that is the sum of the
formal fibres of `^h A` at the points `y_i`. The conclusion then follows from the hypothesis made on `P` in `(18.7.1)`.

**Corollary (18.7.3).**

<!-- label: IV.18.7.3 -->

*Let `A` be a Noetherian local ring. In order for `^h A` to be universally Japanese, it is necessary and sufficient that
`A` be so.*

In effect, for a Noetherian local ring `B`, it amounts to the same thing to say that `B` is universally Japanese, or
that the formal fibres of `B` are geometrically reduced `(7.6.4 and 7.7.1)`; the conclusion follows therefore from
`(18.7.2)`.

**Corollary (18.7.4).**

<!-- label: IV.18.7.4 -->

*Let `A` be a Noetherian local ring. In order for the formal fibres of `^h A` to be geometrically regular, it is
necessary and sufficient that those of `A` be so.*

This is a particular case of `(18.7.2)`.

**Proposition (18.7.5).**

<!-- label: IV.18.7.5 -->

*Let `A` be a Noetherian local ring. If `A` is universally catenary `(5.6.2)` (resp. formally catenary `(7.1.9)`, resp.
strictly formally catenary `(7.2.6)`), the same holds for `^h A`.*

With the notations of `(18.6.4)`, if `A` is universally catenary, the same holds for the `A_О»`, which are essentially of
finite type `A`-algebras `(5.6.3)`. To prove that in this case `^h A` is universally catenary, it will therefore suffice
to establish the following lemma:

**Lemma (18.7.5.1).**

<!-- label: IV.18.7.5.1 -->

*Let `(B_Оұ, ПҶ_{ОІОұ})` be an inductive system of Noetherian rings and suppose that, for `Оұ в©Ҫ ОІ`, `ПҶ_{ОІОұ}` makes `B_ОІ` a
faithfully flat `B_Оұ`-module and that `B = lim_вҶ’ B_Оұ` is Noetherian. Then, if the `B_Оұ` are catenary (resp. universally
catenary), the same holds for `B`.*

To say that `B` is universally catenary amounts to saying that `B[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n]` is catenary for every `n` `(5.6.2)`, and
it is immediate that the inductive system `(B_Оұ[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n])` satisfies the same conditions as `(B_Оұ)`; it suffices
therefore to prove that if the `B_Оұ` are catenary, the same holds for `B`. If `рқ”ӯ_0 вҠғ рқ”ӯ_1 вҠғ вӢҜ вҠғ рқ”ӯ_n` is a saturated chain
of prime ideals of `B`, the inverse images `рқ”ӯ_{0Оұ} вҠғ рқ”ӯ_{1Оұ} вҠғ вӢҜ вҠғ рқ”ӯ_{nОұ}` of these ideals in `B_Оұ` form a chain of prime
ideals, and it suffices to show that for `Оұ` sufficiently large, this chain is saturated. Now, each `рқ”ӯ_i` is an ideal of
finite type, hence there exists `О»` such that, for `Оұ в©ҫ О»`, one has `рқ”ӯ_{iОұ} = рқ”ӯ_{iОұ+1}`. One has therefore
`1 = codim(V(рқ”ӯ_i), V(рқ”ӯ_{i+1})) = codim(V(рқ”ӯ_{iОұ}), V(рқ”ӯ_{i+1, Оұ}))` since `B` is a flat `B_Оұ`-module (`(6.1.4)` and
`(0_I, 6.2.3)`), which completes the proof of the lemma.

Suppose now `A` formally catenary. Let `рқ”ӯ` be a prime ideal of `^h A`, `рқ”®` its inverse image in `A`, so that
`рқ”® В· ^h A вҠӮ рқ”ӯ`, and consequently `^h A / рқ”ӯ` is a quotient ring of `^h A / рқ”® В· ^h A`. It suffices therefore to prove that
`^h A / рқ”® В· ^h A` is formally catenary for every prime ideal `рқ”®` of `A` `(7.1.9)`, and since `^h A / рқ”® В· ^h A = ^h(A/рқ”®)`
by `(18.6.8)`, it suffices `(7.1.11)` to see that if `A` is integral and formally catenary, `^h A` is formally
equidimensional. But since the completion of `^h A` is equal to `ГӮ`, this follows from the hypothesis that `A` is
formally catenary.

<!-- original page 144 -->

Suppose finally `A` strictly formally catenary; then we have just seen that `^h A` is formally catenary, and it remains
to prove that the fibres of the morphism `Spec(ГӮ) вҶ’ Spec(^h A)` satisfy property `(S_1)` `(7.2.5, b)`. But this follows
from the hypothesis on `A` and from `(18.7.2)` applied to the case where `P(Z, k)` is the property `(S_1)` for `Z`.

**Corollary (18.7.6).**

<!-- label: IV.18.7.6 -->

*If a Noetherian local ring `A` is excellent `(7.8.2)`, the same holds for `^h A`.*

**Remark (18.7.7).** вҖ” It can happen that `^h A` is an excellent local ring without `A` being universally catenary (nor
consequently excellent). To see this, let us take up again the example of the ring `A` of `(5.6.11)`, with the same
notations. The ring `E` constructed in `(5.6.11)` is excellent when `k_0` is of characteristic `0`
`(7.8.3, (ii) and (iii))`; consider two rings `E_1`, `E_2` isomorphic to `E`, and "glue" `Spec(E_1)` and `Spec(E_2)` so
that if `рқ”Ә_i` and `рқ”Ә'_i` are the maximal ideals of `E_i (i = 1, 2)` corresponding to `рқ”Ә` and `рқ”Ә'`, the point `рқ”Ә_1` is
"glued" to `рқ”Ә_2` and the point `рқ”Ә'_1` to `рқ”Ә'_2`; in precise terms, if `Оө_i` and `Оө'_i` are the canonical homomorphisms
of `E_i` onto `k(рқ”Ә_i)` and `k(рқ”Ә'_i) (i = 1, 2)`, the scheme obtained is `Spec(R)`, where `R` is the subring of
`E_1 Г— E_2` consisting of pairs `(x_1, x_2)` such that `Оө_2(x_2) = Оө_1(x_1)` and `Оө'_1(x_1) = Оө'_2(x_2)`. One verifies
easily (for example with the help of `(17.6.3)`) that `R` is a finite Г©tale `C`-algebra, and that there are two maximal
ideals `рқ”Ҝ_1`, `рқ”Ҝ_2` of `R` lying over the maximal ideal `рқ”«` of `C`, the completions of `R_{рқ”Ҝ_1}` and `R_{рқ”Ҝ_2}` being
canonically isomorphic to that of `A = C_рқ”«`; `R_{рқ”Ҝ_1}` is therefore a strictly essentially Г©tale `A`-algebra, and
consequently its Henselization is equal to `^h A`. Moreover, one has seen `(7.8.4, (ii))` that the formal fibres of `A`
are geometrically regular, hence the same holds for those of `^h A` `(18.7.2)`. Finally, the ring `R` is universally
catenary, for its quotients by its two minimal prime ideals are isomorphic to `E`, whence the conclusion by
`(5.6.3, (iii))`. The ring `R_{рқ”Ҝ_1}` is therefore excellent, and consequently the same holds for `^h A` `(18.7.6)`,
whereas `A` is not universally catenary.

### 18.8. Strictly local rings and strict Henselization

**Proposition (18.8.1).**

<!-- label: IV.18.8.1 -->

*Let `A` be a local ring. The following conditions are equivalent:*

*a) `A` is a Henselian ring and its residue field `k` is separably closed.*

*b) `A` is a Henselian ring and every Г©tale cover of `S = Spec(A)` is trivial.*

*c) For every Г©tale morphism `f : X вҶ’ S` and every point `x вҲҲ X` such that `f(x)` is the closed point `s` of `S`, there
exists an `S`-section `u : S вҶ’ X` of `X` such that `u(s) = x`.*

The hypothesis c) implies that for every Г©tale morphism `f : X вҶ’ S`, the residue fields at the points of `f^{вҲ’1}(s)` are
all isomorphic to `k`, and moreover that condition b) of `(18.5.11)` is satisfied. Hence `A` is Henselian, and the fact
that every Г©tale cover of `S` is trivial follows from `(18.2.10, (ii))`; so c) implies b). As the Г©tale covers of
`Spec(k)` are trivial if and only if `k` is separably closed, b) implies a) by virtue of `(18.5.11, b)`. Finally, it
also follows from `(18.5.11, b)` that a) implies c).

**Definition (18.8.2).**

<!-- label: IV.18.8.2 -->

*One says that a local ring is a **strictly local ring** if it satisfies the equivalent conditions of `(18.8.1)`. One
calls a **strictly local scheme** a scheme isomorphic to the spectrum of a strictly local ring.*

**Remark (18.8.3).** вҖ” The conditions of `(18.8.1)` are also equivalent to the following:

*d) For every morphism `f : X вҶ’ S` locally of finite type and every point `x вҲҲ X` such that `f(x)` is the closed point
`s` of `S` and that `рқ’Ә_{X, x} / рқ”Ә_s В· рқ’Ә_{X, x}` is a finite separable extension of `k(s) = k`, there exists an open
neighbourhood `U` of `x` in `X` such that `f | U` is a closed immersion.*

<!-- original page 145 -->

(One will note that the hypothesis of d) is satisfied if `f` is formally unramified at the point `x` `(17.4.1.2)`.)

We leave the proof to the reader, it being substantially the same as that of `(18.5.18)`.

**Lemma (18.8.4).**

<!-- label: IV.18.8.4 -->

*Let `A`, `A'` be two local rings, `ПҶ : A вҶ’ A'` a local homomorphism making `A'` into an essentially Г©tale `A`-algebra
`(18.6.1)`. Then, for every strictly local ring `B`, every local homomorphism `ПҲ : A вҶ’ B`, and every `k(A)`-algebra
homomorphism `Оұ : k(A') вҶ’ k(B)`, there exist one and only one local homomorphism `ПҲ' : A' вҶ’ B` such that `ПҲ = ПҲ' вҲҳ ПҶ`
and that `Оұ` equals the homomorphism `ПҲМ„'` deduced from `ПҲ'` by passage to the quotients.*

With the notations of `(18.6.2)`, the homomorphism `Оұ` corresponds to a `k(y)`-morphism `Spec(k(y)) вҶ’ Spec(k(x'))`,
hence to a well-determined point `x'` in `X'` lying over `y`. The existence of the `Y`-section `f'` of `X'` such that
`f'(y) = x'` follows therefore from `(18.8.1, c)` since `f'` is Г©tale and `B` strictly local, and its uniqueness follows
from the fact that `f'` is separated and from `(17.4.9)`.

**Lemma (18.8.5).**

<!-- label: IV.18.8.5 -->

*Let `A` be a local ring, `A_1`, `A_2` two essentially Г©tale local `A`-algebras, `K` a field, extension of `k(A)`.*

*(i) For every `k(A)`-homomorphism `Оі : k(A_1) вҶ’ k(A_2)`, there exists at most one `A`-homomorphism (necessarily local)
`ПҲ : A_1 вҶ’ A_2` such that `Оі` is the homomorphism `ПҲМ„` deduced from `ПҲ` by passage to the quotients.*

*(ii) For every pair of local `A`-homomorphisms `ОІ_1 : A_1 вҶ’ K`, `ОІ_2 : A_2 вҶ’ K`, there exist an essentially Г©tale local
`A`-algebra `A_3`, two `A`-homomorphisms `ПҶ_1 : A_1 вҶ’ A_3`, `ПҶ_2 : A_2 вҶ’ A_3`, and an `A`-homomorphism `ОІ : A_3 вҶ’ K`
such that `ОІ_1 = ОІ вҲҳ ПҶ_1` and `ОІ_2 = ОІ вҲҳ ПҶ_2`.*

With the notations of `(18.6.3)`, the homomorphisms `ОІ_1`, `ОІ_2` in (ii) correspond to two `S`-morphisms
`Spec(K) вҶ’ X_1`, `Spec(K) вҶ’ X_2`, with respective images `x_1`, `x_2`; one deduces from them a well-determined
`S`-morphism `Spec(K) вҶ’ X_3` `(I, 3.2.1)` with image `x_3` lying over `x_1` and `x_2`; the `A`-algebra
`A_3 = рқ’Ә_{X_3, x_3}` and the homomorphism `A_3 вҶ’ K` corresponding to these data satisfy the conditions of (ii). On the
other hand, the datum of `Оі` in (i) corresponds to an `S`-morphism `Spec(k(x_2)) вҶ’ Spec(k(x_1))`, or again to a point
`x_3` of `X_3` lying over `x_2`; the uniqueness of `ПҲ` follows from the uniqueness of an `X_2`-section of `X_3` passing
through `x_3` `(17.4.9)`.

**(18.8.6)** Let `A` be a local ring, `рқ”Ә` its maximal ideal, `k` its residue field, `О©` a separable closure of `k`.
Consider the set `рқ”Ҳ` of essentially Г©tale `A`-algebras defined in `(18.6.1)`, and denote by `L` the set of local
`A`-homomorphisms `A' вҶ’ О©`, where `A'` ranges over `рқ”Ҳ`; one will note that such a homomorphism factors as
`О» : A' вҶ’^{Пү_О»} k(A') вҶ’ О©`, where `Пү_О» : k(A') вҶ’ О©` is an `A`-homomorphism (since `рқ”Ә A'` is the maximal ideal of `A'`);
conversely, the datum of such a homomorphism `Пү_О»` uniquely determines a homomorphism `О» вҲҲ L`. For every `О» вҲҲ L`, we
shall denote by `A_О»` the essentially Г©tale `A`-algebra belonging to `рқ”Ҳ` on which `О»` is defined. The set `L` is
preordered by the relation "there exists an `A`-homomorphism `ПҶ_{ОјО»} : A_О» вҶ’ A_Ој` such that `О» = ПҶ_{ОјО»}^* вҲҳ Ој`", and it
follows from `(18.8.5, (i))` that this homomorphism `ПҶ_{ОјО»}` is unique. Moreover, `L` is increasingly filtered for the
preceding preorder relation (which we still note `О» в©Ҫ Ој`), by virtue

<!-- original page 146 -->

of `(18.8.5, (ii))`. It is clear that `(A_О», ПҶ_{ОјО»})` is an inductive system of local `A`-algebras, the `ПҶ_{ОјО»}` being
local homomorphisms; moreover, it follows from `(17.3.5)` that for `О» в©Ҫ Ој`, `A_Ој` is an essentially Г©tale `A_О»`-algebra.
If `ПҶМ„_{ОјО»} : k(A_О») вҶ’ k(A_Ој)` is the `A`-homomorphism deduced from `ПҶ_{ОјО»}` by passage to the quotients,
`(k(A_О»), ПҶМ„_{ОјО»})` is an inductive system of separable algebraic extensions of `k`, and the `Пү_О» : k(A_О») вҶ’ О©` form an
inductive system of `k`-homomorphisms. Moreover, the inductive limit

```text
  (18.8.6.1)    Пү : lim_вҶ’ k(A_О») вҶ’ О©
```

is a `k`-isomorphism. It suffices in effect to prove that for every finite separable extension `k'` of `k`, there exists
an essentially Г©tale `A`-algebra `A'` such that `k'` is the residue field of `A'` and that the homomorphism `k вҶ’ k'` is
deduced from `A вҶ’ A'` by passage to the quotients. But this follows from `(18.1.1)` applied to Г©tale morphisms, taking
into account that `Spec(A)` is the only neighbourhood of its closed point.

Note now that if `рқ”Ә_О»` is the maximal ideal of `A_О»`, it follows from `(17.6.1)` that for `О» в©Ҫ Ој`, one has
`рқ”Ә_Ој = рқ”Ә_О» В· A_Ој` and that `A_Ој` is a flat `A_О»`-module. Hence it follows from `(0_III, 10.3.1.3)` that the ring
`lim_вҶ’ A_О»` is local, that the canonical homomorphism `w : A вҶ’ lim_вҶ’ A_О»` is local, and that one has a canonical
`k`-isomorphism

```text
  lim_вҶ’ k(A_О») вҘІ k(lim_вҶ’ A_О»);
```

identifying these two fields, one deduces a canonical `k`-isomorphism

```text
  (18.8.6.2)    Пү^{вҲ’1} : О© вҘІ k(lim_вҶ’ A_О»).
```

**Definition (18.8.7).**

<!-- label: IV.18.8.7 -->

*Let `A` be a local ring, `k = k(A)` its residue field, `i : k вҶ’ О©` a homomorphism of `k` into a separable closure `О©`
of `k`; one calls the **strict Henselization** of `A` relative to `i`, and one denotes by `^{hs} A_{(i)}` (or `^{hs} A`
when this leads to no confusion) the inductive limit of the inductive system `(A_О», ПҶ_{ОјО»})` defined in `(18.8.6)`.*

As one has a canonical `k`-isomorphism `Пү^{вҲ’1} : О© вҘІ k(^{hs} A_{(i)})`, it is canonically endowed with a structure of
`^{hs} A_{(i)}`-algebra by the local homomorphism

```text
  ^{hs} A_{(i)} вҶ’ k(^{hs} A_{(i)}) вҘІ О©.
```

As in `(18.6.5)` one sees that the definition given in `(18.8.7)` depends only in appearance on the choice of the set
`рқ”Ҳ`; we shall see further below `(18.8.8, (i) and (ii))` that `^{hs} A_{(i)}` is an object representing a functor
entirely defined by the data of `A` and `i` `(0_III, 8.1.8)`, and is therefore defined as such up to unique isomorphism.

**Proposition (18.8.8).**

<!-- label: IV.18.8.8 -->

*Let `A` be a local ring, `k` its residue field, `i : k вҶ’ О©` a homomorphism of `k` into a separable closure of `k`,
`^{hs} A_{(i)}` the strict Henselization of `A` corresponding to `i`.*

*(i) `^{hs} A_{(i)}` is a strictly local ring `(18.8.2)` and the structure homomorphism `w : A вҶ’ ^{hs} A_{(i)}` is
local.*

*(ii) For every local homomorphism `u : A вҶ’ B`, where `B` is a strictly local ring, and every `k`-homomorphism
`ПҶ : О© вҶ’ k(B)`, there exists one and only one `A`-homomorphism `v : ^{hs} A_{(i)} вҶ’ B` such that `ПҶ` factors as
`О© вҘІ k(^{hs} A_{(i)}) вҶ’^{vМ„} k(B)`, where `vМ„` is deduced from `v` by passage to the quotients.*

<!-- original page 147 -->

*(iii) `^{hs} A_{(i)}` is a faithfully flat `A`-module, and if `рқ”Ә` is the maximal ideal of `A`, `рқ”Ә В· ^{hs} A_{(i)}` is
the maximal ideal of `^{hs} A_{(i)}`, and `k(^{hs} A_{(i)})` is a separable closure of `k`.*

*(iv) In order for `^{hs} A_{(i)}` to be Noetherian, it is necessary and sufficient that `A` be so.*

*(v) If `A` is strictly local (so `О© = k`), one has `^{hs} A = A`.*

*(vi) If `i' : k вҶ’ О©'` is a second homomorphism of `k` into a separable closure of `k`, then for every `k`-isomorphism
`Пғ : О© вҘІ О©'`, the corresponding `A`-homomorphism (by (ii)) `v_Пғ : ^{hs} A_{(i)} вҶ’ ^{hs} A_{(i')}` is an isomorphism.*

We have already seen above that `^{hs} A_{(i)}` is a local ring and that `w` is a local homomorphism; the fact that
`^{hs} A_{(i)}` is Henselian (and consequently strictly local) is proved as in `(18.6.6)`. The assertions of (iii) also
follow from `(0_III, 10.3.1.3)`, as does the sufficiency of condition (iv); the necessity of this condition follows from
the fact that `^{hs} A_{(i)}` is a faithfully flat `A`-module `(0_I, 6.5.2)`.

To prove (ii), let us remark, with the notations of `(18.8.6)`, that for every `О» вҲҲ L`, there exists one and only one
local `A`-homomorphism `v_О» : A_О» вҶ’ B`, such that the composite `k(A_О») вҶ’^{Пү_О»} О© вҶ’^ПҶ k(B)` is deduced from `v_О»` by
passage to the quotients, by virtue of `(18.8.4)` and the hypothesis that `B` is strictly local. The uniqueness of `v_О»`
moreover entails that the `v_О»` form an inductive system, whence the existence of the homomorphism `v` satisfying the
conditions of (ii); its uniqueness follows from `(17.4.9)`. The uniqueness of `v` entails at once assertion (vi), by
considering the composites `v_Пғ вҲҳ v_{Пғ^{вҲ’1}}` and `v_{Пғ^{вҲ’1}} вҲҳ v_Пғ`. Finally, if `A` is strictly local, and `A' = B_рқ”«`
an essentially Г©tale local `A`-algebra, where `B` is an Г©tale `A`-algebra, it follows from `(18.8.1)` that there exists
a `Spec(A)`-section of `Spec(B)` taking the value `рқ”«` at the closed point of `Spec(A)`, hence one deduces from
`(17.4.1)` that the homomorphism `A вҶ’ A'` is bijective, which proves (v).

**(18.8.8.1)** Let `рқ’һ` be the category of strictly local rings, with the local homomorphisms as morphisms; for every
`B вҲҲ рқ’һ`, denote by `F(B)` the set of pairs `(u, ПҲ)` formed of a local homomorphism `u : A вҶ’ B` and an `A`-isomorphism
`ПҲ : О© вҘІ k(B)` such that the composite `k(A) = k вҶ’^i О© вҶ’^ПҲ k(B)` is deduced from `u` by passage to the quotients. One
can say that the object `^{hs} A_{(i)}` represents the covariant functor `F : рқ’һ вҶ’ Ens` `(0_III, 8.1.8)`.

One will note that by virtue of `(18.8.8, (vi))` the strict Henselizations `^{hs} A_{(i)}` are all `A`-isomorphic (for
the various `k`-homomorphisms `i` of `k` into separable closures of `k`), but for given `i` and `i'`, there are in
general infinitely many `A`-isomorphisms `^{hs} A_{(i)} вҘІ ^{hs} A_{(i')}`. In precise terms, the group of
`A`-automorphisms of `^{hs} A_{(i)}` is isomorphic to the Galois group of `О©` over `k`.

**(18.8.9)** Now let `A` be a semi-local ring, `рқ”Ә_j (1 в©Ҫ j в©Ҫ n)` its maximal ideals, and for each index `j`, consider a
homomorphism `i_j : k(A_{рқ”Ә_j}) вҶ’ О©_j` of `k(A_{рқ”Ә_j})` into a separable closure of this field. One calls the **strict
Henselization** of `A` relative to the `i_j`, and one denotes by `^{hs} A` (when this gives rise to no confusion), the
product `вҲҸ_j (^{hs}(A_{рқ”Ә_j}))` of the strict Henselizations of the local rings `A_{рқ”Ә_j}` relative to the homomorphisms
`i_j`.

<!-- original page 148 -->

It is therefore, by virtue of `(18.8.8)`, a faithfully flat `A`-module and a semi-local `A`-algebra whose maximal ideals
are the `рқ”Ә_j В· ^{hs} A` and the radical `рқ”Ҝ В· ^{hs} A` (if `рқ”Ҝ` designates the radical of `A`). Finally, the universal
property `(18.8.8, (ii))` subsists on replacing "local homomorphism" by "semi-local homomorphism" `(18.6.7)`, and on
replacing `О©` by `вҲҸ_j О©_j`.

**Proposition (18.8.10).**

<!-- label: IV.18.8.10 -->

*Let `A` be a semi-local ring, `B` a finite `A`-algebra. Let `рқ”«_i (1 в©Ҫ i в©Ҫ r)` be the maximal ideals of `B`. Then there
is, for each `j`, a maximal ideal `рқ”®_j` of `B вҠ—_A (^{hs} A)` lying over `рқ”«_j`, such that `^{hs} B` is isomorphic to the
direct composite of the local rings `(B вҠ—_A (^{hs} A))_{рқ”®_j} (1 в©Ҫ j в©Ҫ r)`.*

One may evidently restrict to the case where `A` is local, on replacing `A` by `A_{рқ”Ә_i}`, where `рқ”Ә_i` is the maximal
ideal of `A` inverse image of `рқ”«_i`. Set on the other hand `C = B_{рқ”«_i}`; by virtue of the definition of `^{hs} B`
`(18.8.1)`, everything reduces to seeing that `^{hs} C` is `C`-isomorphic to `(C вҠ—_A (^{hs} A))_рқ”®`, where `рқ”®` is one of
the maximal ideals of `C вҠ—_A (^{hs} A)`. Let `k` and `K` be the residue fields of `A` and `C`, `О©` that of `^{hs} A`,
which is by definition a separable closure of `k`; as `K` is a finite extension of `k`, one may suppose `K` and `О©`
contained in the same algebraic closure of `k`; it is then immediate that `K вҠ—_k О©` is a direct composite of a finite
number of fields, all isomorphic to the separable closure `K О©` of `K`. On the other hand, the ring `^{hs} A` being
Henselian, `C вҠ—_A (^{hs} A)` is a direct composite of the local rings `(C вҠ—_A (^{hs} A))_{рқ”®_j}`, where `рқ”®_j (1 в©Ҫ j)`
ranges over the maximal ideals of `C вҠ—_A (^{hs} A)`, and these local rings are Henselian `(18.5.10)` and have `K О©` for
residue field, hence are strictly local `(18.8.1)`. Set for brevity `C' = C вҠ—_A (^{hs} A)` and `C'_j = C'_{рқ”®_j}`, which
is therefore a quotient ring of `C'`; let `f : C вҶ’ C'`, `g : ^{hs} A вҶ’ C'`, `ПҶ_j : C' вҶ’ C'_j` be the canonical maps.

Let `v : C вҶ’ ^{hs} C` be the canonical homomorphism; there exists one and only one local homomorphism
`u : ^{hs} A вҶ’ ^{hs} C` which, by passage to the quotients, gives the canonical injection `О© вҶ’ K О©` and such that the
composite `A вҶ’ ^{hs} A вҶ’^u ^{hs} C` is equal to the composite `A вҶ’ C вҶ’^v ^{hs} C` `(18.8.8)`; hence there exists a
unique local homomorphism `w_0 : C' вҶ’ ^{hs} C` such that `w_0 вҲҳ g = u`, `w_0 вҲҳ f = v`, and since `^{hs} C` is a local
ring, this homomorphism factors as `C' вҶ’^{ПҶ_i} C'_i вҶ’^w ^{hs} C` for a well-determined index `i`, `w` being a local
homomorphism. On the other hand, the ring `C'_i` being strictly local, there exists a local homomorphism
`w' : ^{hs} C вҶ’ C'_i` which, by passage to the quotients, gives the identity automorphism of `K О©` and which is such
that `w' вҲҳ v = ПҶ_i вҲҳ f` `(18.8.8)`. One deduces first from this that `w вҲҳ w'` is an endomorphism of `^{hs} C` which, by
passage to the quotients, gives the identity automorphism of `K О©`, hence is

<!-- original page 149 -->

the identity `(18.8.8)`. On the other hand, one has `w' вҲҳ w вҲҳ ПҶ_i вҲҳ f = w' вҲҳ v = ПҶ_i вҲҳ f`, and
`w' вҲҳ w вҲҳ ПҶ_i вҲҳ g = w' вҲҳ u = ПҶ_i вҲҳ g`, whence `w' вҲҳ w вҲҳ ПҶ_i = ПҶ_i`, in other words `w' вҲҳ w` is the identity automorphism
of `C'_i`. Q.E.D.

**Remark (18.8.11).** вҖ” The proof of `(18.8.10)` uses the fact that `B` is integral over `A`, but uses the fact that `B`
is a finite `A`-algebra only to establish that `K вҠ—_k О©` is a direct composite of a finite number of fields. Now, this
last property is still satisfied when one supposes that `B` is a semi-local integral `A`-algebra whose maximal ideals
`рқ”«_i` have residue fields of finite separable degrees `[k(рқ”«_i) : k]_s`.

**Proposition (18.8.12).**

<!-- label: IV.18.8.12 -->

*Let `A` be a semi-local ring.*

*(i) In order for `^{hs} A` to be reduced (resp. normal), it is necessary and sufficient that `A` be so.*

*(ii) Suppose `A` Noetherian. Then, for every prime ideal `рқ”ӯ` of `A`, the ring `(^{hs} A)_рқ”ӯ / рқ”ӯ В· (^{hs} A)_рқ”ӯ` is a
direct composite of a finite number of separable algebraic extensions of `k(рқ”ӯ)` (which implies that the fibres of the
canonical morphism `Spec(^{hs} A) вҶ’ Spec(A)` are geometrically regular and are discrete spaces).*

**Corollary (18.8.13).**

<!-- label: IV.18.8.13 -->

*Let `A` be a Noetherian local ring. In order for `^{hs} A` to possess one of the following properties:*

*a) being a Cohen-Macaulay ring `(0, 16.5.3)`;*

*b) satisfying condition `(S_n)` `(5.7.3)`;*

*c) being regular;*

*d) satisfying condition `(R_n)` `(5.8.2)`;*

*it is necessary and sufficient that `A` possess this same property.*

**Corollary (18.8.14).**

<!-- label: IV.18.8.14 -->

*Let `A` be a Noetherian semi-local ring. In order for a prime ideal `рқ”ӯ` of `^{hs} A` to belong to `Ass(^{hs} A)`, it is
necessary and sufficient that `рқ”ӯ вҲ© A` belong to `Ass(A)`.*

The proofs are the same as those of `(18.6.9)`, `(18.6.10)` and `(18.6.11)` respectively.

**Proposition (18.8.15).**

<!-- label: IV.18.8.15 -->

*Let `A` be a local ring; the following properties are equivalent:*

*a) `A` is geometrically unibranch (resp. reduced and geometrically unibranch).*

*b) For every essentially Г©tale local `A`-algebra `A'`, `Spec(A')` is irreducible (resp. integral).*

*c) `Spec(^{hs} A)` is irreducible (resp. integral).*

One reduces as in `(18.6.12)` to the case where `A` is reduced, using the relation
`^{hs}(A_{red}) = (^{hs} A) вҠ—_A A_{red}` `(18.8.11)`, and the equivalence of b) and c) is proved as in `(18.6.12)`; the
same holds for the fact that a) implies c), taking into account `(18.8.11)` and the definition of a geometrically
unibranch integral local ring. Finally, to prove that c) implies a), let us keep the same notations as in `(18.6.12)`;
it is still a question of seeing that `^{hs} B` is integral. But, by `(18.8.10)`, `^{hs} B` is a localized ring of the
semi-local ring `B вҠ—_A (^{hs} A)`, which by flatness still identifies with a subring of the field `L`, hence is
integral; the same holds therefore for `^{hs} B`, which completes the proof.

**Corollary (18.8.16).**

<!-- label: IV.18.8.16 -->

*Let `A` be a Henselian local ring (resp. strictly local). In order for `A` to be unibranch (resp. geometrically
unibranch), it is necessary and sufficient that `Spec(A)` be irreducible.*

<!-- original page 150 -->

**Proposition (18.8.17).**

<!-- label: IV.18.8.17 -->

*Let `A` be a Noetherian local ring. If `A` is universally catenary, the same holds for `^{hs} A`.*

The proof is the same as that of `(18.7.5)`.

**Proposition (18.8.18).**

<!-- label: IV.18.8.18 -->

*(i) Every filtered inductive limit of strictly local rings (where the transition homomorphisms are local) is a strictly
local ring.*

*(ii) The functor `A вҶҰ ^{hs} A` on the category of local rings (where the morphisms are the local homomorphisms)
commutes with filtered inductive limits.*

*(iii) Every strictly local ring `A` is the inductive limit of a filtered inductive system of Noetherian strictly local
rings (the transition homomorphisms being local).*

The proofs are modelled on those of `(18.6.14)`.

### 18.9. Formal fibres of Henselian Noetherian rings

**Theorem (18.9.1).**

<!-- label: IV.18.9.1 -->

*Let `A` be a Henselian Noetherian local ring whose formal fibres are geometrically normal. Then the formal fibres of
`A` are geometrically integral (hence geometrically connected).*

The two assertions of the statement are in fact equivalent, a locally Noetherian connected and normal prescheme being
integral. As every finite integral `A`-algebra is a Henselian local ring `(18.5.9 and 18.5.10)`, it follows from
`(7.3.16.2)` that one is reduced to proving that if one supposes moreover `A` integral, then the fibre of the morphism
`Spec(ГӮ) вҶ’ Spec(A)` at the generic point of `Spec(A)` is integral, which follows from the

**Corollary (18.9.2).**

<!-- label: IV.18.9.2 -->

*Let `A` be a Henselian Noetherian local ring that is integral, whose formal fibres are geometrically normal. Then `ГӮ`
is integral.*

In effect, it follows from `(18.8.16)` that `A` is unibranch, so the theorem follows from the hypothesis made on the
formal fibres of `A` and from `(7.6.3)`.

**Corollary (18.9.3).**

<!-- label: IV.18.9.3 -->

*Under the hypotheses of `(18.9.2)`, the field of fractions `L` of `ГӮ` is a separable extension of the field of
fractions `K` of `A`, and `K` is algebraically closed in `L`.*

This follows from the fact that the fibre of the morphism `Spec(ГӮ) вҶ’ Spec(A)` at the generic point of `Spec(A)` is
geometrically integral and from `(4.3.2)` and `(4.3.5)`.

**Corollary (18.9.4).**

<!-- label: IV.18.9.4 -->

*Let `A` be a Henselian Noetherian local ring whose formal fibres are geometrically normal (for example a Henselian
Noetherian local ring that is excellent), and set `A' = ГӮ`. Let `X` be an `A`-prescheme, `X' = X вҠ—_A A'`, `g : X' вҶ’ X`
the canonical projection. Then the map `U вҶҰ g^{вҲ’1}(U)` is a bijection of the set of subsets that are at once open and
closed in `X` onto the set of subsets that are at once open and closed in `X'`.*

As `g` is a faithfully flat and quasi-compact morphism, one knows `(2.3.12)` that the topology of `X` is the quotient of
that of `X'` by the equivalence relation defined by `g`. Everything reduces therefore to seeing that an open and closed
subset `U'` of `X'` is saturated for this relation. Now, as the morphism `Spec(A') вҶ’ Spec(A)` has its fibres
geometrically connected `(18.9.1)`, the fibres of `g` are connected, whence at once our assertion.

In particular, if `X` is locally connected (which will be the case if `X` is locally Noetherian), then, for every
connected component `U` of `X` (which is open and closed

<!-- original page 151 -->

in `X`), `g^{вҲ’1}(U)` is connected `(Bourbaki, Top. gГ©n., chap. I, 3rd ed., В§ 11, nВ° 3, prop. 7)`. If one denotes by
`ПҖ_0(X)` the set of connected components of `X`, the map `ПҖ_0(X') вҶ’ ПҖ_0(X)` canonically deduced from `g` is therefore
bijective.

**Corollary (18.9.5).**

<!-- label: IV.18.9.5 -->

*Under the hypotheses of `(18.9.4)`, the functor*

```text
  (18.9.5.1)    Z вҶҰ Z вҠ—_A A'
```

*from the category of Г©tale preschemes over `X` to the category of Г©tale preschemes over `X'` is fully faithful.*

Let `Z_1`, `Z_2` be two Г©tale preschemes over `X`, and set `Z'_i = Z_i вҠ—_A A' (i = 1, 2)`; it is a question of proving
that every `X'`-morphism `Z'_1 вҶ’ Z'_2` arises, by base change, from a unique `X`-morphism `Z_1 вҶ’ Z_2`. Suppose first
that `Z_2` is separated over `X`; then, since `Hom_X(Z_1, Z_2)` identifies with `О“(Z_1 Г—_X Z_2 / Z_1)`, and
`Z_1 Г—_X Z_2` is Г©tale and separated over `Z_1`, `Hom_X(Z_1, Z_2)` identifies functorially, by virtue of `(17.9.3)`,
with the set of open and closed subsets `U` of `Z_1 Г—_X Z_2` such that the restriction to `U` of the projection
`p : Z_1 Г—_X Z_2 вҶ’ Z_1` is a surjective and radicial morphism. The assertion follows therefore in the case considered
from `(18.9.4)` and from the fact that `Z'_1 Г—_{X'} Z'_2 = (Z_1 Г—_X Z_2) вҠ—_A A'`.

Let us pass to the general case: it will suffice to prove that the graph `О“'` of an `X'`-morphism `Z'_1 вҶ’ Z'_2` which is
open `(17.9.3)` in `Z'_1 Г—_{X'} Z'_2` is of the form `О“ вҠ—_A A'`, where `О“` is induced on an open subset of
`Z = Z_1 Г—_X Z_2`. In effect, the restriction to `О“` of the projection `p : Z вҶ’ Z_1` is then an isomorphism, for by base
change `A вҶ’ A'` this restriction becomes the isomorphism restriction to `О“'` of the projection `p' : Z' вҶ’ Z'_1` (with
`Z' = Z вҠ—_A A'`), and it suffices to apply `(2.7.1, (viii))`; the conclusion then follows from the characterization of
graphs of morphisms `(I, 5.3)`.

If `q : Z' вҶ’ Z` is the canonical projection, to prove that `О“'` is of the form `q^{вҲ’1}(О“)`, where `О“` is open in `Z`, it
suffices, since `q` is a faithfully flat and quasi-compact morphism, to prove that there exists a set `U вҠӮ Z` such that
`О“' = q^{вҲ’1}(U)` `(2.3.12)`. Set `Z'' = Z' Г—_Z Z' = Z Г—_X X''`, where `X'' = X' Г—_X X'`, and let `r_1 : Z'' вҶ’ Z'`,
`r_2 : Z'' вҶ’ Z'` be the canonical projections. Applying `(4.5.19.1)`, it suffices to show that
`r_1^{вҲ’1}(О“') = r_2^{вҲ’1}(О“')`. But this is a property which is true if and only if it is so after each base change
`Spec(k(x)) вҶ’ X`, where `x` ranges over `X`. In other words, it suffices to prove the corollary when `X` is the spectrum
of a field, but since every Г©tale `X`-prescheme is then automatically separated over `X` `(17.6.2, c')`, one is reduced
to the case considered at the beginning of the proof.

**Remarks (18.9.6).** вҖ” (i) It is possible that, if the residue field of `A` is of characteristic `0`, the functor
`(18.9.5.1)` even induces an equivalence of the category of Г©tale covers of `X` and of the category of Г©tale covers of
`X'`. One can in any case prove this when `A` is excellent, using Hironaka's resolution of singularities (M. Artin). It
is plausible that the analogous statement is still true without restriction on the characteristic of the residue field,
provided one restricts to "principal Galois covers" whose group is of order prime to the residue characteristic (cf.
`[41]`).

<!-- original page 152 -->

(ii) One does not know whether the formal fibres of `A` are geometrically connected (let alone geometrically
irreducible) when `A` is an arbitrary Henselian local ring. It would suffice that, for every Noetherian Henselian
integral local ring `A`, `Spec(ГӮ)` be irreducible. One does not know whether this is always so.

(iii) One does not know whether, when `A` is an excellent local ring, its strict Henselization `^{hs} A` is excellent.
One can see that, to clarify this question, one may reduce to the case where `A = k[[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n]]`, `k` being a field
of characteristic `p > 0`. Taking into account `(18.8.17)`, the question is whether the formal fibres of `^{hs} A` are
geometrically regular. The answer is affirmative when `n = 1`, but is not known for `n = 2`. One can show that the
answer is affirmative whenever, for every scheme `Y_1` finite over `Y = Spec(A)`, one can resolve the singularities of
`Y_1` `(7.9.1)`.

The connectedness assertion made in `(18.9.1)` generalizes in the following way:

**Theorem (18.9.7).**

<!-- label: IV.18.9.7 -->

*Let `A`, `B` be two Noetherian local rings, `ПҒ : A вҶ’ B` a local homomorphism, `f : Spec(B) = X вҶ’ Spec(A) = Y` the
corresponding morphism. Suppose the following conditions verified:*

*(i) `f` is flat and all the fibres `X_y = f^{вҲ’1}(y) (y вҲҲ Y)` are geometrically reduced `(4.6.2)`.*

*(ii) Either the ring `A` is geometrically unibranch `(0, 23.2.1)`, or the ring `A` is unibranch `(0, 23.2.1)` and
`k(B)` is a primary extension `(4.3.1)` of `k(A)`.*

*Then, if `О·` is the generic point of `Y`, `X_О·` is connected, and for every closed subset `T` of `X` such that `f(T)`
is rare in `Y`, `X вҲ’ T` is connected.*

The two conclusions stated are in fact equivalent; indeed, the hypothesis that `f(T)` is rare entails that `f(T)` does
not contain `О·`; on the other hand, since `{О·}` is pro-constructible `(1.9.6)` and `f` is flat, `X_О·` is dense in `X`
`(2.3.10)`, and consequently if `X_О·` is connected, the same holds for `X вҲ’ T` which contains it. Conversely, when `U`
ranges over the set of affine open neighbourhoods of `О·` in `Y`, `X_О·` is the projective limit of the sub-preschemes
induced on the open sets `f^{вҲ’1}(U)` of `X` `(8.1.2, a)`; if one supposes that `X вҲ’ T` is connected for every closed
subset `T` of `X` such that `f(T)` is rare in `Y`, the `f^{вҲ’1}(U)` are connected, hence the same holds for `X_О·`
`(8.4.1)`.

Let us first show that one may restrict to the case where `A` is integral and `Y = Spec(A)` geometrically unibranch
`(6.15.1)` (which implies that `A` is geometrically unibranch, but is not equivalent to this condition `(6.15.2)`). It
is clear that one may first suppose `Y` reduced, by considering the morphism `X Г—_Y Y_{red} вҶ’ Y_{red}`, deduced from `f`
by base change, which is flat, and has the same fibres as `f`. One may therefore suppose `A` integral and unibranch; if
`K` is the field of fractions of `A`, there then exists a finite `A`-subalgebra `A''` of `K` such that, if `A'` is the
integral closure of `A`, the morphism `Spec(A') вҶ’ Spec(A'')` is radicial `(0, 23.2.5)`; one concludes `(6.15.5)` that
`Spec(A'')` is geometrically unibranch. As `A` is unibranch, `A'` is a local ring, hence the same holds for `A''`; let
us show that the ring `B'' = B вҠ—_A A''` is also a local ring. In effect, `B''` is a finite `B`-algebra, hence a
Noetherian semi-local ring;

<!-- original page 153 -->

if `k''` is the residue field of `A''`, the maximal ideals of `B''` are the points of `Spec(B'')` lying over the closed
point of `Spec(B)`, hence the points of `Spec(k(B) вҠ—_{k(A)} k'')` `(I, 3.4.9)`, since the closed point of `Spec(A'')` is
the only point lying over the closed point of `Spec(A)`. Now, when `A` is geometrically unibranch, `k''` is a radicial
extension of `k(A)`, hence `Spec(k(B) вҠ—_{k(A)} k'')` is radicial over `Spec(k(B))` and therefore comprises a single
point. When `A` is unibranch and `k(B)` is a primary extension of `k(A)`, `Spec(k(B) вҠ—_{k(A)} k'')` is irreducible
`(4.3.2)` and since it is a finite and discrete space `(I, 6.4.4)` it is again reduced to a point, which shows that in
both cases envisaged `B''` is local. If `Y'' = Spec(A'')`, `X'' = Spec(B'') = X Г—_Y Y''`, the morphism
`f'' = f_{(Y'')} : X'' вҶ’ Y''` is flat and has its fibres geometrically reduced; moreover, if `О·''` is the generic point
of `Y''`, `k(О·'') = k(О·) = K` by definition, hence the fibres `X_О·` and `X''_{О·''}` are isomorphic. It suffices
therefore to prove that `X''_{О·''}` is connected.

**Remark (18.9.7.1).** вҖ” When the ring `A` is Japanese, one may, in what precedes, take `A'' = A'` by definition
`(0, 23.1.1)`; one sees therefore that in this case one would even be reduced to proving the theorem when `A` is
integrally closed.

**(18.9.7.2)** Let us henceforth suppose that `Y` is integral and geometrically unibranch. Note that if `T` is a closed
subset of `X` such that `f(T)` is rare in `Y`, `T` contains no maximal point of `X` since `f` is flat `(2.3.4)`, hence
is rare in `X`; as `X` is a local scheme, hence connected, to prove that `X вҲ’ T` is connected, it suffices, by virtue of
`(15.5.6.1)`, to show that for every `x вҲҲ X` such that `f(x) вү  О·`, `Spec(рқ’Ә_{X, x}) вҲ’ {x}` is connected. Set `y = f(x)`,
`A_1 = рқ’Ә_{Y, y}`, `B_1 = рқ’Ә_{X, x}`, `Y_1 = Spec(A_1)`, `X_1 = Spec(B_1)`, `f_1 : X_1 вҶ’ Y_1` the morphism corresponding
to the local homomorphism `A_1 вҶ’ B_1` deduced from `ПҒ`; it is clear that `f_1` is flat, and it follows from `(4.6.1)`
that its fibres are geometrically reduced; moreover `A_1` is integral and geometrically unibranch `(6.15.1)` and
`dim(A_1) в©ҫ 1`. One is thus reduced to proving the

**Lemma (18.9.7.3).**

<!-- label: IV.18.9.7.3 -->

*Let `A`, `B` be two Noetherian local rings, `Y = Spec(A)`, `X = Spec(B)`, `ПҒ : A вҶ’ B` a local homomorphism, `f : X вҶ’ Y`
the corresponding morphism. Suppose the following conditions verified:*

*(i) `f` is flat and all the fibres `X_y (y вҲҲ Y)` are geometrically reduced.*

*(ii) `A` is integral, geometrically unibranch and `dim(A) в©ҫ 1`.*

*Then, if `b` is the closed point of `X`, `X вҲ’ {b}` is connected.*

Let us first note that by virtue of Hartshorne's theorem `(5.10.7)`, `X вҲ’ {b}` is connected if one has `prof(B) в©ҫ 2`.
Now one has `(6.3.1)`

```text
  (18.9.7.4)    prof(B) = prof(A) + prof(B вҠ—_A k)
```

on denoting by `k` the residue field of `A`. On the other hand, since `A` is integral and `dim(A) в©ҫ 1`, one has
`prof(A) в©ҫ 1`, hence `prof(B) в©ҫ 2` except when `prof(B вҠ—_A k) = 0`; moreover, `B вҠ—_A k` is reduced by (i), so the
relation `prof(B вҠ—_A k) = 0` signifies that `B вҠ—_A k` is a field `(0, 16.4.7)`. We shall henceforth suppose that this
last condition is verified. We shall begin by treating a case where the proof is very simple.

**A) Case where `A` is integrally closed.** Then, if `dim(A) в©ҫ 2`, one has `prof(A) в©ҫ 2` `(0, 16.5.1)`, hence
`prof(B) в©ҫ 2`. One therefore has only to consider the case where `dim(A) = 1` and where `B вҠ—_A k`

<!-- original page 154 -->

is a field; `A` is then a discrete valuation ring, hence regular, and since `B вҠ—_A k` is a field and `f` is flat, `B` is
regular `(0, 17.3.3)`; but moreover `(6.1.1.1)`, one has `dim(B) = dim(A) + dim(B вҠ—_A k) = dim(A) = 1`, hence `B` is
also a discrete valuation ring. But then `X вҲ’ {b}` is reduced to a single point, whence lemma `(18.9.7.3)` in this case.

One observes that this proves the statement of theorem `(18.9.7)` when one supposes moreover that, in this statement,
the ring `A` is Japanese, for by virtue of remark `(18.9.7.1)`, one is reduced to the case where `A` is integrally
closed, and then, in the reduction preceding `(18.9.7.3)`, the ring `A_1 = рқ’Ә_{Y, y}` is also integrally closed and one
may apply the result that has just been proved.

**B) Case where `dim(A) в©ҫ 2`.** The result of `(18.9.7.3)` will then follow from the two following lemmas:

**Lemma (18.9.7.5).**

<!-- label: IV.18.9.7.5 -->

*Let `A` be a Noetherian semi-local reduced ring, `A'` its integral closure in its total ring of fractions,
`X = Spec(A)`, `X' = Spec(A')`; let `S` be the set of closed points of `X` and `U = X вҲ’ S`. Suppose that for every point
`x' вҲҲ X'` lying over a point of `S`, one has `dim(рқ’Ә_{X', x'}) в©ҫ 2`; then the ring `A^{(1)} = О“(U, рқ’Ә_X)` is integral over
`A` and is an `A`-algebra isomorphic to a sub-algebra of `A'`.*
