`dim(A/рқ”®) = n` imply, by virtue of `(18.11.5.1)`, that `m вүҘ n`; one can therefore consider a family `(x_i)_{1 вүӨ i вүӨ m}`
of elements `x_i вҲү рқ”ӯ`, of which the first `n` form a system of parameters of `A`. Multiplying moreover the `x_i` by
invertible elements `u_i` of `A`, one can, thanks to `(18.11.5.2)`, suppose that the images of the `dx_i` (`1 вүӨ i вүӨ m`)
in `(О©_{A/k}^1)_рқ”ӯ` generate this `A_рқ”ӯ`-module, and the multiplication by the `u_i` has not altered the fact that the
`x_i` for `1 вүӨ i вүӨ n` form a system of parameters. Let us then consider the local `k`-homomorphism `u : B вҶ’ A` such that
`u(T_i) = x_i` for `1 вүӨ i вүӨ m` (Bourbaki, Alg. comm., chap. III, В§4, nВ° 5, prop. 6); since the `x_i` generate an ideal
of definition of `A`, it results from `(0_I, 7.4.4 and 7.4.3)` that `u` makes `A` into a finite `B`-algebra. One
therefore has `(18.11.3.5)` the exact sequence

```text
  (О©_{B/k}^1 вҠ—_B A) вҶ’^v О©_{A/k}^1 вҶ’ О©_{A/B}^1 вҶ’ 0.
```

But the `dx_i` are the canonical images by `v` of the elements `dT_i вҠ— 1` `(0, 20.5.2.6)`. If one localizes the
preceding exact sequence at `рқ”ӯ`, one sees therefore that `v_рқ”ӯ : (О©_{B/k}^1 вҠ—_B A)_рқ”ӯ вҶ’ (О©_{A/k}^1)_рқ”ӯ` is surjective, and
consequently one has `(О©_{A/B}^1)_рқ”ӯ = (О©_{A/B}^1)_рқ”Ҝ = 0` (where `рқ”Ҝ` is the inverse image of `рқ”ӯ` in `B`, cf.
`(16.4.15)`). By virtue of `(17.4.1)`, this implies property b) of `(18.11.5)`. Q.E.D.

**Remark (18.11.6).** вҖ” In the statement of `(18.11.5)`, one cannot suppress the hypothesis `рқ”ӯ вү  рқ”Ә`. Indeed, for every
local `k`-homomorphism `u : B вҶ’ A`, where `B = k[[T_1, вҖҰ, T_r]]` (`r` an arbitrary integer) making `A` into a finite
`B`-algebra, `рқ”Ә` is the only point of `Spec(A)` above the maximal ideal `рқ”«` of `B`; the morphism `Spec(A) вҶ’ Spec(B)`
cannot be unramified at `рқ”Ә` unless `A/рқ”« A` is a field, separable extension of `k` `(17.4.1)`, which implies that the
residue field `K` of `A` is a separable extension of `k`. If this condition is not satisfied, the conclusion of
`(18.11.5)` can never be verified for `рқ”ӯ = рқ”Ә`, whatever the integer `m`.

**Corollary (18.11.7).**

<!-- label: IV.18.11.7 -->

*Let `k` be a field, `A` a complete Noetherian local equidimensional `k`-algebra, whose residue field is a finite
extension of `k`, `рқ”ӯ` a prime ideal of `A`. Then the minimum number of generators of the `A_рқ”ӯ`-module `(О©_{A/k}^1)_рқ”ӯ` is
at least equal to `dim(A)`.*

It is a particular case of `(18.11.5.1)`.

More particularly:

<!-- original page 177 -->

**Corollary (18.11.8).**

<!-- label: IV.18.11.8 -->

*Let `k` be a field, `A` a complete Noetherian local integral `k`-algebra, whose residue field is a finite extension of
`k`. If `K` is the field of fractions of `A`, one has `rg_K((О©_{A/k}^1) вҠ—_A K) вүҘ dim(A)`.*

It suffices to set `рқ”ӯ = 0` in `(18.11.7)`.

**Corollary (18.11.9).**

<!-- label: IV.18.11.9 -->

*Let `k` be a field, `A` a complete Noetherian local `k`-algebra of dimension `n`, whose residue field is a finite
extension of `k`. Let `рқ”ӯ` be a prime ideal of `A` distinct from the maximal ideal, and containing a minimal prime ideal
`рқ”®` such that `dim(A/рқ”®) = n`. Suppose that the `A_рқ”ӯ`-module `(О©_{A/k}^1)_рқ”ӯ` admits `n` generators. Then:*

*(i) the `A_рқ”ӯ`-module `(О©_{A/k}^1)_рқ”ӯ` is free of rank `n`.*

*(ii) There exists a local `k`-homomorphism `u : B вҶ’ A`, where `B = k[[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n]]`, making `A` into a finite
`B`-algebra, and such that the corresponding morphism `Spec(A) вҶ’ Spec(B)` is Г©tale at the point `рқ”ӯ`.*

*(iii) The `k`-algebra `A_рқ”ӯ` is geometrically regular.*

Let us prove first (ii); by virtue of `(18.11.5)`, there exists a local homomorphism `u : B = k[[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n]] вҶ’ A`
making `A` into a finite `B`-algebra, and such that the corresponding morphism `Spec(A) вҶ’ Spec(B)` is unramified at the
point `рқ”ӯ`; set `рқ”Ҝ = uвҒ»В№(рқ”ӯ)`. The hypothesis on `рқ”® вҠӮ рқ”ӯ`, and the fact that `A` is a quotient of a regular ring
`(0, 19.8.8)` imply that one has `dim(A_рқ”ӯ) = n вҲ’ dim(A/рқ”ӯ)` `(0, 16.5.12)`. One has similarly `dim(B_рқ”Ҝ) = n вҲ’ dim(B/рқ”Ҝ)`.
Finally, since the morphism `Spec(A) вҶ’ Spec(B)` is unramified at the point `рқ”ӯ`, the fibre of this morphism at the point
`рқ”Ҝ` is of dimension `0`, hence `(0, 16.3.9)` one has `dim(A/рқ”ӯ) вүӨ dim(B/рқ”Ҝ)` and consequently `dim(B_рқ”Ҝ) вүӨ dim(A_рқ”ӯ)`. One
concludes therefore from `(18.10.1)` that the morphism `Spec(A) вҶ’ Spec(B)` is Г©tale at the point `рқ”ӯ`.

Assertion (iii) results from the fact that `A_рқ”ӯ` is formally smooth over `B_рқ”Ҝ` and that `B_рқ”Ҝ` is formally smooth over
`k` (for the preadic topologies) `(0, 19.3.4 and 19.3.5)`, hence `A_рқ”ӯ` is formally smooth over `k` for its preadic
topology, and consequently is geometrically regular over `k` `(0, 22.5.8)`.

Let us prove finally (i). Let `k'` be an algebraically closed extension of `k`, and consider the semi-local `k'`-algebra
`ГӮ' = A вҠ—МӮ_k k'`. If one considers `A` as a finite `B`-module by means of the homomorphism `u`, one can write, up to a
canonical isomorphism, `ГӮ' = A вҠ—_B (B вҠ—МӮ_k k')` (`(7.5.7.1)`, in the statement of which one recalls that it is not
necessary to suppose the residue field of `B` to be a finite extension of `k`). Set `B' = B вҠ—МӮ_k k'`, which identifies
canonically with the formal power series algebra `k'[[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n]]`. Since the morphism `Spec(A) вҶ’ Spec(B)` is finite
and Г©tale at the point `рқ”ӯ`, the morphism `Spec(ГӮ') вҶ’ Spec(B')` is finite, and Г©tale at every point `рқ”ӯ'` above `рқ”ӯ`
`(17.3.3)`; moreover, `ГӮ'` is direct composite of local rings `A'_i` of dimension `n` (`1 вүӨ i вүӨ r`) `(18.11.4)` and `рқ”ӯ'`
identifies with a prime ideal `рқ”ӯ'_i` of one of the `A'_i`. The same reasoning as above proves then that `(A'_i)_{рқ”ӯ'_i}`
is geometrically regular over `k'`, and since `k'` is perfect, it results from `(18.11.3)` that
`(О©МӮ_{A'_i/k'}^1)_{рқ”ӯ'_i}` is a `(A'_i)_{рқ”ӯ'_i}`-module free of finite type. But

<!-- original page 178 -->

since `(A'_i)_{рқ”ӯ'_i}` is isomorphic to `(О©_{A/k}^1)_рқ”ӯ вҠ—_{A_рқ”ӯ} (A'_i)_{рқ”ӯ'_i}` `(18.11.4)` and `(A'_i)_{рқ”ӯ'_i}` is an
`A_рқ”ӯ`-module faithfully flat, one sees that `(О©_{A/k}^1)_рқ”ӯ` is an `A_рқ”ӯ`-module free of finite type `(2.5.2)`; moreover,
by virtue of `(18.11.5.1)` and of the hypothesis `dim(A/рқ”®) = n`, one concludes that `(О©_{A/k}^1)_рқ”ӯ` is an `A_рқ”ӯ`-module
free of rank `n`. Q.E.D.

**Theorem (18.11.10).**

<!-- label: IV.18.11.10 -->

*Let `k` be a field of characteristic exponent `p`, `A` a complete Noetherian local `k`-algebra, whose residue field is
a finite extension of `k`, `рқ”ӯ` a prime ideal of `A` distinct from the maximal ideal. The following conditions are
equivalent:*

*a) For every extension `k'` of `k`, and every prime ideal `рқ”ӯ'` of `ГӮ' = A вҠ—МӮ_k k'` above `рқ”ӯ`, `ГӮ'_{рқ”ӯ'}` is a regular
ring.*

*a') There exist a perfect extension `k'` of `k` and a prime ideal `рқ”ӯ'` of `ГӮ' = A вҠ—МӮ_k k'` above `рқ”ӯ`, such that
`ГӮ'_{рқ”ӯ'}` is regular.*

*b) Let `n` be the largest of the dimensions of the irreducible components of `Spec(A)` to which `рқ”ӯ` belongs; then
`(О©_{A/k}^1)_рқ”ӯ` is an `A_рқ”ӯ`-module free of rank `n`.*

*Suppose moreover that `n = dim(A)` (which will be the case if `A` is equidimensional); then the preceding conditions
are also equivalent to:*

*c) There exists a local `k`-homomorphism `u : B вҶ’ A`, where `B = k[[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n]]`, making `A` into a finite
`B`-algebra, and such that the corresponding morphism `Spec(A) вҶ’ Spec(B)` is Г©tale at the point `рқ”ӯ`.*

*Each of the conditions a), a'), b) implies the following:*

*d) The ring `A_рқ”ӯ` is geometrically regular over `k`.*

*If moreover `[k : k^p] < +вҲһ`, condition d) is equivalent to a), a') and b).*

The fact that d) implies b) when `[k : k^p] < +вҲһ` is none other than `(18.11.3)`. It is clear that a) implies trivially
a'); let us show that c) implies a) when `dim(A) = n`. With the notations of a), one has then `ГӮ' = A вҠ—_B B'`, where
`B' = B вҠ—МӮ_k k' = k'[[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n]]` `(7.5.7.1)`. The morphism `Spec(ГӮ') вҶ’ Spec(B')` is then finite and Г©tale at the
point `рқ”ӯ'`, and the reasoning that proves `(18.11.9, (iii))` shows that `ГӮ'_{рқ”ӯ'}` is regular.

The fact that b) implies c) when `dim(A) = n` results from `(18.11.9)`. Let us show that a') implies b) when
`dim(A) = n`. One knows that `ГӮ'` is an `A`-module flat `(18.11.4)` and `dim(ГӮ') = dim(A) = n`; it results from
`(2.3.4)` and from `(6.1.1)` that there exists a minimal prime ideal `рқ”®'` of `ГӮ'` contained in `рқ”ӯ'`, above `рқ”®` and such
that `dim(ГӮ'/рқ”®') = dim(A/рқ”®) = n`. Moreover, it results from `(18.11.4)` that
`(О©МӮ_{ГӮ'/k'}^1)_{рқ”ӯ'} = (О©_{A/k}^1)_рқ”ӯ вҠ—_{A_рқ”ӯ} ГӮ'_{рқ”ӯ'}`; since `k'` is perfect, the hypothesis that `ГӮ'_{рқ”ӯ'}` is regular
implies that it is geometrically regular over `k'` `(6.7.7)`. Since `k'^p = k'`, one can apply to `ГӮ'` and `рқ”ӯ'` the fact
that d) implies b), hence `(О©МӮ_{ГӮ'/k'}^1)_{рқ”ӯ'}` is an `ГӮ'_{рқ”ӯ'}`-module free of rank `n`; by faithful flatness
`(18.11.4 and 2.5.2)`, one concludes that `(О©_{A/k}^1)_рқ”ӯ` is an `A_рқ”ӯ`-module free of rank `n`.

This shows the equivalence of a), a'), b) and c) when `dim(A) = n`. It remains to prove that a), a') and b) are still
equivalent in the general case. Let `рқ”Қ` be the ideal of `A`, kernel of the canonical homomorphism `A вҶ’ A_рқ”ӯ`, and set
`A_1 = A/рқ”Қ`; one has necessarily `рқ”Қ вҠӮ рқ”ӯ`, and if one sets `рқ”ӯ_1 = рқ”ӯ/рқ”Қ`, the canonical homomorphism `A_рқ”ӯ вҶ’ (A_1)_{рқ”ӯ_1}` is
bijective; one concludes `(I, 6.5.4)` that the canonical injection `Spec(A_1) вҶ’ Spec(A)` is a local isomorphism at the
point `рқ”ӯ_1`, and one has `рқ”Қ_рқ”ӯ = 0`. One sees as in `(18.11.3)` that one has an exact sequence

```text
  (рқ”Қ/рқ”Қ^2) вҶ’^j О©_{A/k}^1 вҠ—_A A_1 вҶ’ О©_{A_1/k}^1 вҶ’ 0
```

<!-- original page 179 -->

and localizing at `рқ”ӯ`, there comes an isomorphism `(О©_{A/k}^1)_рқ”ӯ = (О©_{A_1/k}^1)_{рқ”ӯ_1}`. This shows that condition b)
for the ring `A` and the ideal `рқ”ӯ` is equivalent to condition b) for the ring `A_1` and the ideal `рқ”ӯ_1`. On the other
hand, with the notations of a), one has `ГӮ'_1 = A_1 вҠ—МӮ_k k' = ГӮ'/рқ”Қ ГӮ'` up to isomorphism (`(7.5.7.1)`, where the
hypothesis on the residue field of `B` is superfluous); if `рқ”ӯ'` is a prime ideal of `ГӮ'` above `рқ”ӯ`, every element of
`рқ”Қ ГӮ'` annihilates an element of `ГӮ' вҲ’ рқ”ӯ'`, hence `рқ”Қ ГӮ' вҠӮ рқ”ӯ'`, and if one sets `рқ”ӯ'_1 = рқ”ӯ'/рқ”Қ ГӮ'`, `рқ”ӯ'_1` is above `рқ”ӯ_1`
and `(ГӮ'_1)_{рқ”ӯ'_1}` identifies canonically with `ГӮ'_{рқ”ӯ'}`; this shows therefore that condition a) (resp. a')) for the
ring `A` and the ideal `рқ”ӯ` is equivalent to condition a) (resp. a')) for the ring `A_1` and the ideal `рқ”ӯ_1`. Now, all
the minimal prime ideals of `A` contained in `рқ”ӯ` contain `рқ”Қ` since `Spec(A_1) вҶ’ Spec(A)` is a local isomorphism at the
point `рқ”ӯ_1`; on the other hand the ideals of `Ass_A(A/рқ”Қ)` are the ideals of `Ass(A)` which are contained in `рқ”ӯ`
(Bourbaki, Alg. comm., chap. IV, В§1, nВ° 2, prop. 6); so the minimal prime ideals of `A_1` are all contained in `рқ”ӯ_1`,
and one has consequently `dim(A_1) = n`. It then suffices to apply to `A_1` and to `рқ”ӯ_1` what has been proved above.

**Remarks (18.11.11).** вҖ” (i) The equivalence of conditions d) and b) in `(18.11.10)` is no longer valid when one no
longer supposes that `[k : k^p] < +вҲһ`. Indeed, in the example of `(0, 22.7.7, (ii))`, the ring `B = A/рқ”®` is integral and
of dimension `1`; on the other hand, the sequence

```text
  (рқ”®/рқ”®^2) вҠ—_A L вҶ’^j О©_{A/k}^1 вҠ—_A L вҶ’ О©_{B/k}^1 вҠ—_B L вҶ’ 0
```

is exact (same proof as in `(18.11.3)`), and one knows that `j` is not injective, hence `j = 0` since `(рқ”®/рқ”®^2) вҠ—_A L` is
of rank `1`. One concludes that `rg_L(О©_{B/k}^1 вҠ—_B L) = 2`. Since `B_рқ”ӯ` is a geometrically regular `k`-algebra, one
sees that here condition d) does not imply b).

(ii) The notations being those of `(18.11.10)`, suppose that `n = dim(A)` and let `(x_i)_{1 вүӨ i вүӨ n}` be a system of
parameters of `A` not belonging to `рқ”ӯ`; one deduces from it a local `k`-homomorphism `u : B вҶ’ A` such that
`u(T_i) = x_i` for `1 вүӨ i вүӨ n`, making `A` into a finite `B`-algebra. In order that the corresponding morphism
`Spec(A) вҶ’ Spec(B)` be Г©tale at the point `рқ”ӯ`, it is necessary and sufficient that the images of the `dx_i` in
`(О©_{A/k}^1)_рқ”ӯ` form a system of generators of this `A_рқ”ӯ`-module. Indeed, one has seen in the proof of `(18.11.5)` that
if the morphism `Spec(A) вҶ’ Spec(B)` is unramified at the point `рқ”ӯ`, the canonical homomorphism
`(О©_{B/k}^1 вҠ—_B A)_рқ”ӯ вҶ’ (О©_{A/k}^1)_рқ”ӯ` is surjective and the images of the elements `dT_i вҠ— 1`, which generate
`О©_{B/k}^1 вҠ—_B A`, are the `dx_i`, whence the necessity of the condition. Conversely, the same reasoning shows that if
this condition is verified, the morphism `Spec(A) вҶ’ Spec(B)` is unramified at `рқ”ӯ`, and the reasoning of `(18.11.9)`
proves in fact that this morphism is Г©tale at `рқ”ӯ`.

**Corollary (18.11.12).**

<!-- label: IV.18.11.12 -->

*Let `k` be a field of characteristic exponent `p` such that `[k : k^p] < +вҲһ`, `A` a complete Noetherian local and
integral `k`-algebra, which is not a field, and whose residue field is a finite extension of `k`. There then exists a
finite radicial extension `k'` of `k` such that, setting `ГӮ' = A вҠ—МӮ_k k'`, the `k'`-algebra `ГӮ'_{red}` and the prime
ideal `0` of this algebra verify the equivalent conditions a), a'), b), c) and d) of `(18.11.10)`. In particular, if
`n = dim(A) = dim(ГӮ')`,*

<!-- original page 180 -->

*there exists a local `k'`-homomorphism `B' = k'[[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n]] вҶ’ ГӮ'_{red}` making `ГӮ'_{red}` into a finite
`B'`-algebra, and such that the field of fractions `K'` of `ГӮ'_{red}` is a finite separable extension of the field of
fractions `k'((T_1, вҖҰ, T_n))` of `B'`.*

The morphism `Spec(ГӮ') вҶ’ Spec(A)` being radicial and finite, `ГӮ'` is a complete local ring and its nilradical is the
only prime ideal above the ideal `0` of `A`; by flatness, `ГӮ'` identifies with a subring of `K вҠ—_k k'`, which is
moreover the total ring of fractions of `ГӮ'`; one has consequently `K' = (K вҠ—_k k')_{red}`. It is a question of proving,
in view of the equivalence d) `вҮ”` c) of `(18.11.10)`, that there exists a finite radicial extension `k'` of `k` such
that `(K вҠ—_k k')_{red}` is a separable extension of `k'` `(6.7.6)`. Now one knows `(0, 19.8.9)` that under the
hypotheses made, there exists a sub-`k`-algebra `C = k[[T_1, вҖҰ, T_n]]` of `A` such that `A` is a finite `C`-algebra; `K`
is therefore a finite extension of the field of fractions `K_1 = k((T_1, вҖҰ, T_n))` of `C`, which is separable over `k`
`(0, 21.9.6.4)`. If `p` is the characteristic exponent of `k`, one can therefore write
`K вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ} = K вҠ—_{K_1} (K_1 вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ})` and `K_1 вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}` is a field, radicial extension of `K_1`; one
concludes that `K вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}` is a finite algebra over the field `K_1 вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}`, hence an Artinian ring. The
conclusion therefore results from the following more general lemma:

**Lemma (18.11.12.1).** *Let `k` be a field of characteristic `p > 0`, `K` an extension of `k`. The following conditions
are equivalent:*

*a) The ring `K вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}` is Artinian.*

*b) There exists an extension `k'` of `k` of finite type such that `(K вҠ—_k k')_{red}` is a separable `k'`-algebra.*

*c) There exists a finite radicial extension `k'` of `k` such that `(K вҠ—_k k')_{red}` is a separable extension of `k'`.*

Let us first show that c) implies a). The ring `A = K вҠ—_k k'` is then a local Artinian ring, and if `рқ”‘` is its
nilradical, the residue field `L = A/рқ”‘` is separable over `k'`; consequently `L вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}` is a field, and since it is
equal to `(A вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ})_{red} = (A/рқ”‘)(вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ})`, one sees that `рқ”‘ вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}` is the nilradical of
`A вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ} = K вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}`; since `рқ”‘` is an ideal of finite type, the nilradical of `K вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}` is therefore of
finite type, which implies that the ring `K вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}` is Artinian.

Conversely, let us prove that a) implies c). Let `рқ”‘` be the nilradical of the Artinian local ring `B = K вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}`,
which is by hypothesis generated by a finite number of elements of the form `z_i = вҲ‘ О»_{ij} вҠ— Оҫ_{ij}`, where
`О»_{ij} вҲҲ K`, `Оҫ_{ij} вҲҲ k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}`. Let `k'` be the finite radicial extension of `k` generated by the `Оҫ_{ij}`, `рқ”‘_0` the
ideal of `B_0 = K вҠ—_k k'` generated by the `z_i`; it is clear that the `z_i` are nilpotent in `B_0`; on the other hand,
one has `рқ”‘_0 вҠ—_{k'} k^{pвҒ»вҲһ} = рқ”‘`, and consequently `рқ”‘ вҲ© B_0 = рқ”‘_0`, hence `рқ”‘_0` contains the nilradical of `B_0`, hence
it is equal to it. Since `B/рқ”‘ = (B_0/рқ”‘_0) вҠ—_{k'} k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}` is reduced, one concludes that `B_0/рқ”‘_0 = (K вҠ—_k k')_{red}` is
separable over `k'` `(4.6.1)`.

It is clear that c) implies b). Conversely, suppose b) verified, and note that there exists a separable extension `k_1`
of `k` such that `k'` is a finite radicial extension of `k_1`; set `K_1 = K вҠ—_k k_1`, which is a field. Applying the
equivalence of a) and c) to the extension `K_1` of `k_1`, one sees that `K_1 вҠ—_{k_1} k_1^{pвҒ»вҲһ}` is an Artinian ring; but
this ring is equal

<!-- original page 181 -->

to `K вҠ—_k k_1^{pвҒ»вҲһ} = (K вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}) вҠ—_{k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}} k_1^{pвҒ»вҲһ}`, hence `K вҠ—_k k^{pвҒ»вҲһ}` is also Artinian (Bourbaki, Alg.
comm., chap. I, В§3, nВ° 5, cor. of prop. 8); one has thus proved that b) implies a), which finishes the proof of
`(18.11.12.1)` and of `(18.11.12)`.

### 18.12. Applications of Г©tale localization to quasi-finite morphisms (generalizations of earlier results)

The results of this number have been communicated to us by P. Deligne.

**Theorem (18.12.1).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.1 -->

*Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a morphism locally of finite type, `x` a point of `X`, `y = f(x)`. Suppose that `x` is an isolated
point of the space `fвҒ»В№(y)`. Then, there exist an Г©tale morphism `Y' вҶ’ Y`, a point `x'` of `X' = X Г—_Y Y'` above `x` and
an open neighbourhood `V'` of `x'` in `X'` such that, if `f' = f_{(Y')} : X' вҶ’ Y'`, `f' | V'` is a finite morphism. If
moreover `f` is separated, `V'` is both open and closed, and `X'` is therefore the sum of two sub-preschemes induced on
opens of `X'`, of which one is finite over `Y'` and contains `x'`.*

The last assertion results from the fact that, if `f` is separated, the same is true of `f'`; so, if `j' : V' вҶ’ X'` is
the canonical injection, the fact that the morphism `f' | V' = f' вҲҳ j'` is finite implies that the same is true of `j'`
`(II, 6.1.5)`, and consequently `V' = j'(V')` is closed in `X'` `(II, 6.1.10)`.

The question being local on `X`, one can suppose `Y = Spec(A)` and `X = Spec(B)` affine, `B` being an `A`-algebra of
finite type, hence of the form `C/рқ”Қ`, where `C = A[T_1, вҖҰ, T_r]` and `рқ”Қ` is an ideal of `C`; `f` is therefore separated,
and one can moreover suppose that `fвҒ»В№(y) = {x}`. Let `(рқ”Қ_О»)` be the family of ideals of finite type of `C` contained in
`рқ”Қ`, so that `рқ”Қ` is the filtered union of the `рқ”Қ_О»`. If `X` and the `X_О» = Spec(C/рқ”Қ_О»)` are considered as closed
sub-preschemes of `Z = Spec(C)`, one has therefore, for the underlying spaces, `X = вӢӮ X_О»`; if `f_О» : X_О» вҶ’ Y` is the
structural morphism, one deduces that `f_О»вҒ»В№(y) = вӢӮ f_О»вҒ»В№(y)`, and since the sets `f_О»вҒ»В№(y)` are closed in the
Noetherian space `Z_y = Spec(k(y)[T_1, вҖҰ, T_r])`, there exists an index `О»` such that `f_О»вҒ»В№(y) = fвҒ»В№(y) = {x}`. One can
therefore suppose that the `X_О»` verify the same condition as `X` at the point `x`; if one proves the proposition for
such an `X_О»`, it will result for `X`, since if `x'` is a point above `x` in `Z' = Z Г—_Y Y'`, `X'_О» = pвҒ»В№(X_О»)`, where
`p : Z' вҶ’ Z` is the projection (so that one has also `X' = pвҒ»В№(X)`), if there exists an open neighbourhood `V'_О»` of
`x'` in `X'_О»` which is finite over `Y'`, a fortiori the restriction of `f'_О»` to the closed sub-prescheme `X' вҲ© V'_О»`
of `V'_О»` will be a finite morphism. One is therefore reduced to the case where `f` is of finite presentation. Note
moreover that the set of points of `X` isolated in their fibre is open in `X` `(13.1.4)`, so `f` is quasi-finite at the
point `x`, and one can consequently restrict to the case where `f` is quasi-finite. Let `A^h` be the Henselized local
ring of `рқ’Ә_{Y,y}`, and set `Y^h = Spec(A^h)`. If `X^h = X Г—_Y Y^h`, `f^h = f_{(Y^h)} : X^h вҶ’ Y^h` is separated,
quasi-finite and of finite presentation; since `A^h` is Henselian, there is for every `x^h вҲҲ X^h` above `x` an open and
closed neighbourhood `V^h` of `x^h` in `X^h` which is finite over `Y^h` `(18.5.11, c))`; since the immersion `V^h вҶ’ X^h`
is open and closed, it is quasi-compact, hence of finite presentation `(1.6.2)`, so `f^h | V^h` is of finite
presentation.

This being so, by definition, `A^h` is the inductive limit of a filtered family `(A_Оұ)` of strictly essentially Г©tale
`рқ’Ә_{Y,y}`-algebras `(18.6.5)`; each `A_Оұ` is itself the inductive limit of a filtered family `(B_{ОұОІ})` of Г©tale
`рқ’Ә_{Y,y}`-algebras (`(18.6.1)` and `(8.1.2, a))`). Finally, since `B_{ОұОІ}` may be supposed an `рқ’Ә_{Y,y}`-algebra of
finite presentation, it results moreover from `(8.1.2, a))` and from `(17.7.8)` that `B_{ОұОІ}` is the inductive limit of
a filtered family `(C_{ОұОІОі})` of Г©tale `A`-algebras. Finally, one sees, using the theorem of the double inductive limit,
that `Y^h` is the projective limit of a filtered family `(Y_Оұ)` of affine schemes Г©tale over `Y`. If `x_Оұ` is the
projection of `x^h` onto `X_Оұ = X Г—_Y Y_Оұ`, one can suppose that the neighbourhood `V^h`, which is quasi-compact, is of
the form `V_Оұ Г—_{Y_Оұ} Y^h` where `V_Оұ` is an open neighbourhood of `x_Оұ` in `X_Оұ` `(8.2.11)`. Finally, `V^h` being of
finite presentation over `Y^h`, one concludes from `(8.10.5, (x))` that for a suitable `Оұ`, `V_Оұ` is finite over `Y_Оұ`.
Q.E.D.

**Remark (18.12.2).** вҖ” In the preceding proof, one sees (taking account of `(18.6.2)`) that one has constructed a `Y'`
answering the question, and such moreover that if `y' = f'(x')`, the homomorphism `k(y) вҶ’ k(y')` is bijective.

**Corollary (18.12.3).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.3 -->

*Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a morphism locally of finite type and separated, `y` a point of `Y` such that the subspace `fвҒ»В№(y)`
is finite and discrete. There then exist an Г©tale morphism `Y' вҶ’ Y`, a point `y' вҲҲ Y'` above `y`, such that
`k(y') = k(y)`, and a decomposition of `X'` into the sum of two sub-preschemes `X'_1`, `X'_2` induced on opens of `X'`,
such that the restriction of `f' = f_{(Y')} : X' вҶ’ Y'` to `X'_1` is a finite morphism and one has
`X'_2 вҲ© f'вҒ»В№(y') = вҲ…`.*

If `n` is the number of points of `fвҒ»В№(y)`, one reasons by recurrence on `n`, the corollary being trivial for `n = 0`.
Let `x` be a point of `fвҒ»В№(y)`; by virtue of `(18.12.1)` and `(18.12.2)` there is an Г©tale morphism `Y_1 вҶ’ Y`, a point
`y_1` of `Y_1` above `y` such that `k(y_1) = k(y)`, and if one sets `S_1 = X Г—_Y Y_1`, `f_1 = f_{(Y_1)} : S_1 вҶ’ Y_1`,
there exists a point `x_1` of `f_1вҒ»В№(y_1)`

<!-- original page 182 -->

such that `S_1` is the sum of two opens `V_1`, `X_1`, `V_1` being finite over `Y_1` and a neighbourhood of `x_1`. By
virtue of the relation `k(y_1) = k(y)`, the fibre `f_1вҒ»В№(y_1)` in `S_1` is isomorphic to `fвҒ»В№(y)`, so `X_1 вҲ© f_1вҒ»В№(y_1)`
is finite, discrete and has `n вҲ’ 1` points. Since `f_1 | X_1` is locally of finite type and separated, one applies the
hypothesis of recurrence to this morphism: there is an Г©tale morphism `Y' вҶ’ Y_1`, a point `y' вҲҲ Y'` above `y_1` such
that `k(y') = k(y_1)`, and, if `X' = X Г—_Y Y'` and if `p : X' вҶ’ S_1` is the canonical projection, one has a
decomposition of `pвҒ»В№(X_1)` into a sum of two sub-preschemes `U'` and `X'_2` induced on opens of `X'` such that
`X'_2 вҲ© f'вҒ»В№(y') = вҲ…` and that `U'` is finite over `Y'`. Moreover, `V' = pвҒ»В№(V_1)` is finite over `Y'` and `X'` is the
sum of `U'`, `V'` and `X'_2`; one will therefore answer the question by taking `X'_1` to be the sum of `U'` and `V'`.

The following corollary improves `(8.11.1)`:

**Corollary (18.12.4).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.4 -->

*In order that a morphism `f : X вҶ’ Y` be finite, it is necessary and sufficient that it be separated, universally
closed, locally of finite type and that, for every `y вҲҲ Y`, `fвҒ»В№(y)` be a finite discrete space; in particular, a proper
and quasi-finite morphism is finite.*

Indeed, one can apply corollary `(18.12.3)` to an arbitrary point `y` of `Y`. With the notations of that corollary, `f'`
is a closed morphism, so, since `X'_2` is closed in `X'`, `f'(X'_2)` is closed in `Y'` and does not contain `y'`; there
consequently exists an open neighbourhood `U'` of `y'` in `Y'` such that `U' вҶ’ Y` is of finite type and that
`f'вҒ»В№(U') = X Г—_Y U'` is finite over `U'`. Let `U` be the image of `U'` in `Y`, which is an open of `Y` by virtue of
`(11.3.1)` since the morphism `Y' вҶ’ Y` is Г©tale, hence flat and locally of finite presentation; one evidently has still
`X Г—_Y U = X Г—_Y U' = fвҒ»В№(U) Г—_U U'`. Since now the morphism `U' вҶ’ U` is faithfully flat and quasi-compact, one deduces
from `(2.7.1, (xv))` that the morphism `fвҒ»В№(U) вҶ’ U`, restriction of `f`, is finite, which proves the corollary.

**Remark (18.12.5).** вҖ” One will note that in the proof of `(18.12.4)` one has not used the hypothesis that `f` is
universally closed in its general form, but only that `f_{(Y')}` is a closed morphism for every Г©tale morphism `Y' вҶ’ Y`.

**Corollary (18.12.6).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.6 -->

*Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a morphism of preschemes. The following conditions are equivalent:*

*a) `f` is a closed immersion.*

*b) `f` is a proper monomorphism.*

*c) `f` is proper and, for every `y вҲҲ Y`, the `k(y)`-prescheme `X_y = fвҒ»В№(y)` is radicial and geometrically reduced over
`k(y)` (i.e. empty or `k(y)`-isomorphic to `Spec(k(y))`).*

This is deduced from `(18.12.4)` as `(8.11.5)` is deduced from `(8.11.1)`.

**Proposition (18.12.7).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.7 -->

*Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a morphism locally of finite type, `y` a point of `Y`. In order that there exist an open
neighbourhood `U` of `y` such that the restriction `fвҒ»В№(U) вҶ’ U` of `f` be a closed immersion, it is necessary and
sufficient that `X_y` be a `k(y)`-prescheme radicial and geometrically reduced over `k(y)` (i.e. empty or
`k(y)`-isomorphic to `Spec(k(y))`) and that there exist an open neighbourhood `V` of `y` such that the restriction
`fвҒ»В№(V) вҶ’ V` of `f` be a universally closed morphism.*

The conditions being evidently necessary, let us prove that they are sufficient. One can restrict to the case where
`X_y вү  вҲ…`. By virtue of the second condition, one can already suppose `f` universally closed. Let us show moreover that
one can suppose `f` affine, hence separated; this results from the following lemma:

**Lemma (18.12.7.1).** *Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a closed morphism, `y вҲҲ Y` a point such that every neighbourhood of `X_y`
contains an affine neighbourhood of `X_y` (condition always verified when `X_y` is empty or reduced to a single point).
Then there exists an affine open neighbourhood `U` of `y` such that the restriction `fвҒ»В№(U) вҶ’ U` of `f` be an affine
morphism.*

Indeed, let `U_0` be an affine open neighbourhood of `y` in `Y` and let `V` be an affine open neighbourhood of `X_y`
contained in `fвҒ»В№(U_0)`. Since `f` is closed, there exists an affine open neighbourhood `U вҠӮ U_0` of `y` such that
`fвҒ»В№(U) вҠӮ V`. Since the restriction `g : V вҶ’ U_0` of `f` is an affine morphism, the same is true of its restriction
`fвҒ»В№(U) вҶ’ U` `(II, 1.2.5)`.

Suppose therefore `f` affine and universally closed, and let us show that there exists an open neighbourhood `U` of `y`
such that the restriction `fвҒ»В№(U) вҶ’ U` is a finite morphism; since one can suppose `Y` and `X` affine, one can suppose
`f` of finite type, hence proper, and it suffices to prove that there exists a neighbourhood `U` of `y` such that
`fвҒ»В№(U) вҶ’ U` is a quasi-finite morphism `(18.12.4)`. But there exists a neighbourhood `V` of the set `X_y` (reduced to a
single point) such that `f | V` is quasi-finite `(13.1.4)`, and since `f` is closed there is a neighbourhood `U` of `y`
such that `fвҒ»В№(U) вҠӮ V`, which finishes the proof, taking account of `(18.12.6)`.

**Proposition (18.12.8).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.8 -->

*Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a morphism of preschemes. In order that `f` be integral, it is necessary and sufficient that `f` be
affine and universally closed.*

The conditions are necessary `(II, 6.1.10)`; let us prove that they are sufficient. One can suppose `Y = Spec(A)`
affine, hence also `X = Spec(B)`, and it must be proved that every element `b вҲҲ B` is integral over `A` `(II, 6.1.1)`.
Let `B'` be the sub-`A`-algebra of `B` generated by `b`, which is an `A`-algebra of finite type; set `X' = Spec(B')`, so
that `f : X вҶ’ Y` factors as `X вҶ’^g X' вҶ’^h Y`, where `h` is of finite type, and `g` is dominant since the homomorphism
`B' вҶ’ B` is injective `(I, 1.2.7)`. Since `h` is separated and `h вҲҳ g` universally closed, `g` is universally closed
`(II, 5.4.3 and`

<!-- original page 183 -->

`5.4.9)`, hence surjective since it is dominant; one concludes `(II, 5.4.3 and 5.4.9)` that `h` is also universally
closed, hence proper since it is of finite type and separated. But then, for every `y вҲҲ Y`, the morphism
`hвҒ»В№(y) вҶ’ Spec(k(y))` deduced from `h` is proper and affine, hence finite `(III, 4.4.2)`, in other words `h` is
quasi-finite; one deduces therefore from `(18.12.4)` that `h` is finite, which proves that `B'` is a finite `A`-algebra,
and consequently that `b` is integral over `A`. Q.E.D.

**Remark (18.12.9).** вҖ” It may be that a morphism `f : X вҶ’ Y` be integral when one supposes it only separated,
universally closed and such that for every `y вҲҲ Y`, the morphism `fвҒ»В№(y) вҶ’ Spec(k(y))` deduced from `f` is integral. It
would be necessary for this to prove that these conditions imply that `f` is affine, or again that every fibre `X_y` is
contained in an affine open neighbourhood.

**Corollary (18.12.10).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.10 -->

*A morphism `f : X вҶ’ Y` which is injective and universally closed is integral.*

It suffices, by `(18.12.8)`, to prove that `f` is affine, which results from lemma `(18.12.7.1)` and from the
hypothesis.

**Corollary (18.12.11).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.11 -->

*Let `f : X вҶ’ Y` be a morphism of preschemes (resp. a morphism locally of finite type). In order that `f` be a universal
homeomorphism `(2.4.2)`, it is necessary and sufficient that `f` be integral (resp. finite), radicial and surjective.*

One knows that the conditions are sufficient `(2.4.5)`; they are necessary by virtue of `(18.12.10)` and `(18.12.4)`.

The following proposition improves `(8.11.2)`:

**Proposition (18.12.12).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.12 -->

*Every morphism `f : X вҶ’ Y` which is quasi-finite and separated is quasi-affine.*

Set `рқ’ң = f_*(рқ’Ә_X)`, which is a quasi-coherent `рқ’Ә_Y`-algebra since `f` is quasi-compact and separated `(1.7.4)`; let
`Z = Spec(рқ’ң)` `(II, 1.3.1)` so that `f` factors canonically as `X вҶ’^g Z вҶ’^h Y`, `h` being affine and `g` corresponding
to the identity automorphism of `рқ’ң` `(II, 1.2.7)`; it will suffice to prove that `g` is an open immersion, or, what
amounts to the same `(17.9.1)`, that `g` is Г©tale and radicial. It will evidently suffice to show that, for every
`y вҲҲ Y`, the morphism `g` is Г©tale and radicial at each point of `fвҒ»В№(y)`. Now, for every `y вҲҲ Y`, one can apply to `f`
the result of `(18.12.3)`, of which we preserve the notations; since the morphism `Y' вҶ’ Y` is flat, and that `f` is
quasi-compact and separated, one has, up to canonical isomorphism, `f'_*(рқ’Ә_{X'}) = рқ’ң вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_Y} рқ’Ә_{Y'} = рқ’ң'` `(2.3.1)`, so
`Z' = Z Г—_Y Y'` identifies with `Spec(f'_*(рқ’Ә_{X'}))`, and in the canonical factorization `X' вҶ’^{g'} Z' вҶ’^{h'} Y'` of
`f'` `(II, 1.2.7)`, one has `h' = h_{(Y')}` and `g' = g_{(Y')}`. This being so, the decomposition of `X'` into the sum
of two sub-preschemes `X'_1`, `X'_2` implies the decomposition of `рқ’ң'` into the direct product of the two quasi-coherent
`рқ’Ә_{Y'}`-algebras `рқ’ң'_1`, `рқ’ң'_2`, direct images respectively of `рқ’Ә_{X'_1}` and `рқ’Ә_{X'_2}`, so that `Z'` identifies with
the sum `Z'_1 вҠ” Z'_2`, where `Z'_i = Spec(рқ’ң'_i)` and `g'(X'_i) вҠӮ Z'_i` for `i = 1, 2`. Since `X'_1` is finite over `Y'`,
`g'_1 = g' | X'_1` is an isomorphism of `X'_1` onto `Z'_1`, since `f' | X'_1` is affine; since `X'_2 вҲ© f'вҒ»В№(y') = вҲ…`,
one sees that `g'` is Г©tale and radicial at each point of `f'вҒ»В№(y')`. The morphism `Y' вҶ’ Y` being flat and locally of
finite presentation, one therefore deduces first from `(17.7.4)` that `g` is Г©tale at all points of `X` projections of
points of `f'вҒ»В№(y')`, that is to say at all points of `fвҒ»В№(y)` `(I, 3.5.2)`. On the other hand, the morphism
`g'_{y'} : f'вҒ»В№(y') вҶ’ h'вҒ»В№(y')` deduced from `g'` is radicial; since `k(y') = k(y)`, the morphism
`g_y : fвҒ»В№(y) вҶ’ hвҒ»В№(y)` is also radicial, in other words `g` is radicial at each point of `fвҒ»В№(y)`, which finishes
proving the proposition.

The following statement improves similarly `(8.12.6)`:

**Corollary (18.12.13)** *("Main Theorem" of Zariski).* вҖ” *Let `Y` be a quasi-compact and quasi-separated prescheme,
`f : X вҶ’ Y` a quasi-finite and separated morphism. Then there exists a factorization of `f`*

```text
  X вҶ’^g Z вҶ’^u Y
```

*where `g` is an open immersion (necessarily quasi-compact) and `u` a finite morphism.*

Indeed, it results from `(18.12.12)` that `f` is quasi-affine, hence quasi-projective. One can then apply `(8.12.8)`,
where the hypothesis of the existence of an ample `рқ’Ә_Y`-Module can in fact be replaced by the sole hypothesis that `Y`
is quasi-compact and quasi-separated: indeed, it results from `(8.12.3)` that the existence of the announced
factorization in `(8.12.8)` is a property local on `Y`, and that it therefore suffices to prove it when `Y` is affine.

**Remark (18.12.14).** вҖ” One can give of `(18.12.13)` a proof analogous to that of `(18.12.12)` not using `(8.12.8)`
(but using `(18.12.3)`, hence `(18.5.11)`, which itself uses the "Main theorem" in its local form `(8.12.9)`). Let us
indeed keep the notations of the proof of `(18.12.12)`, and let `в„¬` be the quasi-coherent `рқ’Ә_Y`-Algebra, *integral
closure* of `рқ’Ә_Y` in `рқ’ң` `(II, 6.3.2)`. If one sets `T = Spec(в„¬)`, it suffices, by virtue of `(8.12.3)`, to prove that
the `Y`-morphism `gМғ : X вҶ’ T` corresponding to the canonical injection `в„¬ вҶ’ рқ’ң` is an immersion, and for this it suffices
to show `(17.9.1)` that `gМғ` is Г©tale and radicial. With the notations of `(18.12.12)`, one can suppose that
`Y = Spec(C)` and `Y' = Spec(C')` are affine, `C'` being an Г©tale `C`-algebra `(17.3.2)`; hence `рқ’ң = Гғ`, where `A` is

<!-- original page 184 -->

a `C`-algebra, `рқ’ң' = Гғ'` with `A' = A вҠ—_C C'`, and `в„¬ = BМғ`, where `B` is the integral closure of `C` in `A`. The
algebra `A'` is isomorphic to the product `A'_1 Г— A'_2`, where `A'_1` is a finite `C'`-algebra. It will suffice to prove
that `B' = B вҠ—_C C'`, which identifies by flatness with a sub-`C'`-algebra of `A'`, contains `A'_1`, for indeed `B'`
will then decompose into the product `A'_1 Г— A''_2`, where `A''_2` is a sub-`C'`-algebra of `A'_2`, and if one sets
`T'_2 = Spec(A''_2)`, `T' = T Г—_Y Y'` will be the sum of `Z'_1 = Spec(A'_1)` and `T'_2`, and `gМғ' | X'_1` will be an
isomorphism of `X'_1` onto `Z'_1`, which will allow one to conclude as in `(18.12.12)`.

To prove that `B'` contains `A'_1`, it evidently suffices to prove the following proposition, which extends partially
`(6.14.4)` when one no longer makes Noetherian hypotheses:

**Proposition (18.12.15).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.15 -->

*Let `C` be a ring, `C'` an Г©tale `C`-algebra, `A` a `C`-algebra, `B` the integral closure of `C` in `A`; one sets
`A' = A вҠ—_C C'`, `B' = B вҠ—_C C'`, `B'` being identified with a sub-algebra of `A'`; then `B'` is the integral closure of
`C'` in `A'`.*

By considering the filtered increasing family of sub-`C`-algebras of finite type of `A` and reasoning as in
`(6.14.4, II)`, one can first suppose that `A` is a `C`-algebra of finite type, hence of the form `E/рқ”Қ`, where
`E = C[T_1, вҖҰ, T_r]` and `рқ”Қ` is an ideal of `E`; one has then `A' = E'/рқ”Қ E'`, where `E' = C'[T_1, вҖҰ, T_r]`. Let `(рқ”Қ_О»)`
be the filtered increasing family of ideals of finite type of `E` contained in `рқ”Қ`, so that `A` is the inductive limit
of the `E/рқ”Қ_О»`; if `B_О»` is the integral closure of `C` in `E/рқ”Қ_О»`, `B` is the inductive limit of the `B_О»`, as the
reasoning of `(5.13.4)` shows. Similarly the integral closure of `C'` in `E'/рқ”Қ E'` is the inductive limit of the
integral closure of `C'` in `E'/рқ”Қ_О» E'`; if one proves that the latter is equal to `B_О» вҠ—_C C'`, it will result that
`B' = lim^вҶ’ (B_О» вҠ—_C C')` will be the integral closure of `C'` in `A'`. One is thus reduced to proving the proposition
when `A` is a `C`-algebra of finite presentation.

Let us next show that one can reduce to the case where `C` is Noetherian. Indeed, `C` is the filtered union of its
sub-`в„Ө`-algebras of finite type `C_Оұ`, so it results from `(17.7.8)` that there exists an index `Оұ` and an Г©tale
`C_Оұ`-algebra `C'_Оұ` such that `C' = C'_Оұ вҠ—_{C_Оұ} C`; moreover `C'` is the inductive limit of the
`C'_ОІ = C'_Оұ вҠ—_{C_Оұ} C_ОІ` for `ОІ вүҘ Оұ`. One can moreover suppose, since `A` is a `C`-algebra of finite presentation, that
`A = A_Оұ вҠ—_{C_Оұ} C`, where `A_Оұ` is a `C_Оұ`-algebra of finite type, and `A` is the inductive limit of the
`A_ОІ = A_Оұ вҠ—_{C_Оұ} C_ОІ` for `ОІ вүҘ Оұ` `(8.9.1)`. The reasoning of `(5.13.4)` then shows that `B` is the inductive limit of
the integral closures `B_ОІ` of the `C_ОІ` in the `A_ОІ`. Similarly `A'` is the inductive limit of the
`A'_ОІ = A_ОІ вҠ—_{C_ОІ} C'_ОІ = A_Оұ вҠ—_{C_Оұ} C'_ОІ` for `ОІ вүҘ Оұ`, hence the same reasoning as above shows that it will suffice
to prove that `B'_ОІ = B_ОІ вҠ—_{C_ОІ} C'_ОІ` is the integral closure of `C'_ОІ` in `A'_ОІ`.

Once reduced to the case where `C` is Noetherian, the proposition becomes a particular case of `(6.14.4)`. One must
nevertheless observe that, when `C'` is supposed Г©tale over `C` Noetherian, the proof of `(6.14.4)` no longer requires
the delicate theorem `(6.14.1)`. Indeed, the successive reductions of the proof of `(6.14.4)` reduce, without using
`(6.14.1)`, to the case where `C` is integral, `A` the field of fractions of `C`. Since then `B` is a normal ring and
the morphism `Spec(B') вҶ’ Spec(B)` is Г©tale, it results from `(17.5.7)` that `B'` is a normal ring; the reasoning ends by
appealing only to the elementary lemma `(6.14.1.1)`, but not to the difficult part of the proof of `(6.14.1)`.

**Proposition (18.12.16).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.16 -->

*Let `g : Y вҶ’ S` be a quasi-compact morphism, `f : X вҶ’ Y` a separated and quasi-finite morphism. For every invertible
`рқ’Ә_Y`-Module `в„’`, ample relative to `S` `(II, 4.6.1)`, the `рқ’Ә_X`-Module `f*(в„’)` is ample relative to `S`.*

Indeed, by virtue of `(18.12.12)`, the morphism `f` is quasi-affine, hence `(II, 5.1.6)` the `рқ’Ә_X`-Module `рқ’Ә_X` is ample
for `f`. One deduces `(II, 4.6.13, (ii))` that `рқ’Ә_X вҠ—_{рқ’Ә_Y} f*(в„’^{вҠ— n}) = f*(в„’^{вҠ— n})` is ample relative to `S` for `n`
large enough. But since `f*(в„’^{вҠ— n}) = (f*(в„’))^{вҠ— n}`, this implies that `f*(в„’)` is ample relative to `S`
`(II, 4.6.9, (i))`.

**Corollary (18.12.17).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.17 -->

*Let `Z` be an affine scheme, `h : X вҶ’ Z` a morphism of finite type, `в„’` an invertible `рқ’Ә_X`-Module. With the notations
of `(II, 4.5.2)`, the conditions of `(II, 4.5.2)` (which are equivalent to the fact that `в„’` is ample) are also
equivalent to each of the following:*

*b'') `h` is separated, one has `G(s) = X` and the canonical morphism `u : G(s) вҶ’ Proj(S)` has its fibres finite and
discrete.*

*b''') One has `G(s) = X` and the canonical morphism `u` is radicial.*

If `Z = Spec(A)`, the ring `S` is canonically equipped with a structure of graded `A`-algebra, so one has a structural
morphism `g : Proj(S) вҶ’ Z` which is separated `(II, 2.4.2)`, and one has `h = g вҲҳ u`.

Since every radicial morphism is separated `(1.8.7.1)`, b''') implies that `h` is separated, hence implies b''). Since
condition b) of `(II, 4.5.2)` evidently implies b''), it remains to see that b'') implies that `в„’` is ample. Since
`h = g вҲҳ u` is of finite type by hypothesis and `g` is separated, `u` is also of finite type `(I, 6.3.4)`, hence the
hypothesis b'') implies that `u` is quasi-finite and separated `(I, 5.5.1)`. To prove that `в„’` is ample, we shall apply
`(18.12.16)`. Set `Y = Proj(S)`. Since `X` is quasi-compact, there exist an integer `n > 0` and a finite number of
elements `f_j вҲҲ S_n` such that the inverse images `uвҒ»В№(D_+(f_j))` cover `X`; one can therefore consider `u` as a
quasi-finite and separated morphism of `X` into the open `Y' = вӢғ D_+(f_j)` of `Y`. Consider then the invertible
`рқ’Ә_{Y'}`-Module `в„’' = рқ’Ә_Y(n) | Y'` `(II, 2.5.8)`; it is very ample relative to `Z` `(II, 4.4.3)`, and `u*(в„’')` is none
other by definition than `в„’^{вҠ— n}`

`(II, 3.7.9, (i))`. By virtue of `(18.12.16)`, `в„’^{вҠ— n}` is therefore ample relative to `Z` (which is equivalent to
saying that it is ample `(II, 4.6.6)`), and consequently the same is true of `в„’` `(II, 4.5.6, (i))`.

We leave to the reader the task of stating similarly conditions equivalent to those of `(II, 4.6.3)` for `рқ’Ә_X`-Modules
relatively ample.

[^18.5-azumaya-nagata]: The notion of Henselian local ring is due to Azumaya, that of Henselization to Nagata, to whom
    one also owes the principal results of this theory.
